The Jibril Tasdiq Problem: Resolving the Apparent Conflict
Qutb al-Razi's problem and its solution regarding Jibril's tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the taswir and tasdiq aspects of a definition and explain how Jibril's 'Sadaqta' relates to the latter.

Core Idea
A definition has two inseparable aspects: conveying conception and asserting truth of correspondence.

Qutb al-Razi posed a subtle problem: if definitions aim at conception (taswir), why did Jibril say 'You have spoken the truth' (tasdiq) after the Prophet's definition of iman? Tasdiq belongs to judgments, not definitions. The commentator resolves this by showing that every sound definition implicitly asserts a true correspondence between definiendum and definiens, and Jibril's assent was to that correspondence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The problem: if definition's purpose is taswir, then Jibril's tasdiq seems misplaced because tasdiq is about judgments. Recognize the tension in the Arabic: 'التَّصدِيقَ إِنَّما يكون في القضيَّة'.
This is a genuine puzzle that challenges the definition's role.
2
Understand the solution: two aspects
The answer states that the Prophet's statement has two aspects: a taswir aspect (the definition itself) and a tasdiq aspect (the truth of the correspondence). Jibril's tasdiq was for the correspondence.
The definiendum and definiens are coextensive, so the statement is both a definition and a true proposition.
3
Apply to Jibril's case
Jibril's 'Sadaqta' was not an assertion that the definition correctly pictures iman (though it does), but rather that the proposition 'iman is belief in Allah...' is true (i.e., the definiendum and definiens coextend).
Thus the tasdiq aspect is distinct from the taswir aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ . وقوله : «الإفادة تصوره» يُخرج ما عداه. الدسوقي العطار. ونظر فيه أبو الفتح، أمَّا أَوَّلاً ; فَلِأَنَّهُ يجوز أن يكونَ الكلام تركيباً خَبريًّا باعتبارِ دلالتِهِ على الحُكْم ; وإِنْ لم يتحقق خبرٌ كَخبرِ الشَّاكُ والنَّائم والسَّاهي على ما تقرَّرَ في موضعِهِ ، وأَمَّا ثانياً ; فَلِأَنَّهُ يجوز أن يكونَ الحُكْمُ على الطَّبيعة على وجه يسري إلى الأفراد وإن لم تلاحظ الأفراد على ما هو التَّحقيق في أحكام المحصوراتِ، على أنا لا نسلّم كذبَ الحكم على الطَّبيعة بطريق الطبيعة أيضاً .ا.هـ. وبقي هَهُنا إشكال نفيس أوردَهُ القطبُ الرَّازِيُّ في رسالتِهِ المعمولة في العلوم المختلفة، وهو المختلفة، وهو أَنَّهُ إذا كانَ الغرضُ مِنَ الحمل في التَّعريفِ التَّصوير ; يشكل عليه قولُ جبريل عليهِ السَّلامُ : صَدَقْتَ ; حينَ أجَابَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم لَمَّا سألَ عَنْ حقيقة الإيمانِ ماذا هو ؟ فقالَ الرَّسُولُ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الإيمانُ أنْ تؤْمِنَ بِالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخِرِ وتؤمن بالقدرِ خَيْرِهِ وَشَرِّهِ» ; لأنَّ التَّصدِيقَ إِنَّما يكون في القضيَّة، وحاصل الجوابِ أَنَّ التَّعريفَ إِنَّما يستقيم إذا كان المعرَّفُ مُساوياً للمعرّفِ ; أي: يصدقُ كُلُّ منهما على ما صدق عليهِ الآخَرُ ، وبالعكس; فيكونُ لِقَولِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم جهتانِ ; جهة التّصوير : وَهِيَ التّعريفُ، وجهة أَنَّ مَا صدق عليه الإيمان يصدق عليه الاعتقاد بالله وملائكته التصديق : وهي ... إلخ، فتصديقُ جبريل راجع إلى جهةِ التَّصديق لا إلى جهة التصوير ا . هـ . (قَوْلُهُ : لِإِفَادَةِ تَصَوُّرِهِ) خرج بهذا القيدِ المحمولُ الَّذي لا يكون الغرضُ منه إفادةَ التَّصورِ، قال المحشّي : والمراد لإفادة المبدأ تصوره; لأنَّ المفيد هو المبدأ، والمعرَّفُ مُعدٌ كَمَا قيلَ أو في حكم المعدّ في عدم وجوبِ اجتماعِهِ مَعَ المعرِّفِ ; لأنَّهُ كَثيراً ما ينتفي مع بقاء المعرف، فنسبة الإفادة إليه مجازا . هـ. أرادَ أَنَّ المفيد المبدأ الفيَّاضُ، وهو العقل العاشرُ ; لأنَّهُ المراد عندَهُم وصرَّحُوا بِهِ، فَتفسيرُ البعض المبدأ بِالشَّخص ; خروجٌ عَنِ اصطلاحِهِم ، مَعَ أَنَّ إِسنادُهَا إِلَيْهِ كَإسنادِهَا هو.
Chapter: On the Definiens and its Divisions. His statement: 'the conveyance of its conception' excludes what is other than it. Al-Dasuqi, al-Attar. Abu al-Fath examined it: firstly, because it is permissible that the speech be a declarative composition by virtue of its indication of judgment even if no actual predicate is realized, like the report of the doubter, the sleeper, and the forgetful as established in its place; secondly, because it is permissible that the judgment be about the nature in a way that extends to individuals even if individuals are not considered, according to the verification in the rules of quantified propositions, and we do not admit the falsity of the judgment about the nature by way of nature itself. There remains here a precious problem raised by Qutb al-Razi in his treatise composed on the various sciences – and it is: if the purpose of predication in definition is picturing (taswir), it would be problematic in light of Jibril's statement 'You have spoken the truth' when the Prophet answered him when he asked about the reality of faith: 'What is it?' The Messenger said: 'Faith is to believe in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, and to believe in divine decree, its good and evil' – because tasdiq occurs only in a judgment. The gist of the answer is that the definition is valid only if the definiendum and definiens are coextensive, i.e., each applies to everything the other applies to, and vice versa; thus the Prophet's statement has two aspects: a picturing aspect, which is the definition, and a tasdiq aspect – that what faith applies to, belief in Allah etc. also applies – so Jibril's tasdiq goes back to the tasdiq aspect, not the taswir aspect. (His statement: 'to convey its conception') – this condition excludes the predicate whose purpose is not to convey conception. The commentator said: 'What is meant is the conveyance of its conception by the Active Intellect (al-mabda'), because the conveyor is the Active Intellect, and the definiendum is a preparer (mu'add) as it is said, or in the ruling of a preparer, in that its conjunction with the definiens is not necessary because it often ceases while the definiens remains, so the attribution of conveyance to it is metaphorical.' He meant that the conveyor is the Effusive Intellect (al-mabda' al-fayyad), which is the Tenth Intellect, because that is what they mean and they stated it explicitly; so the interpretation of 'al-mabda'' by some as 'the person' is a departure from their convention, although the attribution of conveyance to it is like the attribution of conveyance to him.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter on the definiens and its divisions. The commentator first notes that the phrase 'the conveyance of its conception' excludes other types of predication. Then Abu al-Fath critiques this: first, a declarative sentence may convey judgment even without an actual predicate, like statements from a doubter; second, judgment may be about the nature in a way that covers individuals, as in quantified propositions. Next, a problem from Qutb al-Razi is presented: if the purpose of predication in definition is taswir (picturing/conception), why did Jibril say 'You have spoken the truth' after the Prophet's definition of iman, since tasdiq belongs to judgments? The answer: the definition has two aspects: taswir (the definition itself) and tasdiq (the correspondence of definiendum and definiens). Jibril's tasdiq refers to the correspondence, not to the definitional function. The final part explains that 'conveyance of its conception' is ultimately attributed to the Active Intellect (the Tenth Intellect) as the efficient cause of understanding, the definiendum being only a preparatory factor; any interpretation of 'al-mabda'' as a human person is a deviation from standard terminology.

Key Terms
التصوير
التصديق
المعرّف
المعرف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Jibril say 'You have spoken the truth'?
A) Because the definition was grammatically correct.
B) Because the definition included a judgment that required assent.
C) Because Jibril was confirming the truth of the content, not the definitional aspect.
D) Because the Prophet's definition was a clear description.

Key Takeaway
A sound definition possesses both a taswir aspect (conveying conception) and a tasdiq aspect (asserting the truth of coextension); Jibril's tasdiq pertained to the latter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take a definition from a kalam text (e.g., 'al-'ilm is a necessary attribute of Allah'). Identify the taswir and tasdiq aspects. Explain how a listener would both conceive and assent.
?
Construct a hypothetical objection similar to Qutb al-Razi's for a definition of 'shirk'. Then resolve it using the two-aspect theory.

The True Agent of Conception: The Active Intellect as Conveyor
Commentator clarifies that the Active Intellect is the true conveyor of conception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the conveyance of conception is attributed to the Active Intellect (al-mabda') and distinguish this from the view that the definiendum itself is the agent.

Core Idea
The true conveyor of conception is the Active Intellect; the definiendum is only a preparer (mu'add).

In a marginal note, the commentator clarifies that the phrase 'conveyance of its conception' ultimately refers to the Active Intellect (or Tenth Intellect) as the efficient cause. The definiendum (e.g., the words of a definition) merely prepares the soul to receive conception from the Active Intellect. This reflects the falsafa doctrine of emanation and distinguishes the human instrument from the divine cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase being clarified
The base text says 'the conveyance of its conception' (إفادة تصوره). The commentator explains that this conveyance is attributed to al-mabda' (the Active Intellect), not to the verbal definition itself.
Al-mabda' here means the Tenth Intellect, the celestial intellect responsible for bestowing forms.
2
Understand the concept of 'mu'add' (preparer)
The definiendum (the expression) is said to be a 'mu'add' or in the ruling of a preparer. It does not actively convey conception but prepares the soul to receive it from the Active Intellect.
The conjunction of definiens and definiendum is not necessary; the definiendum may cease while the definiens remains (e.g., the definition survives the loss of the instance).
3
Recognize the metaphorical attribution
Attributing conveyance to the definiendum is metaphorical. The real agent is the Active Intellect. The commentator warns against interpreting 'al-mabda'' as a human person, which is a departure from the standard falsafa convention.
This distinction preserves the causal chain: the human words are instrumental, not efficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(قَوْلُهُ : لِإِفَادَةِ تَصَوُّرِهِ) خرج بهذا القيدِ المحمولُ الَّذي لا يكون الغرضُ منه إفادةَ التَّصورِ، قال المحشّي : والمراد لإفادة المبدأ تصوره; لأنَّ المفيد هو المبدأ، والمعرَّفُ مُعدٌ كَمَا قيلَ أو في حكم المعدّ في عدم وجوبِ اجتماعِهِ مَعَ المعرِّفِ ; لأنَّهُ كَثيراً ما ينتفي مع بقاء المعرف، فنسبة الإفادة إليه مجازا . هـ. أرادَ أَنَّ المفيد المبدأ الفيَّاضُ، وهو العقل العاشرُ ; لأنَّهُ المراد عندَهُم وصرَّحُوا بِهِ، فَتفسيرُ البعض المبدأ بِالشَّخص ; خروجٌ عَنِ اصطلاحِهِم ، مَعَ أَنَّ إِسنادُهَا إِلَيْهِ كَإسنادِهَا هو.

The Objection of Qutb al-Razi on the Definition of Iman and Its Resolution
Qutb al-Razi's objection about Prophet's definition of iman and its resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the two aspects of a definitional statement (conception and assent) resolve the apparent conflict between the purpose of definition and Jibril's response of assent.

Core Idea
A definition serves conception; Jibril's assent refers to the truth of the proposition, not the definition.

This passage presents a nuanced objection raised by Qutb al-Razi concerning the definition of faith (iman) given by the Prophet (peace be upon him) in response to Jibril's question. The objection challenges a core principle of definition in Islamic logic: that the purpose of definition is conception (tasawwur). Yet Jibril responded with an expression of assent (tasdiq). How can a definition, which aims at conception, elicit a response of assent? The answer reveals a key distinction between the content of a definition and the truth of the statement containing it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of definition
Recall that in Islamic logic, definitions (hudud) are meant to produce conception (tasawwur), i.e., a clear mental grasp of the meaning of a term, not to assert the truth of a proposition (tasdiq). This is the starting point of the objection.
2
State Qutb al-Razi's objection
Qutb al-Razi observes that when Jibril asked about the reality of iman, the Prophet gave a definition listing the pillars of faith. Jibril responded with 'Sadaqta' (You have spoken truthfully), which is an act of assent. But assent belongs to propositions, not definitions. So if the purpose of definition is conception, why did Jibril give assent?
The hadith is found in Sahih Muslim.
3
Analyze the answer: two aspects of the statement
The answer distinguishes two aspects in the Prophet's statement: (1) the aspect of conception (taswir), which is the definition itself, and (2) the aspect of assent (tasdiq), which concerns the truth of the proposition. The definition is coextensive (musawi) with the definiendum, meaning it applies to exactly the same things. The truth of the statement is a separate matter.
Coextensiveness is a condition for a valid definition.
4
Apply the distinction to resolve the objection
Jibril's 'Sadaqta' refers to the truth of the proposition that the definition correctly describes faith, not to the definitional act itself. Thus, the definition still fulfills its purpose of conception, and the objection is resolved.
This shows that a definitional statement can be both a definition (for conception) and a proposition (subject to assent).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقي هَهُنا إشكال نفيس أوردَهُ القطبُ الرَّازِيُّ في رسالتِهِ المعمولة في العلوم المختلفة، وهو أَنَّهُ إذا كانَ الغرضُ مِنَ الحمل في التَّعريفِ التَّصوير؛ يشكل عليه قولُ جبريل عليهِ السَّلامُ: صَدَقْتَ؛ حينَ أجَابَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم لَمَّا سألَ عَنْ حقيقة الإيمانِ ماذا هو؟ فقالَ الرَّسُولُ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الإيمانُ أنْ تؤْمِنَ بِالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخِرِ وتؤمن بالقدرِ خَيْرِهِ وَشَرِّهِ»؛ لأنَّ التَّصدِيقَ إِنَّما يكون في القضيَّة، وحاصل الجوابِ أَنَّ التَّعريفَ إِنَّما يستقيم إذا كان المعرَّفُ مُساوياً للمعرّفِ؛ أي: يصدقُ كُلُّ منهما على ما صدق عليهِ الآخَرُ، وبالعكس؛ فيكونُ لِقَولِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم جهتانِ؛ جهة التّصوير: وَهِيَ التّعريفُ، وجهة التَّصديق: وهي ... إلخ، فتصديقُ جبريل راجع إلى جهةِ التَّصديق لا إلى جهة التصوير ا.هـ.
And there remains here a precious objection raised by Qutb al-Razi in his treatise on the various sciences: that if the purpose of predication in definition is conception, then the statement of Jibril, peace be upon him, 'You have spoken truthfully' when the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, answered him when he asked about the reality of faith: 'What is it?' and the Messenger said: 'Faith is that you believe in God, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, and believe in destiny, its good and evil' — becomes problematic, because assent only occurs in a proposition. The gist of the answer is that a definition is valid only if the definer is coextensive with the definiendum, i.e., each applies to whatever the other applies to, and vice versa. Thus the Prophet's statement has two aspects: an aspect of conception, which is the definition, and an aspect of assent... etc. So Jibril's 'You have spoken truthfully' refers to the aspect of assent, not to the aspect of conception. End.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage presents an objection raised by Qutb al-Razi concerning the definition of definition. The objection uses the famous hadith of Jibril asking the Prophet about the reality of faith. If the purpose of a definition is to convey conception (tasawwur), then why did Jibril respond with 'Sadaqta' (You have spoken truth), which is an act of assent (tasdiq)? Assent pertains to propositions, not to definitions. The answer given is that a valid definition must be coextensive (musawi) with the definiendum. The Prophet's statement has two aspects: the aspect of conception (taswir) which is the definition itself, and the aspect of assent (tasdiq) which concerns the truth of the statement. Jibril's 'Sadaqta' refers to the truth of the proposition, not to the definitional aspect. Thus the objection is resolved: the definition still serves conception, and the response of Jibril relates to a different dimension.

Key Terms
التَّصْوِير
التَّصْدِيق
المُسَاوَاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Jibril say 'Sadaqta' after the Prophet defined faith?
A) Because the definition was correct for conception.
B) Because the statement as a proposition was true, not because the definition alone.
C) Because Jibril was testing the Prophet's knowledge.
D) Because the definition included assent inherently.

Key Takeaway
A definitional statement has two aspects: conception (the definition itself) and assent (the truth of the proposition); the purpose of definition remains conception, while assent pertains to the truth of the statement.

The True Giver of Conception: Active Intellect vs. Definition
Commentary refining the role of the principle vs. definition in imparting conception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the role of the Active Intellect (al-mabda' al-fayyad) from the role of definition in conveying conception, and explain why the attribution of imparting to definition is metaphorical.

Core Idea
Definitions don't give conception; they only prepare. The Active Intellect gives it.

In this passage, the commentator refines a claim made earlier that the definition (al-mu'arraf) imparts conception. He argues that the true efficient cause of conception is not the definition, but the 'principle' (al-mabda'), which in this context refers to the Active Intellect. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly locating the source of knowledge in Islamic philosophy and avoiding a confusion of preparatory causes with actual causes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two causal roles mentioned
In the passage, the commentator distinguishes between the 'mabda' (the effusive principle) and the 'mu'arraf' (the definiendum). The former is the true giver, the latter is merely preparatory. Locate these two roles in the Arabic.
The definiendum here is the thing being defined, not the definition itself.
2
Understand the distinction between true cause and preparatory cause
The commentator says the definiendum is 'mu'add' or in the status of a preparation. A preparatory cause (mu'add) disposes the recipient but does not produce the effect. The true efficient cause (the mabda' al-fayyad) is what actually imparts the form. How does this distinction affect our understanding of how we get new concepts?
3
Recognize why attribution of imparting to definition is metaphorical
The passage states that the definition often remains while the conception disappears, showing that the definition is not the cause that sustains conception. So saying 'the definition imparts conception' is a metaphor. What does that imply for the reliability of definitions?
4
Evaluate the misinterpretation of 'mabda' as the person
Some interpreted 'mabda' as the person being defined (e.g., 'Zayd is the principe'). The commentator rejects this as a departure from technical terminology. Why is this misinterpretation problematic? What does it reveal about the commentator's commitment?
This underscores that the term 'mabda' has a fixed technical meaning in falsafah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال المحشّي: والمراد لإفادة المبدأ تصوره؛ لأنَّ المفيد هو المبدأ، والمعرَّفُ مُعدٌ كَمَا قيلَ أو في حكم المعدّ في عدم وجوبِ اجتماعِهِ مَعَ المعرِّفِ؛ لأنَّهُ كَثيراً ما ينتفي مع بقاء المعرف، فنسبة الإفادة إليه مجازا. أرادَ أَنَّ المفيد المبدأ الفيَّاضُ، وهو العقل العاشرُ؛ لأنَّهُ المراد عندَهُم وصرَّحُوا بِهِ، فَتفسيرُ البعض المبدأ بِالشَّخص؛ خروجٌ عَنِ اصطلاحِهِم، مَعَ أَنَّ إِسنادُهَا إِلَيْهِ كَإسنادِهَا للمقول؛ لأنَّ كُلًّا واسطةٌ في الإفادة، والمفيد حقيقة عندهم هو المبدأ الفياض، يدلُّ لِذلكَ ما سننقلُهُ عن الخلخالي.
The commentator said: What is intended is that the principle conveys its conception; because the giver is the principle, and the definiendum is a preparation, as has been said, or in the status of a preparation, in that its coexistence with the definer is not necessary; because it often ceases while the definer remains, so the attribution of imparting to it is metaphorical. He meant that the giver is the effusive principle, which is the Tenth Intellect; because that is what is intended with them and they have stated it. Thus interpreting 'principle' as the person is a departure from their terminology, even though attribution of imparting to it is like attribution to the utterance; because each is a medium in imparting, and the true giver with them is the effusive principle. That is indicated by what we will quote from al-Khalkhali.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage refines the earlier statement that definition imparts conception. The commentator argues that the true giver of conception is the 'mabda' (principle), i.e., the Active Intellect (al-'Aql al-'Ashir). The definiendum (the person or thing being defined) is merely a preparatory cause (mu'add). The attribution of imparting to the definition itself is metaphorical, because the definition often remains while the conception disappears. Some have misinterpreted 'mabda' as the person being defined, but that is a departure from technical terminology. The Active Intellect is the real source of knowledge, and definitions and utterances are only intermediaries. Al-Khalkhali will confirm this view.

Key Terms
المبدأ الفيَّاض
مُعِدّ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The definition itself (al-mu'arraf).
B) The person who defines.
C) The Active Intellect (al-mabda' al-fayyad).
D) The categories of being.

Key Takeaway
The definition does not give conception; it only prepares the mind, while the Active Intellect is the true source of conception.

Why Definitions Must Provide a Distinguishing Conception
Commentator clarifies the intended meaning of tasawwur in definition, rejecting broader/narrower terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether a given definition meets the condition of providing a distinguishing conception based on the criteria of later Islamic logicians.

Core Idea
A definition must give a conception that distinguishes the thing from everything else—not just any mental picture.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies what kind of conception (tasawwur) is intended when we say a definition gives a conception of the defined term. Not every true statement about the thing qualifies; the definition must either capture its essence (bi al-kunh) or at least provide a distinguishing feature that sets it apart from all other things. This distinction is crucial for ensuring that definitions in Islamic sciences are precise and useful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The passage discusses the concept of 'definition' (al-mu'arraf). Note that the commentator is clarifying what kind of conception a definition must provide, not just any conception.
2
Distinguish between 'any conception' and 'distinguishing conception'
The author rejects the idea that any true description (like broader or narrower terms) suffices. The definition must provide a conception that marks the thing off from everything else.
For example, 'human is an animal' is true but not distinguishing because 'animal' includes non-humans.
3
Understand the two forms of distinguishing conception
A definition can give either a complete essential conception (hadd tamm) which captures the essence, or an incomplete but distinguishing conception (hadd ghayr tamm, rasm, etc.) which still distinguishes from all others.
An incomplete definition like 'human is a rational animal' uses the differentia 'rational' to distinguish.
4
Recognize the debate between early and later scholars
Later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) insist the definition must be exactly equal (musawi) to the defined term, neither broader nor narrower. Early scholars (mutaqaddimun) allowed broader or narrower definitions as long as they help in distinguishing.
This debate affects how definitions are constructed in fiqh and kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأنَّه لا يراد بالتَّصورِ تصوره بوجه ما ، وإلا لجاز أن يكون الأعم والأخص معرّفاً. بل المراد تصوُّرُه بِالكُنْهِ كما في الحدّ التام، أو بوجةٍ يميزه عن جميعِ ما عداه، كما في الحدّ الغيرِ التَّامّ ، والرَّسْمِ ، والجنس، والعَرَضِ العام. وإن أفاذا تصرُّرَ الشَّيء بوجه ما ، لكن لم يُفيدا تصوره بالكُنْهِ أو بوجه يميّزه عن جميع ما عَدَاهُ. بناءً على مذهب المتأخّرين المشترطين المساواة، والمتقدّمونَ يُجوِّزُونَ التَّعريف بالأعم والأخص.
Because what is intended by conception is not its conception in any way whatsoever; otherwise it would be permissible for the broader and the narrower to be a definition. Rather what is intended is its conception by the essence as in the complete definition, or by a way that distinguishes it from everything else, as in the incomplete definition, the graphic description, the genus, and the general accident. Even if they give a conception of the thing in some way, they do not give its conception by the essence or by a way distinguishing it from everything else. Based on the doctrine of the later scholars who stipulate equality, while the early scholars permit definition by the broader and narrower.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage clarifies the condition for a valid definition in logic. The core issue is what kind of 'conception' (tasawwur) a definition must produce. The author argues that the intended conception is not merely any conception of the thing—otherwise broad terms like 'animal' for 'human' (which is true but not coextensive) or narrow terms like 'actually writing' would qualify as definitions. Instead, the definition must give a conception that captures the essence of the thing (bi al-kunh) in a complete definition, or at least a conception that distinguishes it from everything else (even if not essential) in other types of definitions like incomplete definition, graphic description, genus, or general accident. The passage notes a difference between early and later logicians: later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) require the definition to be exactly equal (musawi) to the defined term, meaning it must be neither broader nor narrower, while earlier scholars (mutaqaddimun) allowed definitions that are broader or narrower as long as they assist in distinguishing the thing. This is important in Islamic logic, for example, when defining 'hukm' in usul al-fiqh: a later scholar would insist the definition applies to every instance equally, whereas an earlier scholar might accept a definition like 'Allah's address concerning the actions of the legally responsible' even if it doesn't cover all aspects equally.

Key Terms
التصور
الأعم والأخص
المساواة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because 'animal' is broader than 'human' and does not distinguish humans from other animals.
C) Because the definition is incomplete; it lacks the species.
D) Because it does not give any conception at all.

Key Takeaway
For later Islamic logicians, a valid definition must be coextensive with the defined term—it must give a conception that distinguishes the thing from everything else.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refining the Intended Meaning of Tasawwur in Definition
Author addresses objection that definition of tasawwur permits broader/narrower terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the objection to the definition of tasawwur and explain how later logicians refined its intended meaning to require essential or distinguishing conception.

Core Idea
Tasawwur in definition is not any conception but only by essence or distinctive trait.

In this passage, al-Sharnubi addresses a key objection: if tasawwur (conception) is defined broadly, then definitions using broader or narrower terms would be valid, yet they are not. The response is that tasawwur is intended in a specific sense—either by the essence (al-kunh) or by a distinguishing characteristic. This refinement is crucial for understanding the logical requirements of a proper definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection states that if tasawwur means any conception, then definitions using broader or narrower terms would give a conception of the definiendum. Find this in the passage: 'If tasawwur is defined as any conception...'
The objection is implied by the statement that such definitions are not permissible.
2
Locate the refinement
The author refines tasawwur to mean either conception by essence (bi al-kunh) or by a distinctive trait. This excludes broader/narrower definitions that do not capture essence or distinction.
The phrase 'بل المراد' indicates the intended meaning.
3
Understand the condition of equality
Later logicians (muta'akhkhirūn) stipulated that the definiens must be co-extensive (musāwī) with the definiendum. This condition ensures that the definition is neither broader nor narrower.
The passage mentions 'المتأخرين المشترطين المساواة'.
4
Recognize the absence of internal evidence
The commentator notes that the definition itself lacks qarīna (evidence) for the refined meaning; the condition is external. Al-Sharnubi criticizes forced attempts to find internal evidence.
This highlights that the condition is an external requirement, not part of the definition's essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكنَّه لم يجز - كما سيجيء .. بل المراد تصوُّرُه بِالكُنْهِ كما في الحدّ التام، أو بوجةٍ يميزه عن جميعِ ما عداه، كما في الحدّ الغيرِ التَّامّ ، والرَّسْمِ ، والجنس، والعَرَضِ العام. وإن أفاذا تصرَّرَ الشَّيء بوجه ما ، لكن لم يُفيدا تصوره بالكُنْهِ أو بوجه يميّزه عن جميع ما عداه . وقولُهُ: (لكنَّهُ لمْ يجز) : أي : وحينئذ ؛ فلم يكن المراد بالتصورِ ما ذكر، وهو التصور بوجه ما . (قَوْلُهُ: بَل الْمُرَادُ . . . إِلَخ فيه : أنَّ المراد لا يدفعُ الإيراد إلَّا إذا قامَتْ قرينةٌ على ذلك المراد، وَلَا قرينةَ هُنا إلَّا أنْ يُقالَ : القرينه حاليَّة، وهو أنَّ النَّصور متى أُطلق؛ لا ينصرفُ إِلَّا لِلتَّمييز عن جميع الغير، وذلك صادق على المميز بالكُنْه، أو ما عداه . بوجةٍ يميّزه عن جميعِ وقولُ الشَّارح : (كَمَا سَيجيء)؛ يدلُّ على أنَّ القرينة ما سيأتي، وفيه : أَنَّ مَا سيأتي في الشُّروط، وهو خارج عن التّعريف، والقرينة لا بد أن تكونَ في التّعريف . (قَوْلُهُ: بِالْكُنْهِ) أي: الحقيقة. (قَوْلُهُ : كَمَا فِى الْحَدِّ التَّامّ الكاف استقصائية، وكذا يُقالُ فيما بعده. (قَوْلُهُ: كَمَا فِي الْحَدِّ الْغَيْرِ النَّام وهو الحد النَّاقصُ والرَّسم بقسميه . العطار . (قَوْلُهُ : لَكِنَّهُ لَمْ يَجُزْ) بناءً على مذهب المتأخّرين المشترطين المساواة، والمتقدّمونَ يُجوِّزُونَ التَّعريف بالأعم والأخص . هو (قَوْلُهُ : إلا أن يقال ... إلخ) هذه تكلفات من المحشّي والشَّارح ينبو عنها مقام التعريف، إذ لماهية المعرف مطلقاً ولو أعمّ أو أخص يدلّ لذلك اشتراط المصنف المساواة، ومعلوم أن الشرط خارج عن الماهية والغرض منه تصحيحها بإخراج ما دخل فيها، ولو كان التعريف لماهية المعرف الصحيحة لما كان هذا الشرط معنى لعدم الاحتياج إليه وممن صرح بأن التعريف المذكور صادق بالأعم والأخص ؛ الخلخالي وأيضاً المتقدمون يرون صحة التعريف بهما . ا . هـ. الشَّرنوبي.
But it is not permissible — as will come later. Rather, the intended [meaning] is conceiving it with its essence (bi al-kunh) as in the complete definition, or in a way that distinguishes it from everything other than it, as in the incomplete definition, and the description, and the genus, and the general accident. Although they give a conception of the thing in some respect, they do not give its conception by essence or by a way that distinguishes it from everything other than it. His statement: 'but it is not permissible' means: And when that is the case, then the intended meaning of conception was not what was mentioned, i.e., conception in some respect. His statement: 'Rather, the intended... etc.' contains [the point] that the intended meaning does not repel the objection except if there is evidence (qarina) for that intended meaning, and there is no evidence here except to say: The evidence is circumstantial, which is that whenever 'conception' is absolutely used, it only refers to distinguishing from all other [things], and that applies to what distinguishes by essence or otherwise. By a way that distinguishes it from all others. And the commentator's statement: 'as will come later' indicates that the evidence is what is coming later. In it [there is the point]: that what is coming later is in the conditions, and it is outside the definition, and the evidence must be in the definition. His statement: 'by essence (bi al-kunh)' means: the reality. His statement: 'as in the complete definition' – the kaf is for comprehensive inclusion, and likewise it is said in what follows. His statement: 'as in the incomplete definition' – which is the incomplete hadd and the two types of rasm. Al-'Attar: His statement: 'but it is not permissible' is based on the doctrine of the later scholars who stipulate equality [between definiens and definiendum], while the earlier scholars permit definition by the more general and more specific. He (al-Sharnubi): His statement: 'except to say... etc.' – these are forced interpretations by the glossator and commentator that the context of definition rejects, for the quiddity of the definiens absolutely, even if more general or more specific, indicates that; therefore the author's stipulation of equality [is needed], and it is known that the condition is outside the quiddity and its purpose is to correct it by excluding what entered it, and if the definition were for the quiddity of the correct definiens, this condition would have no meaning due to lack of need for it. And among those who explicitly stated that the mentioned definition is true of the more general and more specific is al-Khalkhali; also the earlier scholars consider definition by them valid. End. Al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) discussing an objection regarding the definition of tasawwur (conception) in the context of definition. The objection is that if tasawwur is defined as any conception of a thing, then a definition that uses a broader or narrower term would still give a conception, which many logicians reject. The answer is that the intended meaning of tasawwur is not any conception but either conception by the essence (al-kunh) as in a complete definition, or conception by a characteristic that distinguishes the thing from everything else, as in other types of definition. The commentator al-Sharnubi critiques the forced attempts to find evidence for this intended meaning within the definition itself, arguing that the condition of equality (musāwāt) is an external condition added by later scholars, while earlier scholars accepted definition by broader or narrower terms. The passage highlights the debate between the mutaqaddimūn (earlier) and muta'akhkhirūn (later) logicians on whether the definiens must be exactly co-extensive.

التصور
الحد التام
المساواة
القرينة

Checkpoint

B) It must be co-extensive (musāwi) with the definiendum.

D) It must be a synonym.

Key Takeaway
A proper definition requires that the definiens be co-extensive with the definiendum, and that the conception given be either by essence or by a distinguishing characteristic.

The Debate on the Condition of Equality in Definitions: Early vs. Later Logicians
Author addresses objection that definition of tasawwur permits broader/narrower terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of mutaqaddimūn and muta'akhkhirūn regarding the condition of musāwāt and explain al-Sharnubi's critique of forced interpretations.

Core Idea
Early logicians allowed broader/narrower definitions; later scholars required exact co-extensiveness.

This passage also reveals a historical shift in logic: the mutaqaddimūn (earlier scholars) accepted definitions that were broader or narrower than the definiendum, while the muta'akhkhirūn (later scholars) insisted on equality (musāwāt). Al-Sharnubi critiques the attempts by the glossator and commentator to find internal evidence for this condition, arguing that the condition is external. This lesson unpacks that commentary chain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base claim
The base text (matn) likely defined tasawwur as any conception, leading to the objection that broader/narrower definitions would be acceptable.
This is implied by the need for refinement.
2
Find the commentator's response
The commentator restricts tasawwur to essential or distinguishing conception to avoid the objection. This is the first level of interpretation.
The phrase 'بل المراد' signals the commentator's move.
3
Note the glossator's attempt to provide qarīna
The glossator (e.g., al-'Attar) tries to find internal evidence, either circumstantial (qarīna hāliyya) or by referring to later conditions, to justify the restriction.
Al-Sharnubi mentions these attempts as 'تكلفات' (forced interpretations).
4
Understand al-Sharnubi's critique
Al-Sharnubi argues that the condition of equality is external to the definition, not part of the definiens. Early logicians did not require it, so the forced interpretations are unnecessary.
He also names al-Khalkhali as supporting the early view.

Source Text

لكنَّه لم يجز - كما سيجيء .. بل المراد تصوُّرُه بِالكُنْهِ كما في الحدّ التام، أو بوجةٍ يميزه عن جميعِ ما عداه، كما في الحدّ الغيرِ التَّامّ ، والرَّسْمِ ، والجنس، والعَرَضِ العام. وإن أفاذا تصرَّرَ الشَّيء بوجه ما ، لكن لم يُفيدا تصوره بالكُنْهِ أو بوجه يميّزه عن جميع ما عداه . وقولُهُ: (لكنَّهُ لمْ يجز) : أي : وحينئذ ؛ فلم يكن المراد بالتصورِ ما ذكر، وهو التصور بوجه ما . (قَوْلُهُ: بَل الْمُرَادُ . . . إِلَخ فيه : أنَّ المراد لا يدفعُ الإيراد إلَّا إذا قامَتْ قرينةٌ على ذلك المراد، وَلَا قرينةَ هُنا إلَّا أنْ يُقالَ : القرينه حاليَّة، وهو أنَّ النَّصور متى أُطلق؛ لا ينصرفُ إِلَّا لِلتَّمييز عن جميع الغير، وذلك صادق على المميز بالكُنْه، أو ما عداه . بوجةٍ يميّزه عن جميعِ وقولُ الشَّارح : (كَمَا سَيجيء)؛ يدلُّ على أنَّ القرينة ما سيأتي، وفيه : أَنَّ مَا سيأتي في الشُّروط، وهو خارج عن التّعريف، والقرينة لا بد أن تكونَ في التّعريف . (قَوْلُهُ: بِالْكُنْهِ) أي: الحقيقة. (قَوْلُهُ : كَمَا فِى الْحَدِّ التَّامّ الكاف استقصائية، وكذا يُقالُ فيما بعده. (قَوْلُهُ: كَمَا فِي الْحَدِّ الْغَيْرِ النَّام وهو الحد النَّاقصُ والرَّسم بقسميه . العطار . (قَوْلُهُ : لَكِنَّهُ لَمْ يَجُزْ) بناءً على مذهب المتأخّرين المشترطين المساواة، والمتقدّمونَ يُجوِّزُونَ التَّعريف بالأعم والأخص . هو (قَوْلُهُ : إلا أن يقال ... إلخ) هذه تكلفات من المحشّي والشَّارح ينبو عنها مقام التعريف، إذ لماهية المعرف مطلقاً ولو أعمّ أو أخص يدلّ لذلك اشتراط المصنف المساواة، ومعلوم أن الشرط خارج عن الماهية والغرض منه تصحيحها بإخراج ما دخل فيها، ولو كان التعريف لماهية المعرف الصحيحة لما كان هذا الشرط معنى لعدم الاحتياج إليه وممن صرح بأن التعريف المذكور صادق بالأعم والأخص ؛ الخلخالي وأيضاً المتقدمون يرون صحة التعريف بهما . ا . هـ. الشَّرنوبي.
But it is not permissible — as will come later. Rather, the intended [meaning] is conceiving it with its essence (bi al-kunh) as in the complete definition, or in a way that distinguishes it from everything other than it, as in the incomplete definition, and the description, and the genus, and the general accident. Although they give a conception of the thing in some respect, they do not give its conception by essence or by a way that distinguishes it from everything other than it. His statement: 'but it is not permissible' means: And when that is the case, then the intended meaning of conception was not what was mentioned, i.e., conception in some respect. His statement: 'Rather, the intended... etc.' contains [the point] that the intended meaning does not repel the objection except if there is evidence (qarina) for that intended meaning, and there is no evidence here except to say: The evidence is circumstantial, which is that whenever 'conception' is absolutely used, it only refers to distinguishing from all other [things], and that applies to what distinguishes by essence or otherwise. By a way that distinguishes it from all others. And the commentator's statement: 'as will come later' indicates that the evidence is what is coming later. In it [there is the point]: that what is coming later is in the conditions, and it is outside the definition, and the evidence must be in the definition. His statement: 'by essence (bi al-kunh)' means: the reality. His statement: 'as in the complete definition' – the kaf is for comprehensive inclusion, and likewise it is said in what follows. His statement: 'as in the incomplete definition' – which is the incomplete hadd and the two types of rasm. Al-'Attar: His statement: 'but it is not permissible' is based on the doctrine of the later scholars who stipulate equality [between definiens and definiendum], while the earlier scholars permit definition by the more general and more specific. He (al-Sharnubi): His statement: 'except to say... etc.' – these are forced interpretations by the glossator and commentator that the context of definition rejects, for the quiddity of the definiens absolutely, even if more general or more specific, indicates that; therefore the author's stipulation of equality [is needed], and it is known that the condition is outside the quiddity and its purpose is to correct it by excluding what entered it, and if the definition were for the quiddity of the correct definiens, this condition would have no meaning due to lack of need for it. And among those who explicitly stated that the mentioned definition is true of the more general and more specific is al-Khalkhali; also the earlier scholars consider definition by them valid. End. Al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) discussing an objection regarding the definition of tasawwur (conception) in the context of definition. The objection is that if tasawwur is defined as any conception of a thing, then a definition that uses a broader or narrower term would still give a conception, which many logicians reject. The answer is that the intended meaning of tasawwur is not any conception but either conception by the essence (al-kunh) as in a complete definition, or conception by a characteristic that distinguishes the thing from everything else, as in other types of definition. The commentator al-Sharnubi critiques the forced attempts to find evidence for this intended meaning within the definition itself, arguing that the condition of equality (musāwāt) is an external condition added by later scholars, while earlier scholars accepted definition by broader or narrower terms. The passage highlights the debate between the mutaqaddimūn (earlier) and muta'akhkhirūn (later) logicians on whether the definiens must be exactly co-extensive.

الحد التام
المساواة
القرينة

A) He accepts it fully as a valid interpretation.
B) He argues that the qarīna is external and not part of the definition itself.
C) He says the qarīna is purely linguistic.
D) He rejects the condition of equality entirely.

Key Takeaway
The condition of equality (musāwāt) for definiens is a later development; early logicians accepted broader/narrower definitions.

The Condition of Co-Extensiveness in Definition
Author states the condition of co-extensiveness in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given definiens is co-extensive with its definiendum by checking for comprehensiveness and exclusiveness.

Core Idea
A valid definition must exactly match the definiendum — not too broad, not too narrow.

In this passage, the author lays down a fundamental requirement for any sound definition: the definiens must be co-extensive with the definiendum. This means the definition must cover every instance of the thing being defined and nothing else. The commentator al-Dasuqi explains that this condition is about truth (sidq) and is equivalent to saying the definition must be both comprehensive (jāmi') and exclusive (māni'). Let us break down how to check this condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definiens
Find the term being defined (definiendum) and the words used to define it (definiens) in a given definition.
For example, if the definition is 'Fasting is abstaining from food and drink from dawn to sunset', the definiendum is 'fasting' and the definiens is 'abstaining from food and drink from dawn to sunset'.
2
Check comprehensiveness (jāmi')
Ask: Does the definiens apply to every instance of the definiendum? If any instance of the definiendum is not covered by the definiens, the definition is not comprehensive.
If the definition of fasting omitted 'from dawn to sunset', it would be too broad and include general abstention.
3
Check exclusiveness (māni')
Ask: Does the definiens apply to anything outside the definiendum? If the definiens covers things that are not instances of the definiendum, the definition is not exclusive.
If the definition of fasting included 'avoiding sin', it would be too broad because many non-fasting acts avoid sin.
4
Determine co-extensiveness
If both comprehensiveness and exclusiveness are satisfied, the definiens is co-extensive with the definiendum. If either fails, the definition is defective.
The passage stresses that a definition that is more specific (akhaṣṣ) fails comprehensiveness; one that is more general (a'amm) fails exclusiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في المُعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ [شروط المعرِّفِ] (فَيُشْتَرَطُ أَنْ يَكُونَ) المعرَّفُ (مُسَاوِياً) للمعرَّفِ ، الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : فَيُشْتَرَطُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُعَرِّفُ مُسَاوِيَاً لِلْمُعَرَّفِ ) أي : في الصدق، وإِنَّما لم يقيَّد المصنِّفُ بذلك ؛ لأنَّه هو الذي تنصرفُ له المساواة عند الإطلاق؛ بخلافِ المساواة في المعرفة . لا ولذا قيَّده فيما يأتي بقوله : معرفة، وهذا الشَّرطُ هو المشار له بقول بعضهم : بُدَّ أن يكونَ المعرِّفُ جامعاً ومُطّرداً (۱) ، ولا بدَّ أن يكون مانعاً ومنعكساً، فلو كانَ التّعريفُ أخصَّ؛ لَكان غير جامع ، ولو كان أعم؛ لكان غير مانع.
Chapter: On the Definiens and Its Divisions. [Conditions of the Definiens] (It is required that) the definiens be (co-extensive) with the definiendum. Al-Dasuqi: His statement: 'It is required that the definiens be co-extensive with the definiendum' means in truth (fi al-sidq); the author did not qualify it with that because that is what 'co-extensive' refers to when absolutely used, contrary to co-extensiveness in knowledge. No; therefore he qualified it later by saying 'knowledge'. And this condition is what some refer to by the saying: The definiens must be comprehensive (jāmi') and consistent (muttariḍ), and it must be exclusive (māni') and converse (mun'akis). So if the definition were more specific, it would not be comprehensive; and if it were more general, it would not be exclusive.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a definitional statement of a key condition for a valid definition: the definiens must be co-extensive (musāwi) with the definiendum, meaning they apply to exactly the same things. The commentator al-Dasuqi explains that the condition is about truth (sidq) rather than knowledge. The author did not explicitly qualify it with 'in truth' because the absolute term 'musāwi' refers to equality in truth; later he qualifies with 'knowledge' for a different context. This condition is equivalent to saying the definiens must be comprehensive (jāmi') – it covers every instance of the definiendum – and exclusive (māni') – it does not cover anything outside the definiendum. If the definition is too narrow (akhaṣṣ), it fails to include some cases; if too broad (aʿamm), it includes extraneous things. This is a foundational requirement in definition theory, ensuring the definition accurately picks out the intended concept.

Key Terms
مساوياً (musāwiyan): co-extensive in truth
جامع (jāmi'): comprehensive, covering all instances
مانع (māni'): exclusive, excluding non-instances

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a definition is more specific (akhaṣṣ) than the definiendum, what is it missing?
A) It is not exclusive (māni').
B) It is not comprehensive (jāmi').
C) It is not co-extensive.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
For a definition to be valid, the definiens must be co-extensive with the definiendum — no more, no less.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'salat' (prayer) as 'actions and words beginning with takbir and ending with taslim'. Is this definition jāmi' (comprehensive) and māni' (exclusive)? Explain your reasoning.
?
A student defines 'fasting' as 'abstaining from food and drink from dawn to sunset'. Is this definition co-extensive with the shar'i definition of fasting? Identify any missing or extra conditions.

Two Conditions for a Valid Definition: Equivalence and Clarity
Two necessary conditions for a valid definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to test any definition from an Islamic science for the two conditions of equivalence and clarity.

Core Idea
A definition must cover exactly what it defines and be clearer than it.

Definitions are the building blocks of precise knowledge. But not every definition is useful. This passage from Tadhheeb al-Mantiq wa al-Kalam lays down two indispensable conditions: the definiens must be coextensive with the definiendum, and it must be more evident than the thing defined. Without these, a definition fails to convey a concept. In this lesson, you will learn how to apply these criteria to definitions drawn from fiqh, kalam, and usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definiens
In a given definition, locate the term being defined (al-mu'arraf) and the term used to define it (al-mu'arraf).
2
Check extensional equivalence (musawat)
Ask: do the definiens and definiendum apply to exactly the same set of individuals? If the definiens is narrower, it misses some instances (ghayr jami'). If broader, it includes non-instances (ghayr mani').
In fiqh, a narrower definition of 'zakat' might exclude some types of wealth, while a broader one might include voluntary charity.
3
Check clarity (ijla'iyya)
Determine whether the definiens is better known or more evident than the definiendum. The definiens should lead the mind to the definiendum, not the reverse.
If the definiens uses obscure terms, it fails this condition.
4
Decide validity
If both conditions are satisfied, the definition is valid. If either fails, the definition is defective and must be revised.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَيُشْتَرَطُ أَنْ يَكُونَ المُعَرِّفُ مُسَاوِيَاً لِلْمُعَرَّفِ في الصدق، بحيث يصدق كل واحد منهما على جميع أفراد الآخر. وكذا يُشترط أن يكون أَجْلَى وأوضح من المعرَّف، أي بأن يكون معرفته سابقة على معرفة المعرَّف.
It is required that the definiens be equivalent to the definiendum in truth, such that each one applies to all individuals of the other. Likewise, it is required that it be clearer and more evident than the definiendum, meaning that its knowledge precedes knowledge of the definiendum.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for a valid definition (ta'rīf). It begins by stating the first condition: the definiens (al-mu'arraf) must be equivalent (musāwi) to the definiendum (al-mu'arraf) in truth (fī al-ṣidq). This means both terms apply to exactly the same set of individuals; neither is broader nor narrower. If the definiens were narrower (akhaṣṣ), it would fail to include all instances of the definiendum (ghayr jāmi'). If it were broader (a'amm), it would admit non-instances (ghayr māni'). The second condition is that the definiens must be clearer (ajlā) and more evident (awḍaḥ) than the definiendum. This means that knowledge of the definiens should precede knowledge of the definiendum, as the definiens serves as the means to understand the definiendum. Both conditions are essential for a definition to be useful in acquiring a concept.

Key Terms
المُعَرِّف
المُعَرَّف
المساواة
الإجلائية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone defines 'zakat' as 'obligatory charity on specific wealth', which condition of a valid definition is primarily being addressed?
A) Equivalence, because the definiens applies to the same individuals as 'zakat'.
B) Clarity, because 'obligatory charity on specific wealth' is clearer than 'zakat'.
C) Both equivalence and clarity.
D) Neither condition.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must be coextensive with the defined term and clearer than it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Examine the definition of 'sawm' (fasting) as 'abstaining from eating, drinking, and sexual relations from dawn to sunset with intention'. Test it for equivalence: does it cover all valid fasts and exclude non-fasting acts? Also test for clarity: is the definiens clearer than the word 'sawm'?
?
Propose a definition of 'riba' (usury) from the fiqh manuals you have studied. Apply the two conditions and identify whether the definition meets them. If not, suggest a correction.

Conditions of Definition: Equality and Clarity
Dasuqi and 'Attar explain the conditions of equality and clarity in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to test any given definition for the conditions of extensional equality (musawa) and epistemic clarity (ajla) and determine whether it is valid.

Core Idea
A definition must be equal in extension and clearer than the definiendum to truly define.

In this lesson, we examine the two essential conditions for a valid definition as explained by Dasuqi and 'Attar: extensional equality (musawa) and greater manifestness (ajla). The commentators show that a proper definiens must cover exactly the same individuals as the definiendum and must be more clearly known. Understanding these conditions helps us evaluate definitions in Islamic sciences such as fiqh and usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Find the two requirements mentioned at the beginning: equality (musawa) and clarity (ajla). These are the core conditions for a valid definition.
2
Understand equality (musawa)
Equality means that each one (definiens and definiendum) applies to all individuals of the other. Dasuqi explains that they are united in concept but differ in conciseness (definiens is concise essence, definition is detailed essence).
Equality is extensional, not conceptual identity.
3
Understand clarity (ajla)
The definiens must be more manifest, i.e., knowledge of it must precede knowledge of the definiendum. 'Attar emphasizes that the definiens is a cause for knowing the definiendum, so it must be more apparent to the intellect.
The opposite is 'more hidden' (akhfa), which cannot be known except after the definiendum.
4
Test a definition for coextension and reciprocity
'Attar analyzes equality as two universal affirmative propositions: ittiraad (coextension: every instance of definiens is an instance of definiendum, preventing non-instances) and 'aks (reciprocity: every instance of definiendum is an instance of definiens, ensuring completeness). If either fails, the definition is invalid.
Ittiraad failure makes the definition too broad; 'aks failure makes it too narrow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بحيث يصدقُ كلُّ واحد منهما على جميع أفراد الآخرِ. وكذا يُشترط أن يكونَ (أَجْلَى) وأوضح من المعرَّف . الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ: بِحَيْثُ يَصْدُقُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ ... إلخ) أي : فَالمعرَّفُ والمعرفُ مُتَّحدانِ . مفهوماً، وإِنَّما يختلفان بالإجمالِ والتَّفصيل، فالمعرف: الماهية المجملة، والتّعريفُ : الماهية المفصَّلة . (قَوْلُهُ : أَجْلَى) أي: وأجلى. (قَوْلُهُ : أَجْلَى وَأَوْضَحُ مِنَ الْمُعَرَّفِ :أي: بأن يكون معرفته سابقة على معرفة المعرّف، ومقابل الأوضح : الأخفى، وهو ما لا يمكن معرفته إلا بعد معرفة المعرَّف . العطار مفهوم المعرَّفِ كَاشتراط الوحداتِ الثَّمانية فى التَّناقض، وإلا ؛ لَمَا اختلف في التّعريف بالأعمّ مِنَ المعرَّفِ، حيثُ يصدقُ على الأعم وغيرِ الأَجَلي، فإنَّ الأعم وغير الأجلي عندَ مَن اشترط المساواة والإجلائية ليسَ مُفيداً للتصورِ ا.هـ. (قَوْلُهُ : بِحَيْثُ يَصْدُقُ ... إلخ) تصوير للمساواة هنا تنبيهاً على أنَّها في الصدقِ بخلافِ المساواة الآتية المنفيَّةِ ؛ فإنَّها في المعرفة، ولا يرد أنَّ هذا التصويرَ [؟] في هذا البابَ ؛ لأنَّ الغرض منهُ تطبيق المفهوم على المفهوم ؛ لا على الأفرادِ ؛ لأنَّهُ لا يلزمُ مِنْ صدقِ التَّعريف والمعرَّف على أفرادٍ واحدةٍ إرادة تلك الأفرادِ في حالِ التَّعريفِ، ثمَّ إِنَّكَ قَدْ عَلِمْتَ أنَّ مرجعَ التَّساوي لِمُوجبتَيْنِ كُلِّيَّتَيْنِ هُمَا هُنَا : كُلُّ مَا صدقَ عليهِ المعرَّفُ ؛ صدق عليه الماهيَّةُ المعرَّفةُ، وهو معنى الاطّراد ؛ أي: إذا وُجِدَ المعرَّفُ ؛ وُجِدَت الماهيَّةُ المعرَّفةُ، ويلزمُهُ أنْ يكونَ مانِعاً عَن دخول غير أفرادِ الماهية فيه، فإذا انتفَتْ هذه القضيَّةُ؛ فسدَ الطَّردُ ، وكلُّ ما صدق عليه الماهيَّةُ المعرَّفةُ ؛ صدق عليهِ المعرَّفُ ، فيكونُ مُنعَكِساً، بمعنى أنَّهُ : إذا انتفى المعرَّفُ ؛ انتفَتِ الماهيَّةُ المعرفةُ ، ويلزمُهُ أنْ يكونَ جَامِعاً لجميع أفرادِهَا، فإن انتفت هذه الكلية؛ فسد العكس. :(قَوْلُهُ : أَجْلَى ) أي : المعرّفُ مِن حيثُ الوجه الذي هو مُعرّفٌ؛ لا بُدَّ أنْ يكونَ أكثرَ ظُهوراً مِنَ المعرّفِ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ معرّف بالنِّسبة إلى السَّامع؛ لوجوب تقدم معرفتِهِ لِكَونِه سبباً، والقبلية في الحصولِ تستلزم زيادة ظهورِهِ عندَ العقل، وإِنَّما قُيّد
Such that each one of them applies to all individuals of the other. And likewise it is required that the definiens be more manifest and clearer than the definiendum. al-Dasuqi: (His saying: 'such that each one applies...') meaning: the definiendum and the definiens are united in concept, and differ only in conciseness and detail; the definiens is the concise essence, and the definition is the detailed essence. (His saying: 'more manifest') meaning: more manifest. (His saying: 'more manifest and clearer than the definiendum') meaning: that its knowledge is prior to knowledge of the definiendum, and the opposite of 'clearer' is 'more hidden', which is what cannot be known except after knowledge of the definiendum. al-'Attar: The concept of the definiendum, like requiring the eight negations in contradiction; otherwise there would be no disagreement about definition by what is more general than the definiendum, where it applies to the more general and the non-more manifest. For the more general and the non-more manifest according to one who requires equality and manifestation is not useful for conception. End. (His saying: 'such that each applies...') is a depiction of equality here, alerting that it is in truth, unlike the later negated equality, which is in knowledge. And it is not objected that this depiction is [built?] in this chapter because the purpose is to apply concept to concept, not to individuals, because the truth of the definition and definiendum to one set of individuals does not necessitate intending those individuals in the state of definition. Then you have known that the reference of equality for two universal affirmative propositions here is: everything to which the definiens applies, the defined essence applies to it – this is the meaning of ittiraad (coextension); i.e., if the definiens exists, the defined essence exists, and it follows that it prevents the entry of non-individuals of the essence into it. If this proposition is negated, the ittiraad is invalid. And everything to which the defined essence applies, the definiens applies to it, so it is reciprocal ('aks), meaning: if the definiens is absent, the defined essence is absent, and it follows that it encompasses all its individuals. If this universal is negated, the reciprocal is invalid. (His saying: 'more manifest') meaning: the definiens, in the aspect in which it is a definiens, must be more apparent than the definiendum, in that it is a definiens relative to the listener, due to the necessity of its knowledge preceding, as it is a cause, and priority in attainment entails increased manifestation in the intellect. And it is only restricted...
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the conditions for a valid definition. It begins by restating the two main conditions: First, the definiens (mu'arif) must be equal in extension (musawi) to the definiendum (mu'arraf), meaning that every individual of one is an individual of the other. Second, the definiens must be more manifest (ajla) and clearer (awdah) than the definiendum. The commentator al-Dasuqi then explains the first condition: the definiendum and definiens are identical in concept but differ in conciseness vs. detail; the definiens presents the essence concisely, while the definition presents it in detail. For the second condition, he clarifies that 'more manifest' means that knowledge of the definiens must precede knowledge of the definiendum. The opposite is 'more hidden' (akhfa), which cannot be known except after the definiendum. Next, al-'Attar expands on the first condition, equating it to the requirement of eight negations in contradiction (a logical principle). He argues that if equality and manifestation are not required, definition by what is more general would be valid, which is not useful for conception. He then explains the depiction of equality: it is in terms of truth value (sidq), not knowledge. The purpose is to compare concepts, not individuals. He then analyzes equality as two universal affirmative propositions: (1) coextension (ittiraad): everything the definiens applies to, the defined essence applies to; this ensures the definiens prevents non-individuals. (2) reciprocal ('aks): everything the defined essence applies to, the definiens applies to; this ensures the definiens encompasses all individuals. If either universal is negated, the respective condition fails. Finally, al-'Attar returns to the condition of 'more manifest': the definiens must be more apparent to the listener because knowledge of the definiens is the cause of knowledge of the definiendum, and priority in attainment entails greater intellectual clarity. He notes the restriction (taqyid) but the sentence is incomplete.

Key Terms
مساواة
أجلى
اطراد
عكس

Checkpoint
According to the text, if the condition of 'aks fails, what is the consequence for the definition?
A) The definition becomes more general than the definiendum
B) The definition becomes more specific than the definiendum
C) The definition is still valid but less clear
D) The definition is considered a tautology

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must satisfy both extensional equality (every individual matches) and epistemic clarity (definiens is better known).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'wine' (khamr) as 'an intoxicating beverage made from grapes'. Test if it satisfies equality: does it cover all intoxicating beverages? Does it exclude non-intoxicating grape juice? Test clarity: is 'intoxicating' clearer than 'wine'?
?
Identify whether the following definition of 'salah' (prayer) satisfies coextension and reciprocity: 'a set of specific actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim'. Does it cover all valid prayers? Does it prevent non-prayer acts from being included?

Why the Definiens Must Be Different from the Definiendum
The author presents the core argument for why the definiens cannot be identical to the definiendum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical necessity that the definiens must be different from the definiendum and apply this condition to detect circular definitions in Islamic terms.

Core Idea
The definiens must be known before the definiendum, so they cannot be identical.

When defining a term in Islamic logic, the definiens (the defining expression) must satisfy several conditions. One crucial condition is that it cannot be the same as the definiendum. Why? Because the definiens must be known prior to the definiendum, and no thing can be known before itself. This simple yet powerful argument ensures that definitions are informative and non-circular. In this lesson, we unpack this argument and see its application to Islamic legal definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disjunction
Recognize that the definiens must be either identical to the definiendum or different. The author presents this as a logical division.
2
Eliminate the identical option
Understand why identity is impossible: the definiens is known before the definiendum, but a thing cannot be known before itself. This is the core logical proof.
3
Conclude the definiens must be different
Therefore, the definiens is necessarily other than the definiendum. This establishes the condition of non-identity.
4
Apply to an Islamic term
Consider defining 'sawm' (fasting) as 'sawm'. This is circular and invalid. A valid definiens would be 'abstaining from food and drink with intention from dawn to sunset'.

(1) :(قَوْلُهُ : لأن ... إلخ) فيه أن المصنف لم يقرنه بـ «من».
Chapter: On the Definiens and Its Divisions. And it is only required that it be equal to it because it is not free from either being the same as the definiendum or other than it. There is no way to the first because the definiens is known before the definiendum, and a thing cannot be known before itself. Therefore it is determined that it be other than the definiendum. al-Dasuqi: Then his saying: 'more manifest and clearer' is a comparative form not used in its proper sense, because it implies that the definiendum is manifest, whereas what is manifest is not defined. The summary is that what is meant is that it is required for the definiens to be manifest and clear, such that its knowledge precedes knowledge of the definiendum. But this answer has something in it because the conjunction of the comparative with 'min' (than) for the one compared prevents it from being used in an unconventional way, so consider it. (His saying: 'And it is only required...') He restricted himself to explaining the reason for requiring equality, and did not mention the reason for requiring it to be more manifest, because it is obvious. (His saying: 'because it') i.e., the definiens. (His saying: 'the same as the definiendum') as when we interpret 'human' by 'human'. (His saying: 'or other than it') meaning different and contrary to it in conciseness and detail; otherwise it is identical in meaning. al-'Attar: Relative to the listener, because a thing may be more manifest for some people according to their sciences and craft, and not so for others. This is what al-Sayyid conveyed in his glosses on Sharh al-Matali'. And he only said 'more manifest' because the definiens has a manifestation in general in the aspect that it is the instrument of inquiry. And this condition includes both definition by genus and difference (hadd) and description (rasm), as is not hidden. End. 'Abd al-Hakim: (His saying: 'from being the same as the definiendum') If you say: after the definiens has been known as mentioned, its difference from the definiendum is understood from it; so the aforementioned disjunction is bad. I say: what follows from it is that its difference is in one aspect, and it does not require that it be from the aspect that it is a definiens. So the meaning is: the definiens is either the same as the definiendum in the aspect that it is a definiens, or other. There is no way to the first, i.e., there is no way for it, in the aspect that it is a definiens, to be the same as the definiendum such that it does not differ from it in any aspect. Said by 'Abd al-Hakim. (His saying: 'because ...') in it is that the author did not join it with 'min'.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage begins with a chapter heading 'On the Definiens and Its Divisions' and then presents the core reasoning for why the definiens must be equal to the definiendum yet not identical to it. The matn states: the definiens is required to be equal because it cannot be either the definiendum itself or other than it; the first is impossible because the definiens must be known before the definiendum, and a thing cannot be known before itself. Therefore it must be other. The commentator al-Dasuqi first addresses the phrase 'ajla wa awdah' (more manifest and clearer). He notes that this comparative form is not used in its usual sense because it would imply that the definiendum is manifest, but what is manifest does not need definition. The intended meaning is simply that the definiens must be manifest and clear, with knowledge of it preceding. However, Dasuqi points out a grammatical issue: since the comparative is followed by 'min' (than), it cannot be used in an unconventional way; the reader should examine this. He then notes that the author only gave a reason for requiring equality, not for requiring clarity, because the latter is obvious. He gives examples: if we define 'human' as 'human', that is circular and invalid; 'other' means different in conciseness and detail, though identical in meaning. Al-'Attar adds a contextual point: clarity is relative to the listener; what is clear for some may not be for others, citing al-Sayyid's gloss. He explains that the definiens has a general manifestation as the tool of inquiry, and the condition applies to both definitions by genus/difference (hadd) and descriptions (rasm). Finally, 'Abd al-Hakim addresses a potential objection: after knowing the definiens, its difference from the definiendum is understood, so the disjunction (same or other) seems redundant. He replies that the difference is only in one aspect (conciseness vs. detail) and not in the aspect of being a definiens. So the meaning is that the definiens cannot be the same as the definiendum in every aspect; it must differ in some way.

The Condition of Clarity: Is 'More Manifest' a Comparative?
Al-Dasuqi comments on the phrase 'ajla wa awdah' and clarifies its intended meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to interpret the phrase 'ajla wa awdah' (more manifest and clearer) in the context of the definiens condition and explain why it is not a true comparative in this context.

Core Idea
The definiens must be manifest and clear, but 'more manifest' is not used comparatively here because the definiendum is not manifest.

The matn states that the definiens must be 'more manifest and clearer' than the definiendum. But the commentator al-Dasuqi points out a problem: this comparative form implies that the definiendum itself is manifest to some degree, yet if it were manifest, it would not need definition. How do we resolve this? The answer is that the intended meaning is simply that the definiens must be manifest and clear, and the comparative is not used in its usual sense. In this lesson, we explore this linguistic nuance and its implications for definition theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problematic phrase
Find the phrase 'ajla wa awdah' in the commentary. Note that it is a comparative form (af'al tafdeel).
2
Understand the objection
Al-Dasuqi objects that if it is a genuine comparative, it would imply the definiendum is manifest, but what is manifest does not need definition. Therefore the comparative cannot be used in its proper sense here.
3
Reconcile the meaning
The intended meaning is that the definiens must be manifest and clear, with its knowledge preceding that of the definiendum. The comparative is used loosely to indicate priority, not a comparison with a manifest definiendum.
4
Note the grammatical point
Al-Dasuqi adds that because the comparative is followed by 'min' (than), the unconventional usage is problematic. The student is advised to reflect on this.

(قَوْلُهُ : نَفْسَ الْمُعَرَّفِ) كما إذا فسَّرنا إنساناً بإنسان . (قَوْلُهُ : أَوْ غَيْرَهُ) أَي مُغايراً ومُخالفاً لهُ بالإجمال والتفصيل، وإلا ؛ فهو عينه في المعنى. العطار بالنسبة إلى السامع ؛ لأنَّ الشَّيء قد يكونُ أجلى بالنسبة إلى قوم بحسب عليهم وصنعتهم، ولا يكون كذلك بالنسبة إلى قوم آخَرِيْنَ، كَذَا أَفَادَهُ السَّيِّدُ في حواشي شرح المطالع ، وإنّما قال: (أجلى)؛ لأنَّ لِلمعرّف ظهوراً في الجملة بالوجهِ الَّذي هو أَلةُ الطَّلبِ، وهذا الشَّرطُ شامل للحدّ والرَّسْمِ كَمَا لا يخفى ا.هـ. عبد الحكيم . (قَوْلُهُ : مِنْ أَنْ يَكُوْنَ نَفْسَ المُعَرَّفِ فإن قلتَ بعدَ مَا عُرِفَ المعرَّفُ بما مرَّ يُستفاد منهُ مُغايرتُهُ لِلمعرّف ؛ فالتَّرديدُ المذكورُ قبيح ؛ قلتُ : اللازم منهُ أنْ تكونَ مُغايرتُه بوجةٍ، وَلَا يلزمُ أنْ يكونَ ذلكَ مِنْ حيثُ إِنَّه مُعرَّفٌ، فالمراد : لأنَّ المعرَّفَ إمَّا أَنْ يكونَ نفس المعرّفِ من حيثُ إِنَّه مُعرَفٌ؛ أو غيره، لا سبيل إلى الأَوَّلِ ؛ أي: لا سبيل إلى أنَّهُ من حيثُ إِنَّهُ مُعرَفٌ ؛ نفس المعرّف بحيثُ لا يُغايرُهُ بِوجةٍ مِنَ الوجوه؛ قالَهُ عبد الحكيم . (1) :(قَوْلُهُ : لأن ... إلخ) فيه أن المصنف لم يقرنه بـ «من».
Chapter: On the Definiens and Its Divisions. And it is only required that it be equal to it because it is not free from either being the same as the definiendum or other than it. There is no way to the first because the definiens is known before the definiendum, and a thing cannot be known before itself. Therefore it is determined that it be other than the definiendum. al-Dasuqi: Then his saying: 'more manifest and clearer' is a comparative form not used in its proper sense, because it implies that the definiendum is manifest, whereas what is manifest is not defined. The summary is that what is meant is that it is required for the definiens to be manifest and clear, such that its knowledge precedes knowledge of the definiendum. But this answer has something in it because the conjunction of the comparative with 'min' (than) for the one compared prevents it from being used in an unconventional way, so consider it. (His saying: 'And it is only required...') He restricted himself to explaining the reason for requiring equality, and did not mention the reason for requiring it to be more manifest, because it is obvious. (His saying: 'because it') i.e., the definiens. (His saying: 'the same as the definiendum') as when we interpret 'human' by 'human'. (His saying: 'or other than it') meaning different and contrary to it in conciseness and detail; otherwise it is identical in meaning. al-'Attar: Relative to the listener, because a thing may be more manifest for some people according to their sciences and craft, and not so for others. This is what al-Sayyid conveyed in his glosses on Sharh al-Matali'. And he only said 'more manifest' because the definiens has a manifestation in general in the aspect that it is the instrument of inquiry. And this condition includes both definition by genus and difference (hadd) and description (rasm), as is not hidden. End. 'Abd al-Hakim: (His saying: 'from being the same as the definiendum') If you say: after the definiens has been known as mentioned, its difference from the definiendum is understood from it; so the aforementioned disjunction is bad. I say: what follows from it is that its difference is in one aspect, and it does not require that it be from the aspect that it is a definiens. So the meaning is: the definiens is either the same as the definiendum in the aspect that it is a definiens, or other. There is no way to the first, i.e., there is no way for it, in the aspect that it is a definiens, to be the same as the definiendum such that it does not differ from it in any aspect. Said by 'Abd al-Hakim. (His saying: 'because ...') in it is that the author did not join it with 'min'.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage begins with a chapter heading 'On the Definiens and Its Divisions' and then presents the core reasoning for why the definiens must be equal to the definiendum yet not identical to it. The matn states: the definiens is required to be equal because it cannot be either the definiendum itself or other than it; the first is impossible because the definiens must be known before the definiendum, and a thing cannot be known before itself. Therefore it must be other. The commentator al-Dasuqi first addresses the phrase 'ajla wa awdah' (more manifest and clearer). He notes that this comparative form is not used in its usual sense because it would imply that the definiendum is manifest, but what is manifest does not need definition. The intended meaning is simply that the definiens must be manifest and clear, with knowledge of it preceding. However, Dasuqi points out a grammatical issue: since the comparative is followed by 'min' (than), it cannot be used in an unconventional way; the reader should examine this. He then notes that the author only gave a reason for requiring equality, not for requiring clarity, because the latter is obvious. He gives examples: if we define 'human' as 'human', that is circular and invalid; 'other' means different in conciseness and detail, though identical in meaning. Al-'Attar adds a contextual point: clarity is relative to the listener; what is clear for some may not be for others, citing al-Sayyid's gloss. He explains that the definiens has a general manifestation as the tool of inquiry, and the condition applies to both definitions by genus/difference (hadd) and descriptions (rasm). Finally, 'Abd al-Hakim addresses a potential objection: after knowing the definiens, its difference from the definiendum is understood, so the disjunction (same or other) seems redundant. He replies that the difference is only in one aspect (conciseness vs. detail) and not in the aspect of being a definiens. So the meaning is that the definiens cannot be the same as the definiendum in every aspect; it must differ in some way.

Key Terms
المعرف
المعرف
أجلى وأوضح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Dasuqi, why is the phrase 'ajla wa awdah' not used in its proper sense as a comparative?
A) Because the definiens must be known after the definiendum
B) Because it would imply the definiendum is manifest, but manifest things do not need definition
C) Because the definiens is always hidden
D) Because Arabic grammar forbids comparatives

Key Takeaway
The requirement that the definiens be 'more manifest' means it must be clear and prior in knowledge, not that the definiendum is also manifest.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Consider the definition of 'taqlid' (following a scholar) given in Usul al-Fiqh: 'accepting the opinion of a scholar without knowing the evidence'. Explain how this definiens meets the condition of being manifest and clear compared to the definiendum.
?
Identify a definition from Islamic logic (e.g., definition of 'qiyas') and assess whether it uses the phrase 'more manifest' in a genuine comparative sense or merely to indicate clarity.
