Refining the Disjunction: Abd al-Hakim's Response to an Objection
Abd al-Hakim responds to an objection about the disjunction between same and different.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the objection that the disjunction between same and different is redundant and explain Abd al-Hakim's refinement that the difference is in aspect only.

Core Idea
The definiens differs from the definiendum in aspect (conciseness/detail), not in essential meaning.

After learning that the definiens must be different from the definiendum, a student might object: once we know the definiens, we already see it is different, so why even mention the possibility of identity? Abd al-Hakim addresses this by clarifying that the difference is only in one aspect (conciseness vs. detail), not in the aspect of being a definiens. In this lesson, we explore this subtle refinement and understand how the condition preserves the requirement of non-identity while allowing the definiens to express the same essential meaning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objection is: after knowing the definiens, its difference from the definiendum is already clear, so the disjunction (same or different) seems unnecessary or 'bad' (qabeeh).
2
Identify Abd al-Hakim's response
He argues that the difference is only 'in one aspect' (bi wajhin), meaning the definiens differs in conciseness and detail but is the same in essential meaning. The disjunction is not redundant because it addresses the overall relationship.
3
Apply the refinement
The definiens is not exactly identical (which would be circular), nor completely different in meaning. It is different in the sense of being more detailed or concise, but identical in meaning. This resolves the objection.
4
Note the final remark
A final remark points out that the author (in matn) did not join the comparative with 'min', which relates to the earlier discussion about 'more manifest'. This shows the interconnectedness of the commentary.

The Four Invalid Definitions and Conditions for a Valid Definer
Author states the conditions for a definer and lists four invalid definition types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the two necessary conditions for a valid definer and recognize the four types of invalid definitions.

Core Idea
A valid definer must be equal in scope and clearer than the defined.

In this passage, the author explains what makes a definition valid or invalid. The key is that the definer (المعرف) must be both coextensive with the defined term and more evident than it. If it fails either condition, the definition is defective. We will break down the reasoning and learn to spot the four classic invalid definition types used in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definer and defined
Locate in the Arabic text where the author talks about 'المعرِّف' (the definer) and 'المعرَّف' (the defined). Understand that these are the two sides of any definition.
2
Understand why the definer cannot be identical
The author argues that the definer cannot be the same as the defined, because the definer must be known before the defined, and a thing cannot be known before itself. Follow this logical elimination.
3
Extract the two conditions
After eliminating the identical case, the author concludes the definer must be other, but then restricts that other to be neither broader (أعم) nor narrower (أخص). So it must be equal (مساوٍ) and also clearer (أجلى). Note these as the two conditions.
4
List the four invalid definitions
The passage ends by naming four types: الأعم (more general), الأخص (more specific), المساوي معرفة (equal in knowledge, i.e., equally obscure), والأخفى (less clear). Relate each to a violation of the conditions.
The examples from the commentary: defining human as animal (أعم), fire as a substance resembling the soul (أخص), giraffe as an animal with leopard-like skin (مساوي معرفة), and fire with obscure concepts (أخفى).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ. وإِنَّما اسْتُرِطَ أن يكونَ مُساوِياً له؛ لأنَّه لا يخلو من أن يكون نفْسَ المعرَّفِ أو غيرَهُ، لا سبيلَ إلى الأوَّل؛ لأنَّ المعرّف معلوم قبل المعرّف، والشَّيءُ لا يُعلَمُ قبل نفْسِه، فتعين أن يكون غير المعرَّف. ثمَّ ذلكَ الغيرُ لم يَجُزْ أن يكون أعم ولا أخص؛ لما سنذكره، فتعيَّن أن يكونَ مُساوِياً أجلى. وإذا اشتُرِطَ أن يكون مساوياً أجلى فَلَا يَصِحُ التَّعريفُ بِالأَعَمّ، وَالأَخَصّ، وَالمَسَاوِي مَعْرِفَةٌ، وَالْأَخْفَى.
Chapter: On the Definer and its Divisions. It is required that it be equal to it; because it is either the same as the defined or other than it. The first is impossible, because the definer is known before the defined, and a thing is not known before itself. So it is determined that it be other than the defined. Then that other cannot be more general or more specific, for a reason we will mention. So it is determined that it be equal and clearer. And when it is required that it be equal and clearer, then definition is not valid by the more general, nor the more specific, nor the equal known, nor the less clear.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage defines the necessary conditions for a valid definer (المعرِّف) in logical definition. It begins by stating that the definer must be equal (مساوٍ) in scope to the defined term. The reasoning is that the definer can only be either identical to the defined or different from it. It cannot be identical, because that would mean knowing a thing before itself, which is impossible. Therefore it must be different. However, that different definer cannot be broader (أعم) or narrower (أخص) than the defined, as will be explained later. Thus it must be equal (مساوٍ) and also clearer (أجلى) than the defined. The passage then lists four types of definitions that are invalid: (1) using a more general term (الأعم) — e.g., defining 'human' as 'animal' without further specification; (2) using a more specific term (الأخص) — e.g., defining 'fire' as 'a substance resembling the soul'; (3) using an equally known term (المساوي معرفة) — e.g., defining 'giraffe' as 'an animal whose skin resembles a leopard's skin'; (4) using a less clear term (الأخفى) — e.g., defining 'fire' using obscure concepts. The conditions ensure that definition provides new, clearer knowledge.

Key Terms
المعرِّف
مساوٍ
أجلى
أعم
أخص
المساوي معرفة
الأخفى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must the definer (المعرِّف) be equal in scope to the defined?
A) Because if broader, it would include too many things; if narrower, it would omit essential parts.
B) Because the definer must be identical to the defined.
C) Because the definer must be more general to cover all cases.
D) Because the definer must be less clear to challenge the student.

Key Takeaway
A valid definer must be equal in scope (مساوٍ) and clearer (أجلى) than the defined; definitions violating these conditions are invalid, falling into one of four types: أعم, أخص, مساوي معرفة, or أخفى.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify which of the four invalid definition types is present in the following: 'Riba is defined as any increase that is predetermined.' Is this a valid definer? Why or why not?
?
Find an example from your own knowledge of fiqh or kalam where a definition uses a more general term (أعم) and explain why it fails the condition of equality.

Conditions for Valid Definition: Equal Scope and Clarity
Author states the conditions for valid definition and explains why four types are invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given definition is invalid due to being broader, narrower, equally obscure, or more obscure, and explain why.

Core Idea
A valid definition must be equal in scope and clearer than the definiendum.

This passage from Tadhheeb al-Mantiq lays out the fundamental conditions for any valid definition (ta'rif). You will learn to spot why a definition fails: either it doesn't cover exactly the same things (scope error) or it doesn't make things clearer (clarity error). Mastering these conditions will sharpen your ability to evaluate definitions in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definiens
Locate the term being defined (definiendum) and the words used to define it (definiens). For example, if someone defines 'khamr' as 'an intoxicating beverage', 'khamr' is the definiendum and 'intoxicating beverage' is the definiens.
2
Check the scope equality
Ask: Does the definiens apply to exactly the same things as the definiendum? If it applies to more (broader) or fewer (narrower), the definition fails. For instance, defining 'human' as 'animal' is broader; defining 'human' as 'writer' is narrower.
The passage stresses that broader terms do not give essence or distinguishing mark; narrower terms are less known.
3
Check the clarity
Ask: Is the definiens clearer or better known than the definiendum? If it is equally obscure or more obscure, the definition fails because it does not illuminate. For example, defining 'fire' by 'element resembling soul' is more obscure.
The condition of clarity (ajla) ensures the definition explains, not confuses.
4
Apply the two conditions to determine validity
Combine both checks: only if equal scope AND clearer is the definition valid. Otherwise, identify which of the four invalid types it falls into: broader, narrower, equally obscure, or more obscure. The passage explicitly rejects these four.
This step helps you systematically critique any definition you encounter in fiqh, usul, or kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلكَ الغيرُ لم يَجُزْ أن يكون أعم ولا أخص؛ لما سنذكره، فتعيَّن أن يكونَ مُساوِياً أجلى. وإذا اشتُرِطَ أن يكون مساوياً أجلى فلا يصح التعريف بالأعم والأخص والمساوي معرفة والأخفى. والحاصل: أنه لاشتراط تساويهما في الصدق لا يصح التعريف بالأعم ولا بالأخص، ولاشتراط جلائه لا يصح التعريف بالمساوي في المعرفة ولا بالأخفى. فصل في المعرف وأقسامه. وإنما لم يجز بالأعم؛ لأن المقصود من التعريف إما تصور المعرف بالكنه أو بوجه يميزه عن جميع ما عداه، والأعم لا يفيد شيئاً منهما. وإنما لم يجز بالأخص؛ لأنه أقل وجوداً في العقل.
That other [definiens] cannot be broader or narrower, as we will mention, so it is determined that it must be equal and clearer. And when it is conditioned that it be equal and clearer, then definition by the broader, the narrower, the equal in obscurity, and the more obscure is not valid. The summary: due to the condition of their equal scope in truth, definition by the broader or narrower is not valid, and due to the condition of its clarity, definition by the equal in obscurity or the more obscure is not valid. Chapter on the definition and its divisions. And it is not valid by the broader because the purpose of definition is either conceptualization of the definiendum in its essence or by a feature that distinguishes it from everything else, and the broader does not provide any of these. And it is not valid by the narrower because it is less existent in the mind.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage enumerates the conditions for a valid definition (ta'rif). It first states that the definiens cannot be broader (a'amm) or narrower (akhass) than the definiendum; rather, it must be equal (musawi) in scope and clearer (ajla) in conception. The author then explicitly lists four invalid types: (1) broader, (2) narrower, (3) equal in obscurity (musawi ma'rifa), and (4) more obscure (akhfa). The commentator (Dasuqi) summarizes that the condition of equal scope eliminates the broader and narrower, while the condition of clarity eliminates the equal in obscurity and the more obscure. The text then explains why each is invalid: a broader term fails because definition aims either to give the essence (kunnah) or a unique distinguishing mark, and broader covers additional things thus fails both. A narrower term is less existent in the mind (i.e., less known and more obscure), so it cannot clarify. Examples from the commentary illustrate: defining 'human' by 'animal' (broader), or by 'writer in act' (narrower), or defining 'fire' by 'body resembling soul' (more obscure).

Invalid Types of Definition: A'amm, Akhass, Musawi
Author explains three invalid types of definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain why definitions using more general (a'amm), more specific (akhass), or equally known (musawi) terms are invalid in Islamic logic.

Core Idea
A valid definiens must be coextensive and clearer than the definiendum; a'amm, akhass, and musawi fail these conditions.

This passage from the Tadhhib fi 'Ilm al-Mantiq lays out three common mistakes in definition. The author explains why the definiens must be coextensive with the definiendum and better known. Understanding these pitfalls helps you evaluate definitions in Islamic sciences like fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three invalid types
Scan the Arabic for the terms 'الأعم' (more general), 'الأخص' (more specific), and 'المساوي في المعرفة' (equal in knowledge). These are the three types of invalid definientia discussed.
2
Extract the reason for each type
For each type, find the reason given. For a'amm: it does not achieve the purpose of definition (conceiving essence or distinguishing). For akhass: it has less existence in the mind, so it is more obscure. For musawi: it is not more prior in knowledge than the definiendum.
The reason for a'amm is that it fails both aims: it neither reveals essence nor distinguishes.
3
Apply the reason to a test case
Take any definition, e.g., 'human' defined as 'body' (a'amm). 'Body' includes animals, plants, minerals – it does not distinguish humans. Then take a more specific definition, e.g., 'human' defined as 'this particular person' (akhass) – that is too narrow and obscure. Finally, consider two equal concepts like 'movement' and 'stillness' – defining one by the other is circular.
The example of movement and stillness shows why equivalence fails: knowing one necessitates knowing the other, so no priority.
4
Check the underlying principle
The author implies two conditions for a valid definiens: (1) it must be coextensive with the definiendum (neither broader nor narrower), and (2) it must be more known than the definiendum. The three invalid types violate one or both conditions.
A'amm violates coextensiveness; akhass violates clarity; musawi violates priority in knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ
وإِنَّما لم يَجُزْ بالأعمّ ؛ لأنَّ المقصود من التَّعريف، إمَّا تصورُ المعرَّفِ بالكنه، أو بوجه يميزه عن جميع ما عداه، والأعم لا يفيد شيئاً منهما .
وإِنَّما لمْ يَجُزْ بالأخص؛ لأنَّه أقلُّ وجوداً في العقل، وما هو أقل وجوداً في العقل يكون أخفى .
وإنَّما لم يجز بالمساوي معرفةٌ ؛ لأنَّ المعرِّفَ يجب أن يكونَ أقدم معرفةٌ من المعرَّفِ، وما يساوي الشَّيء في المعرفة والجهالة لا يكون أقدم معرفةً، فلا تُعرَّفُ الحركةُ بـ : ما ليس بسكون»؛ لتساوي الحركة والشكونِ معرفةً وجهالةً، فإنَّ من عَرَفَ أحدهما ؛ عرف الآخر، ومن جَهلَ أحدهما جهلَ الآخَرَ .
A chapter on definition and its divisions. It is not permissible to define by the more general because the purpose of definition is either to conceive the definiendum essentially or to distinguish it from everything else, and the more general does not achieve either. It is not permissible to define by the more specific because it has less existence in the mind, and that which has less existence in the mind is more obscure. It is not permissible to define by something equal in knowledge because the definer must be more prior in knowledge than the definiendum, and that which is equal to the thing in knowledge and ignorance is not more prior in knowledge. Thus movement is not defined as 'that which is not stillness' because movement and stillness are equal in knowledge and ignorance: whoever knows one knows the other, and whoever is ignorant of one is ignorant of the other.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage explains the invalid types of definition. The author enumerates three types that fail to satisfy the two primary conditions of definition: (1) coextensiveness with the definiendum, and (2) being clearer than the definiendum. First, the more general (al-a'amm) is invalid because definition aims either to grasp the essence (kunnh) or to distinguish the definiendum from everything else; a more general term includes things other than the definiendum, so it neither reveals the essence nor distinguishes. Second, the more specific (al-akhass) is invalid because it has less existence in the mind—that is, the specific is less frequently conceived than the general, making it more obscure; since the definer must be clearer, the more specific fails. The gloss by Dasuqi clarifies that 'more specific' here means 'specific in some respects' (a'amm min wajh) and its obscurity is relative. Third, definition by something equal in knowledge (al-musawi) is invalid because the definer must be better known (aqdam ma'rifah) than the definiendum; if two concepts are such that knowing one implies knowing the other and ignorance of one implies ignorance of the other, they are equal, and neither can define the other. The example given is movement and stillness: if one knows what movement is, one necessarily knows what stillness is (as its privation), and vice versa. Thus defining movement as 'not stillness' is circular. The commentator Dasuqi adds that the proper definition of movement is 'being in two times in two places' and stillness is 'being in two times in one place', which are clearer and coextensive. The marginal note by al-'Attar discusses a nuance: the equality holds only if movement and stillness are opposites (mutadaddan); if they are privation and possession ('adam wa milkah), then stillness is more obscure. However, the main argument stands: definition by equals is invalid.

Key Terms
الأعم
الأخص
المساوي في المعرفة
المعرف
التعريف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the more general term is less known than the definiendum.
B) Because the more general term does not distinguish the definiendum from other things.
C) Because the more general term is less existent in the mind.
D) Because the more general term is coextensive with the definiendum.

Key Takeaway
A valid definiens must be coextensive and more known than the definiendum; otherwise, it fails to achieve the purpose of definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'sawm' (fasting) as 'abstaining from food and drink from dawn to sunset'. Is this definition coextensive? What would be the problem if it were defined as 'abstaining from food' (a'amm) or 'abstaining from food and drink and sexual intercourse' (akhass for layperson)? Write one sentence evaluating each.
?
The logician's example of movement and stillness shows two concepts equal in knowledge. Find an example from fiqh where two concepts are mutually defining (e.g., 'halal' and 'haram'?) and explain why one cannot define the other.

Why Definition by Equal (Musawi) is Impermissible
Author argues against defining by equal with motion/rest example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a definition uses an equal (musawi) and explain why it fails.

Core Idea
A definer must be better known; an equal cannot define.

In logic, a definition must clarify the unknown by the known. This lesson explores why defining something by an equal—something equally known or unknown—is invalid. The passage from al-Tadhhib establishes this principle with the example of motion and rest, and the commentators clarify nuances about the nature of rest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Find in the Arabic text the condition that the definer (al-mu'arraf) must be prior in knowledge (aqdam ma'rifah) to the defined (al-mu'arraf). This is stated in the opening line.
The term 'aqdam ma'rifah' is key.
2
Extract the equality claim
The author claims that motion and rest are equal in knowledge and ignorance: knowing one implies knowing the other. Locate the sentence: 'li-tasawi al-harakati wa al-sukuni ma'rifatan wa jahālatan'.
This shows they are musawi (equal).
3
Apply the condition to the example
Since neither motion nor rest is prior, defining one by the negation of the other violates the principle. Thus the definition fails.
Even if rest were more hidden (as per al-‘Attar's nuance), it would be even worse; the main point is equality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنَّما لم يجز بالمساوي معرفةٌ ؛ لأنَّ المعرِّفَ يجب أن يكونَ أقدم معرفةٌ من المعرَّفِ، وما يساوي الشَّيء في المعرفة والجهالة لا يكون أقدم معرفةً، فلا تُعرَّفُ الحركةُ بـ : ما ليس بسكون»؛ لتساوي الحركة والشكونِ معرفةً وجهالةً، فإنَّ من عَرَفَ أحدهما ؛ عرف الآخر، ومن جَهلَ أحدهما جهلَ الآخَرَ .
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ: يَكُوْنُ أَخْفَى هذا يقتضي أنَّهُ يستغنى بقوله: (والأخفى) عن قوله: (الأخص)، والجواب : أَنَّهُ ذكرَهُ ؛ لِكَونِهِ مُقابلاً للأعمّ ، وأنَّ الأَوَّلَ وقع في مركزه. (قَوْلُهُ : فَلَا تُعَرَّفُ ... إِلَخ) أي : وإِنَّما نُعرِّفُها بأنَّهَا كَونَانِ فِي آنَيْنِ فِي مَكَانَيْنِ، والشكونُ هو الشكونُ الثَّاني في الحيّز الأوَّل.
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : لِتَسَاوِي الْحَرَكَةِ وَالسُّكُونِ قالَ السَّيِّدُ : هذا إِنَّما يصح إذا لم يكن الشكونُ عبارةٌ عن عدم الحركة، وإلا ؛ لَكانَ السُّكونُ أخفَى مِنَ الحركةِ لَا مُساوياً لها، وإذا امتنع تعريفُ الشَّيء بما يساويه في المعرفة والجهالة؛ كانَ امتناع تعريفه بما هو أخفَى منه أولى .ا.هـ. والحاصل أنَّ الحركة والشكون في مرتبةٍ واحدةٍ مِنَ العِلْمِ والجهل على تقدير أن يكونَ بينَهُما تقابل التّضاد، فإنَّ الحركة حينئذٍ : كونُ الشَّيء في آنين في مكانَيْنِ ، والشكونَ : كونُ الشَّيء في آنين في مكانٍ واحدٍ، وهذانِ المفهومان الوجوديَّانِ المتضادَّانِ مُتساويان في العلم والجهل، أمَّا إذا كانَ بينَهُمَا تقابل العدم والملكة؛ فيكون الشكونُ أخفّى؛ لأنَّ الأعدامَ تُعرَفُ بملكاتِهَا .
Definition by equal is not permissible because the definer must be prior in knowledge to the defined, and what is equal to a thing in knowledge and ignorance is not prior in knowledge. Thus motion is not defined by 'what is not rest', because motion and rest are equal in knowledge and ignorance: whoever knows one knows the other, and whoever is ignorant of one is ignorant of the other. al-Dasuqi: His saying 'is more hidden' implies that his saying '(the more hidden)' suffices instead of his saying '(the more specific)'. The answer: he mentioned it because it is the opposite of the more general, and the first fell in its place. His saying 'so motion is not defined...' i.e. we define it as being in two instants in two places, and rest is the second instant in the same place. al-‘Attar: His saying 'because motion and rest are equal' – al-Sayyid said: this is correct only if rest is not an expression for the absence of motion; otherwise, rest would be more hidden than motion, not equal to it. If definition by what is equal in knowledge and ignorance is impossible, then definition by what is more hidden is even more impossible. The conclusion is that motion and rest are on one level of knowledge and ignorance on the assumption that there is a relation of opposition between them: motion is the thing being in two instants in two places, and rest is the thing being in two instants in one place. These two existential opposing concepts are equal in knowledge and ignorance. But if there is a relation of privation and possession, then rest is more hidden because privations are known by their possessions.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage argues against defining something by what is equal in knowledge and ignorance. The author first states the principle: a definer must be better known (a'raf) than the defined. If two concepts are equally known, neither can be prior. The example given is motion (haraka) and rest (sukun). If you try to define motion as 'what is not rest', the definition fails because knowing motion implies knowing rest, and vice versa. The commentators elaborate: al-Dasuqi notes that the author earlier mentioned 'more hidden' (akhfa) in the text, but here focuses on 'more specific' (akhas) – they are complementary. He explains that motion is defined as 'being in two instants in two places' and rest as 'second instant in the same place'. Al-‘Attar brings an important nuance: the equality holds only if rest is considered an existing attribute (strict opposite of motion). If rest is defined as mere absence of motion (privation), then rest would be more hidden (since privations are known through their opposite possessions). Thus, the definition by equal is invalid, and even more so by the more hidden.

Key Terms
المساوي
أقدم معرفة
الحركة
السكون
النقيض

Checkpoint

C) Because the definition uses a negative term.
D) Because rest is not a genuine attribute.

Key Takeaway
Definition by an equal (musawi) fails because it violates the requirement that the definer be prior in knowledge.

The Invalidity of Definition by the More Hidden (Akhfa)
Author states the invalidity of definition by the more hidden.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a definer is more hidden than the definiendum and explain why such a definition is invalid using the priority argument.

Core Idea
If definition by the equal is invalid, then definition by the more hidden is even more invalid.

In logic, a definition must make the unknown known. Therefore, the definer must be more known than the definiendum. The author argues that if an equally known definer is invalid, then a more hidden definer is even more unacceptable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for valid definition
The definer must be more known than the definiendum. Check if the definer is at least as known.
2
Understand the priority argument
The text uses a priority argument: if definition by something equal is invalid, then by something more hidden (less known) is even more invalid.
This is a qiyas awlawi (a fortiori argument).
3
Apply to a real case
In Islamic sciences, when defining a term, ensure you do not use a term less known. For example, defining 'ribā' using a term like 'al-ribwah' which is even more obscure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وَإِنَّمَا لَمْ يَجُزْ بِالْأَخْفَى ؛ لأنَّ المساوي لَمَّا لم يصح؛ فالأخفى بطريقِ الأولى.
[بيان الحد والرَّسم]
( وَالتَّعْرِيفُ بِالفَصْلِ القَرِيبِ : حَدٌ، وَبِالخَاصَّةِ : رَسْمُ).

(قَوْلُهُ : وَإِنَّمَا لَمْ يَجُزْ بِالْأَخْفَى إِنَّما تعرَّضَ المصنِّفُ لنفي صحتِهِ بعد اشتراط المساواة؛ لهجر الدَّلالة الالتزاميَّةِ فى البيان، ولكونه ضدَّ الأجلّى. (قَوْلُهُ : فَالْأَخْفَى بِطَرِيْقِ الْأَوْلَى فيه : أنَّه لا حاجةً حينئذٍ لِقَولِهِ : (الأخفى) بعد قوله : (المساوي) على هذا، إِلَّا أَنْ يُقالَ : إِنَّه ذكرَ لِلتَّوضيح.
(قَوْلُهُ : وَالتَّعْرِيْفُ بِالْفَصْلِ : حَدٌ، وَبِالْخَاصَّةِ : رَسُمٌ) فيه : أَنَّ التَّعريف صفةٌ لِلشَّخص المعرَّف، والحدُّ والرَّسم ليسَا وَصفَيْن له، وحينئذٍ ؛ فلا يصح حملُهُمَا عليه فكانَ الأَوْلَى أنْ يقول : تحديد وترسيم أو يقول : والفصلُ القريب المعرَّفُ به حد، والخاصة المعرَّفُ بها رسمٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يُقالَ : إِنَّ التَّعريف صارَ حقيقةً عُرفيَّةً في الحد والرسم، والرَّسم، أو أنَّ المصدر بمعنى اسم الفاعل، أو الباء في قوله: بالفصل)؛ للتصوير، تأمل. به
(قَوْلُهُ : حَدٌ) المناسب أن يقول: تحديد وترسيم؛ لأنَّ المبتدأ (١) ، وهو التّعريفُ ؛ فعل الفاعل، أو يقول : والفصلُ القريب المعرَّفُ به حد، والخاصة المعرَّفُ بها رسمٌ، فَتَأَمَّلْ .
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : وَالتَّعْرِيْفُ بِالْفَصْلِ الْقَرِيْبِ الباء للملابسة؛ من ملابسةِ الكُلّي لجزئيه، والمصدر بمعنى اسم الفاعل، فيصيرُ المعنى والمعرَّفُ الملابس للفصل القريب حَدٌ ، ويُقالُ مثلُهُ في نظيرهِ، وَلِلمحشّي هنا كلام ساقط عن درجة الاعتبار. Chapter: On the Definer and its Divisions
Definition by the more hidden is not permissible, because since the equal is not valid, the more hidden is even more so.
[Statement of hadd and rasm]
Definition by the proximate differentia is hadd, and by the property is rasm.
al-Dasuqi: His saying 'definition by the more hidden is not permissible' – the author addressed its invalidity after stipulating equality, because it abandons implicative indication in clarity, and because it is contrary to the more manifest. His saying 'so the more hidden is even more so' – there is no need for his saying 'the more hidden' after his saying 'the equal' except to say he mentioned it for clarification. His saying 'definition by the differentia is hadd, by the property is rasm' – here the 'definition' is an attribute of the person defined, while hadd and rasm are not attributes of him, so it is not correct to predicate them of him. It would have been better to say 'determination and description', or 'the proximate differentia by which it is defined is hadd, and the property by which it is defined is rasm', unless one says that 'definition' has become a conventional term for hadd and rasm, or that the masdar is in the sense of the active participle, or that the ba in 'by the differentia' is for depiction – reflect. His saying 'hadd' – it would be appropriate to say 'determination and description' because the subject (which is 'definition') is a verbal noun, or say 'the proximate differentia by which it is defined is hadd, and the property by which it is defined is rasm' – reflect.
al-‘Attar: His saying 'definition by the proximate differentia' – the ba is for association, from the association of the universal with its parts, and the masdar is in the sense of the active participle, so the meaning becomes: the definer associated with the proximate differentia is hadd. The same is said for its counterpart. The commentator here has worthless speech below consideration. (Footnote: His saying 'because the subject...' – he discussed this objection earlier and answered it, so there is no need to repeat it or to command reflection twice at once. It seems that the author intended by 'definition' the definer, and the ba is for depiction. End.)
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is a new section defining the types of definition. First, it reiterates that definition by something more hidden (akhfa) is invalid, using a priority argument: if something equal is invalid, then something more hidden is even less acceptable. The author then defines two key terms: 'definition by the proximate differentia is called hadd (limiting definition), and by the property (specific property) is called rasm (description).' 

The commentators examine linguistic and logical issues. Al-Dasuqi notes that the author could have omitted 'the more hidden' after already stating 'the equal', but he includes it for clarity. Then he critiques the phrasing: 'definition by the differentia is hadd' – since 'definition' is an attribute of the person being defined, while 'hadd' and 'rasm' are not such attributes, the sentence is problematic. He suggests better formulations: 'determination and description' as verbal nouns, or restructuring to 'the proximate differentia by which it is defined is hadd'. He offers possible justifications: 'definition' became a conventional term for hadd/rasm, or the verbal noun means active participle, or the 'ba' is for depiction.

Al-‘Attar resolves the issue by interpreting the 'ba' as for association (al-mulabasa) and the masdar as active participle, so the meaning becomes 'the definer associated with the proximate differentia is hadd'. He dismisses another commentator's objection as worthless. This passage shows the careful grammatical and logical analysis typical of the sharh tradition.

المساوي

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must use a term more known than the definiendum; the more hidden fails even more than the equal.

Distinguishing Hadd (Essential Definition) from Rasm (Descriptive Definition)
Author defines hadd and rasm, with grammatical critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish hadd from rasm based on whether the definer is a proximate differentia or a property.

Core Idea
Hadd uses the proximate differentia to capture essence; rasm uses a property (khāṣṣah) for description.

This lesson introduces two key types of definitions: hadd (essential definition) and rasm (descriptive definition). The author states that definition by the proximate differentia is hadd, and by the property is rasm. The commentators then examine the grammatical and logical phrasing of this statement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining element
Look at the definer: if it is the proximate differentia (al-faṣl al-qarīb), the definition is hadd; if it is a property (al-khāṣṣah), it is rasm.
2
Understand the difference
Hadd gives the essence (māhiyya) by specifying the immediate specific difference. Rasm gives a description by using a property that is co-extensive but not part of the essence.
3
Analyze the grammatical issue raised
The commentators note that the phrasing 'definition by the differentia is hadd' is grammatically problematic because 'ta'rīf' (definition) is an attribute of the defined, while 'hadd' is a type of definition. Suggested corrections include using 'taḥdīd' or restructuring.
Al-Dasuqi's objection and al-‘Attar's resolution.
4
Apply the distinction to an Islamic example
For instance, defining 'human' as 'rational animal' (hadd) vs. 'laughing animal' (rasm). In fiqh, defining 'ṣalāh' as 'specific actions and words' (rasm) vs. 'submission to Allah' (hadd).

Complete vs Incomplete Definitions: Inclusion of the Near Genus
Author completes classification of definitions into complete and incomplete based on inclusion of the near genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a given definition as complete (tamm) or deficient (naqis) by checking whether it includes the near genus along with the differentia or specific property.

Core Idea
A definition's completeness depends on one thing: does it include the near genus?

In this passage, the author completes the classification of definitions by introducing the condition of completeness. The key insight is that a definition is complete only when it includes the near genus (jins qarib) together with either the near differentia (fasl qarib) for a hadd or the specific property (khassa) for a rasm. Otherwise, it is deficient (naqis). This rule provides a clear criterion for evaluating definitions in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of the definition
List the genus, differentia, and/or specific property mentioned in the definition. For example, in 'rational animal', the genus is 'animal' and the differentia is 'rational'.
The genus must be the immediate (near) genus, not a remote one.
2
Check for the presence of the near genus
Determine whether the genus used is the nearest genus that contains the defined term. For 'human', the near genus is 'animal', not 'body' or 'substance'.
A remote genus alone makes the definition deficient (naqis).
3
Determine completeness based on components
If the near genus is present with the near differentia, it is a complete hadd (حد تام). If the near genus is present with a specific property, it is a complete rasm (رسم تام). Otherwise, it is deficient.
Complete definitions are either hadd tamm or rasm tamm.
4
Apply the distinction to Islamic definitions
Practise by evaluating definitions from Usul al-Fiqh or Kalam, such as 'qiyas is the derivation of a ruling from an original case based on a common effective cause'.
Check if the near genus (e.g., 'derivation of a ruling') and the differentia ('from an original case based on a common effective cause') are included.

إمَّا حد إن كانَ بالجنس والفصل القريتين .
الدسوقي
وحاصل ما ذكرَهُ : أَنَّ الحدّيَّةَ مُوكولةٌ للفصل القريب، والرَّسميَّةً مُوكولةٌ للخاصَّة، والتّمام موكول لمصاحبة الجنس القريب لما ذكر، والنقصان موكول للجنس البعيد، أو عدم ذلكَ الجنس رأساً .
(قَوْلُهُ : فَإِنْ كَانَ الْفَضْلُ ... إلخ) الأَوْلَى أنْ يقول : أي : كلّ من الفصل والخاصة؛ لأنَّ الواجب تثنيةُ الضَّميرِ، فَالإفراد للتَّأويل بكلِّ.
(قَوْلُهُ : إِمَّا حَدٌ . . . إِلَخ) يشيرُ إلى أنَّ المراد بقولِهِ : فتام: حد تام، أو رسم تام ; إذ الاسم الحد الثام، والرَّسمُ الشَّام، لَا مُجرَّد الثَّام، وإنَّما كانَ التَّعريفُ بالجنس والفصل القريبين تاما ; لِكُونِهِ بِجَمِيعِ الذاتيات، وكانَ التَّعريف بالجنس القريب والخاصَّةِ رسماً تاماً ; لِمُشابهتِهِ لِلحدِّ التَّامّ لِلاشتمال على الجنس القريب; معَ التَّقييد بما يخص المعرَّف.
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : إِنْ كَانَ بِالْجِنْسِ وَالْفَصْلِ وَلَا يجب تقديم الجنس، فقد قالَ الشَّيخُ في بعض تعليقاتِهِ : ناطق حيوان حد تام، إلَّا إِنَّ الأَوْلَى تقديم الأعمّ لِشهرتِهِ وظهورِهِ، نَعَمْ لَا بُدَّ مِن تَقييدِ أحدِهِمَا بِالآخَرِ حتَّى تحصل صورةٌ مطابقة للمحدود، وذلك لا يحتاج إلى حركة ثانية ا.هـ. قالَ مير زاهد والسِّرُّ فيهِ أنَّ ذاتِيَّاتِ الشَّيء في أَنفُسِها : موجودةٌ بوجودِ ذلكَ الشَّيء ومُتَّحدةٌ معه، فبعد تحليل الذِّهْنِ بأي ترتيب يحصلُ; تكونُ مُنطبقةً على الحقيقةِ الواحدة المحصَّلة، وإنَّما احتيج لتقييد أحدِهِمَا بِالآخَرِ، إذْ لولاهُ لَكَانَتِ الأجزاء كثرةً محضةً ; فلا تكون منطبقةً على الحقيقة الواحدة المحصلة ا.هـ.
If the near differentia or the specific property [is] with the near genus, then it is complete. Either a hadd if it is by the near genus and differentia. al-Dasuqi: The summary of what he mentioned: that the property of being a hadd is delegated to the near differentia, and the property of being a rasm is delegated to the specific property, and completeness is delegated to the accompaniment of the near genus for what was mentioned, and deficiency is delegated to the remote genus, or the total absence of that genus. (His statement: 'If the differentia... etc.') It is better for him to say: that is, each of the differentia and the specific property, because the pronoun must be dual, so the singular is for interpretation by 'each'. (His statement: 'Either a hadd... etc.') He indicates that what is meant by his saying 'complete' is a complete hadd or a complete rasm, for the name 'hadd' is the complete [definition] and 'rasm' is the complete [description], not merely the complete [in any sense]. Rather, definition by the near genus and near differentia is complete because it is by all the essential properties, and definition by the near genus and specific property is a complete rasm due to its similarity to the complete hadd for including the near genus, along with the restriction to what particularizes the definiendum. al-'Attar: (His statement: 'If by the genus and differentia, and it is not necessary to present the genus first') For the Shaykh said in some of his comments: 'Rational animal' is a complete hadd, except that it is better to present the more general due to its renown and clarity. Yes, it is necessary to restrict one by the other so that a form corresponding to the definiendum is obtained, and that does not require a second movement. End. Mir Zahid said: The secret in it is that the essential properties of the thing in themselves exist with the existence of that thing and are united with it. So after the mind's analysis, in whatever order it obtains, they will be conformable to the one realized reality. The need for restricting one by the other is only because otherwise the parts would be a pure multiplicity and would not conform to the one realized reality. End.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage completes the classification of definitions by introducing the condition of completeness. The matn states: if the near differentia (fasl qarib) or the specific property (khassa) is accompanied by the near genus (jins qarib), then the definition is complete (tamm). It will be either a complete hadd (if using near genus and near differentia) or a complete rasm (if using near genus and specific property). Al-Dasuqi summarizes: the 'haddiyya' (being a hadd) depends on the near differentia, the 'rasmiyya' (being a rasm) depends on the specific property, completeness (tamam) depends on the presence of the near genus, and deficiency (naqs) results from using a remote genus or no genus at all. He also notes a grammatical issue: the pronoun in the condition should be dual, but the singular is used because it is interpreted as 'each'. Then he clarifies that the term 'tamm' in the conclusion refers specifically to a complete hadd or a complete rasm—not just any complete thing. A definition by near genus and near differentia is complete because it includes all the essential properties (dhatiyyat). A definition by near genus and specific property is a complete rasm because it includes the near genus and restricts it with a unique property. Al-'Attar then discusses the order of the components: it is not necessary to present the genus first; 'natiq hayawan' (rational animal) is also a complete hadd. However, it is better to present the more general first for clarity. The secret, as Mir Zahid explains, is that the essential properties exist united in the thing, so any order in the mind still yields a single reality. But a restriction (taqyid) of one component by the other is necessary to avoid a mere multiplicity of parts that would not correspond to the one reality.

الجنس القريب
التمام
النقصان
حد تام
رسم تام

A definition is complete only if it includes the near genus together with a differentia or specific property; otherwise it is deficient.

Hadd and Rasm

The Four Types of Definitions: Perfect and Imperfect Hadd and Rasm
Author classifies definitions into perfect and imperfect hadd/rasm based on components.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given definition as one of the four types (perfect hadd, imperfect hadd, perfect rasm, imperfect rasm) by identifying whether it includes the proximate genus and whether it uses a differentia or property.

Core Idea
A definition is perfect only when it includes the proximate genus; without it, even a correct differentia yields an imperfect definition.

In Islamic logic, definitions are not all equal. Some capture the essence completely, others only partially. This lesson teaches you the precise criteria for evaluating definitions—a skill essential for rigorous work in Usul al-Fiqh and Kalam, where a flawed definition can lead to invalid legal rulings or theological conclusions. The passage classifies definitions into four types based on two factors: the presence of the proximate genus, and whether the distinguishing feature is essential (differentia) or accidental (property).

Guided Path
1
Identify the distinguishing feature
First, check whether the definition uses an essential differentia (fasl qarib) or an accidental property (khassa). This determines whether the definition is a hadd (definition proper) or a rasm (description).
2
Identify the genus used
Next, look for the genus (jins). If present, is it the proximate genus (jins qarib, the immediate category above) or a remote genus (jins ba'id, further up)? If no genus is mentioned, note that too.
3
Apply the rule for perfection
Recall the rule: if the definition includes the proximate genus together with either the proximate differentia or property, it is perfect (tam). If it lacks the proximate genus (using only a remote genus or no genus at all), it is imperfect (naqis).
4
Determine the specific type
Combine the two factors: proximate genus + differentia = hadd tam; proximate genus + property = rasm tam; differentia alone or with remote genus = hadd naqis; property alone or with remote genus = rasm naqis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ كَانَ الْفَصْلُ الْقَرِيبُ أَوِ الْخَاصَّةُ مَعَ الْجِنْسِ الْقَرِيبِ؛ فَتَامٌ. إِمَّا حَدٌّ إِنْ كَانَ بِالْجِنْسِ وَالْفَصْلِ الْقَرِيبَيْنِ، وَإِمَّا رَسْمٌ إِنْ كَانَ بِالْخَاصَّةِ وَالْجِنْسِ الْقَرِيبِ. وَإِلَّا : أَيْ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْفَصْلِ وَالْخَاصَّةِ مَعَ الْجِنْسِ الْقَرِيبِ، بَلْ يَكُونُ وَحْدَهُ أَوْ مَعَ الْجِنْسِ الْبَعِيدِ؛ فَنَاقِصٌ. إِمَّا حَدٌّ إِنْ كَانَ بِالْفَصْلِ الْقَرِيبِ وَحْدَهُ، أَوْ بِهِ وَبِالْجِنْسِ الْبَعِيدِ. وَإِمَّا رَسْمٌ إِنْ كَانَ بِالْخَاصَّةِ وَحْدَهَا أَوْ بِهَا وَبِالْجِنْسِ الْبَعِيدِ. فَالْمُعَرِّفُ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَامٍ : حَدٌّ تَامٌّ، وَحَدٌّ نَاقِصٌ، وَرَسْمٌ تَامٌّ، وَرَسْمٌ نَاقِصٌ.
If the proximate differentia or property is with the proximate genus, then it is perfect: either a definition if it is with the proximate genus and proximate differentia, or a description if it is with the property and proximate genus. And if not—that is, if neither the differentia nor the property is with the proximate genus, but rather alone or with the remote genus—then it is imperfect: either a definition if it is with the proximate differentia alone or with it and the remote genus, or a description if it is with the property alone or with it and the remote genus. So the definer has four divisions: perfect definition, imperfect definition, perfect description, and imperfect description.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a classification of definitions into four types based on the components used. The author begins by stating the condition for a perfect definition: it must include the proximate genus together with either the proximate differentia (for hadd) or the property (for rasm). For example, defining 'human' as 'rational animal' is a perfect definition (hadd tam) because it combines the proximate genus 'animal' with the essential differentia 'rational'. Defining it as 'laughing animal' is a perfect description (rasm tam) because it uses the proximate genus with the accidental property 'laughing'. The passage then states the condition for imperfect definitions: when the proximate genus is missing, either because the differentia or property stands alone or is combined with a remote genus. For instance, defining 'human' simply as 'rational' (without genus) is an imperfect definition (hadd naqis), and defining it as 'laughing' alone is an imperfect description (rasm naqis). The classification thus yields four types: perfect hadd, imperfect hadd, perfect rasm, and imperfect rasm. The commentary further explains that perfection is tied to including the proximate genus, which provides the broader category, while the differentia or property provides the distinguishing feature. In Islamic logic, this classification helps evaluate how fully a definition captures the essence of a thing.

رسم
تام
ناقص
جنس قريب
فصل قريب
خاصة

According to the passage, what makes a definition imperfect (naqis)?
A) It uses a remote genus instead of a proximate genus
B) It lacks the proximate genus, using the differentia or property alone or with a remote genus
C) It uses a property instead of a differentia
D) It includes both genus and differentia but in the wrong order

Key Takeaway
A definition is classified as perfect when it includes the proximate genus; otherwise it is imperfect, regardless of whether it uses a differentia or property.

Why the Accidental General is Excluded from Definitions
Explains why 'arad 'am is excluded from definitions with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the accidental general ('arad 'am) is not included in definitions and identify when its inclusion would be redundant.

Core Idea
The accidental general adds no benefit in definitions; only essential or unique attributes matter.

In defining a species, we use attributes that either capture its essence or uniquely identify it. The accidental general, like 'walking' for humans, spans multiple species and contributes nothing to complete distinction or essential knowledge. This lesson unpacks why such attributes are excluded from definitions, drawing on the classical commentary tradition.

Guided Path
1
Recall the purpose of definition
The passage states that definition aims at either complete distinction (tamyiz tāmm) or knowledge of essential attributes (dhatiyyāt). Keep this twofold objective in mind as you evaluate candidate components.
2
Identify the accidental general's role
The accidental general, like 'breathing' or 'walking', applies to multiple species and is not part of any essence. Check if it contributes to either purpose: does it help distinguish the species uniquely? Does it reveal an essential attribute?
3
Test pairing with the differentia or specific property
If you pair the accidental general with the differentia (e.g., 'rational') or the specific property (e.g., 'laughing'), the distinction is achieved by that partner alone. The accidental general becomes redundant, like saying 'walking rational animal' for humans.
Al-Dasuqi explains: 'the complete distinction is only obtained from the specific property or the differentia, and the accidental has no benefit.'
4
Consider the exception in incomplete descriptions
Al-'Attar notes that in incomplete descriptions (rusum nāqisa), the accidental general may appear, but even then, when paired with a differentia or specific property, it is unnecessary. Al-Sayyid adds that a compound of accidental general and specific property is still a description, but stronger than the property alone.
5
Apply the rule to Islamic definitions
In defining 'salah' as 'specific actions and sayings beginning with takbir and ending with taslim,' adding 'intentional' (a common accidental general) is redundant because intention is already implied by the specific property. This shows how the principle works in fiqh.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(قَوْلُهُ : وَلَا فَائِدَةَ فِي ضَمِّهِ مَعَ أَحَدِهِمَا ) أي : بحيثُ تعرّفه بالماشي الضاحك، أو الماشي الناطق. العطار اعتبارَهُ في الرُّسومِ النَّاقصة دون الحدودِ النَّاقصة مبني على جواز التعريف بالأعم، والتّعريفُ بالعرض العام وحدَهُ، فإنَّهُ كَمَا لا حاجة إليه مع وجودِ الفصل؛ لا حاجةً إليه مع وجودِ الخاصَّةِ .ا.هـ. وصوَّبَ السَّيِّدُ أنَّ المركَّبَ مِنَ العرضِ العام والخاصَّة
And it is not a part of the definition; because if it were a part, it would be either with the specific property or the differentia. And there is no benefit in joining it with one of them. Therefore the accidental general was dropped from consideration in definitions, and it is only mentioned in the chapter on universals to complete the divisions of the universal. Al-Dasuqi: His statement: 'And there is no benefit in joining it with one of them' means: because the complete distinction of the definiendum is only achieved by that one. It may be said: They both also suffice for the genus, for 'animal with rational or laughing' has no benefit. And it is answered: In mentioning it there is a benefit not taken from them, namely clarifying a part of the essence, unlike if we join 'breathing' with 'rational'—there is no benefit in it because it is not from the parts of the essence. And his statement 'and there is no benefit...' etc. means: because the purpose of definition is either complete distinction or knowledge of the essential attributes, and the accidental general does not benefit either. Therefore there is no benefit in joining it with one of them, since complete distinction of the definiendum is only achieved by one of them, and mentioning the accidental with one of them is dispensable. And his statement: 'it would be either with the specific property or the differentia' means: not with the genus, due to the reason given that it is not suitable as a definer. The conclusion: The accidental alone or with the genus is incapable of providing definition because it does not give complete distinction, and when joined with the specific property or the differentia, the complete distinction is only obtained from the specific property or the differentia, and the accidental has no benefit. His statement: 'And there is no benefit in joining it with one of them' means: such that you define it by 'the walking one who laughs' or 'the walking one who speaks rationally.' Al-'Attar: Considering it in incomplete descriptions [rusum] and not in incomplete definitions [hudud] is based on the permissibility of definition by the broader term. And definition by the accidental general alone is such that, just as there is no need for it in the presence of the differentia, there is no need for it in the presence of the specific property. End. And al-Sayyid corrected that the compound of the accidental general and the specific property
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage explains why the accidental general attribute ('arad 'am) is not included in definitions. The author begins by stating that the accidental general cannot be part of a definition because if it were, it would have to be paired with either the specific property (khassa) or the differentia (fasl). However, pairing it adds no benefit, so it is omitted from definitions altogether. The author notes that the accidental general is only mentioned in the chapter on universals for completeness. Al-Dasuqi's commentary elaborates: The purpose of definition is either complete distinction (tamyiz tam) or knowledge of essential attributes (dhatiyyat). The accidental general serves neither purpose. When combined with a specific property or differentia, the distinction is achieved by that property or differentia, rendering the accidental general superfluous. An example: Defining human as 'walking rational animal' is redundant because 'walking' adds no essential information. Al-'Attar adds that the inclusion of the accidental general in incomplete descriptions (rusum naqisa) is permissible because such definitions aim for partial conceptualization, but even then, when combined with a differentia or specific property, it remains unnecessary. Al-Sayyid corrects that a compound of accidental general and specific property constitutes an incomplete description, but it is stronger than the specific property alone. This discussion guards against the misunderstanding that any attribute can be included in a definition. In the Islamic sciences, for example, defining 'salah' as 'a worship consisting of specific actions and sayings' would not include 'intentional' as an accidental general if it is already implied by the specific property.

الفصل (al-fasl)
التمييز التام (tamyiz tamm)
الذاتيات (dhatiyyat)

The accidental general is excluded from definitions because it cannot achieve complete distinction or reveal essential attributes; any contribution it might make is already covered by the differentia or specific property.

Dispute on Equality in Definition: Muta'akhkhirun vs Mutaqaddimun
Discusses the views of early and late scholars on equality in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the later (muta'akhkhirun) and earlier (mutaqaddimun) positions on equality in definition and identify which definitions (complete/incomplete) each allows.

Core Idea
Equality in definition is contested: later logicians require it for all; earlier allow broader/narrower in incomplete definitions.

In the previous lesson, we learned about complete and incomplete definitions. Now we encounter a fundamental methodological dispute: must a definiens be exactly coextensive with the definiendum? Later logicians (muta'akhkhirun) say yes for all definitions. Earlier logicians (mutaqaddimun) say no for incomplete definitions, allowing broader or narrower terms that still convey some conceptualization. This lesson unpacks both positions and their rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Find the terms 'al-muta'akhkhirun' and 'al-mutaqaddimun' in the Arabic. Note that later logicians are post-Avicennan; earlier include al-Farabi and Avicenna.
2
Extract the condition on definition
What does each group require from a definition? The later require 'musawah' (equality in truth) and 'imtiaz' (distinction from all). The earlier require only some conceptualization, even if not fully distinctive.
The earlier allow distinction from some, not all.
3
Understand the rationale
Later logicians argue that definition must give full conceptualization. Earlier logicians argue by analogy with assent: just as assent can be certain or opinion, conceptualization can be by a broader or narrower face. Al-Dasuqi supports this.
The analogy with tasdiq is key.
4
Apply the positions to definition types
Classify: For later logicians, no definition (tam or naqis) can be broader/narrower. For earlier, only incomplete definitions (naqis) may use broader/narrower terms; complete definitions (tam) must be coextensive.
Incomplete definitions include both hadd naqis and rasm naqis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ واعلَمْ أنَّ المتأخّرين اعتبروا في التعريف أن يفيد تصور المعرَّفِ ، إِمَّا بالكُنه، أو بوجه يميّزه عن جميع ما عداه، فلهذا شرطُوا المساواة بين التَّعريف والمعرَّفِ ، وأخرجُوا الأعم والأخصّ عن صلاحيَّةِ التَّعريف أصلاً ، فالتّعريف سواء كان تاماً أو ناقصاً لم يجز بالأعم والأخص عندهم. وأمَّا المتقدّمونَ فاعتبرُوا التَّصوَّرَ بالكُنْهِ أو بوجه ما ، سواءٌ كانَ معَ التَّصورِ بوجةٍ يميّزه عن جميع ما عداه، أو عن بعض ما عداه، والامتياز عن جميع ما عداه ليس بواجب عندهم فلهذا جوزوا التَّعريف بالأعم والأخصّ، لكن خصَّصوا هذا الجواز بالتّعريف الناقص دونَ التَّام كما قال . الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ: شَرَطُوا الْمُسَاوَاةَ :أي: في الصِّدقِ لا في المعرفة؛ إذْ لا يصح. (قَوْلُهُ: وَأَمَّا الْمُتَقَدِّمُوْنَ؛ فَاعْتَبَرُوْا . . إِلَخ) وأيَّدَهُ بعضُهم بأنَّه لو اشترطَتِ المساواة؛ لكان الفن قاصراً ، فإِنَّهُ كما يكونُ المطلوب مِنَ التَّصديقِ اليقين ومجرَّدَ الجزم والظَّنِّ ؛ فَكَذَا يكونُ المطلوبُ مِنَ التَّصوُّرِ الدُّخول بالوجه الأعم والأخص. (قَوْلُهُ : وَالِامْتِيَازُ عَنْ جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ) أي : فقط ليس بواجب عندَهُم . (قَوْلُهُ : بِالتَّعْرِيْفِ النَّاقِصِ) أي : سواء كان حدًا أو رسماً، وقوله: (دونَ التّمام ؛ أي: سواء كان حدًّا أو رسماً. العطار . رسم ناقص، لكنَّهُ أقوى مِنَ الخاصَّة وحدها، وأنَّ المركَّبَ مِنْهُ وَمِنَ الفصل ناقص لكنَّه أكمل من الفصل وحده ا.هـ. وهو متجه . (قَوْلُهُ: وَأَخْرَجُوْا الأَعَمَّ وَالأَخَصَّ) قالَ السَّيِّدُ : والصَّوابُ أنَّ المعتبر في المعرَّفِ كونُهُ مُوصلاً إلى تصورِ الشَّيء إمَّا بِالكُنهِ أو بوجه ما ؛ سواء كانَ معَ التَّصورِ بالوجه تمييزه عن جميع ما عداه أو عن بعض ما عداه وأمَّا الامتياز عن الكُلِّ ؛ فَلَا يجبُ، وَلَا شَكٌّ أَنَّهُ كَما يكون تصرُّرُ الشَّيء بالكنهِ كَسبيًا محتاجاً إلى معرف؛ كذلك تصوره بوجه ما سواءٌ كان مع امتيازه عن جميع ما عداه أو عن بعضه يكونُ كسبيا، فتصوره بوجهةٍ أعم أو أخصَّ إذا كانَ كَسبيًّا لا يكتسب إلَّا بالأعم أو الأخص ؛ فَهُمَا يصلحان للتّعريف في الجملة ا.هـ
Section: On the Definition and Its Divisions. Know that the later scholars considered in definition that it must convey a conceptualization of the definiendum, either by essence or by a face that distinguishes it from everything else. Hence they stipulated equality between the definition and the definiendum, and they excluded the broader and the narrower from being suitable for definition entirely. So definition, whether complete or incomplete, is not permissible with the broader or narrower according to them. As for the earlier scholars, they considered conceptualization by essence or by some face, whether that conceptualization distinguishes it from everything else or from some other things. Distinction from everything else is not obligatory for them. Therefore they permitted definition with the broader and the narrower, but they restricted this permission to incomplete definition, not complete, as he said. Al-Dasuqi: His statement: 'they stipulated equality' meaning: in truth [sincere application], not in knowledge, for that is not valid. His statement: 'And as for the earlier scholars...' etc. And some supported him [the author] by saying: If equality were stipulated, the art [of logic] would be deficient. For just as the requirement in assent is certainty and mere conviction and opinion, so too the requirement in conceptualization is attainment by the broader or narrower face. His statement: 'and distinction from everything else' means: only, it is not obligatory for them. His statement: 'by incomplete definition' means: whether it is a definition [hadd] or a description [rasm]. And his statement: 'not complete' means: whether it is a definition or a description. Al-'Attar: An incomplete description, but it is stronger than the specific property alone, and the compound of it and the differentia is incomplete but more complete than the differentia alone. End. And it is sound. His statement: 'and they excluded the broader and the narrower' al-Sayyid said: The correct view is that the criterion in a definiens is that it leads to conceptualization of the thing, either by essence or by some face, whether that conceptualization distinguishes it from everything else or from some other things. As for distinction from all, it is not obligatory. There is no doubt that just as conceptualization of a thing by essence is acquired and needs a definiens, similarly its conceptualization by some face, whether it distinguishes it from everything else or from some things, is acquired. So its conceptualization by a broader or narrower face, if it is acquired, is not acquired except by the broader or narrower. Therefore both are suitable for definition in general. End.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage presents the divergence between later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) and earlier scholars (mutaqaddimun) regarding the condition of equality (musawah) in definition. The later scholars require that the definiens be coextensive with the definiendum, providing complete distinction. Thus, they exclude broader or narrower terms from any definition. The earlier scholars, however, accept definitions that give some conceptualization even if not fully distinguishing, allowing broader or narrower terms in incomplete definitions. Al-Dasuqi comments that the equality required by later scholars is in truth (sincere application) not in knowledge (ma'rifa), meaning the definiens must apply to exactly the same things as the definiendum. He supports the earlier view by analogy with assent (tasdiq), where certainty, conviction, and opinion are all valid goals; similarly in conceptualization (tasawwur), different levels of conceptual attainment are acceptable. Al-'Attar adds that a compound of accidental general and specific property constitutes an incomplete description (rasm naqis), stronger than the specific property alone, and a compound with differentia is more complete. Al-Sayyid affirms that any definiens that leads to conceptualization, even if not fully distinctive, is suitable for definition. An example: Defining 'human' as 'animal' (broader) is permissible for early scholars as an incomplete definition, giving some conceptualization. In fiqh, defining 'salah' as 'a form of worship' (broader) could be considered an incomplete definition.

Key Terms
المتأخّرون
المتقدّمون
المساواة
التعريف الناقص

Key Takeaway
The dispute on equality in definition centers on whether incomplete definitions may use broader or narrower terms; later logicians forbid it, earlier logicians permit it for incomplete definitions.

Given the definition 'al-ibadah: al-tadhallul wa al-khudhu' (worship: humbling and submission), identify whether this definition is complete or incomplete, and explain whether the early or late logicians would accept it as a definition.
?
Construct an incomplete definition of 'al-bay' (sale) using a broader term (e.g., 'a type of contract') and explain why an early logician would accept it as a definition while a late logician would not.

Equality or Broader? The Two Schools on Definition Conditions
Author presents the debate between early and later logicians on whether a definiens must be coextensive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the later scholars' requirement of equality and the early scholars' permission of broader/narrower in definitions, and apply the appropriate condition to a definition from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Definitions can be complete (co-extensive) or incomplete (broader/narrower); early scholars permitted the latter, later scholars only the former.

In Islamic logic, a definition (ta'rif) aims to produce conceptualization (tasawwur) of a term. But how precise must it be? Later logicians insisted that the definiens must be exactly equal in scope to the definiendum, while earlier scholars allowed broader or narrower definitions as long as they provide some conceptualization. This lesson unpacks this debate and its implications for fields like fiqh and usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two schools
Note that the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) require equality (musawat) between definiens and definiendum; the early scholars (mutaqaddimun) permit broader/narrower for incomplete definitions. Look for the phrases 'شرطوا المساواة' and 'جوزوا التعريف بالأعم والأخص' in the Arabic.
The later scholars exclude broader/narrower entirely; early scholars only permit them in incomplete definitions.
2
Understand the rationale
The later scholars argue that definition should distinguish the term from everything else; early scholars argue that distinction from some is sufficient for conceptualization. The commentator al-Dasuqi supports the early view with an analogy to assent (tasdiq): just as assent can be certain, conjectural, or merely assertive, so too conceptualization can be achieved through broader or narrower faces.
3
Apply to an Islamic example
Consider a definition of 'qiyas' (analogy). A broader definition: 'extending a ruling from one case to another due to a shared attribute.' This includes both analogy proper and a fortiori arguments. A narrower definition: 'extending a ruling because of a common effective cause ('illah) that is co-extensive.' Which school would accept which? The early school would accept the broader definition as an incomplete definition; the later school would reject it because it lacks equality.
This example mirrors the debate in usul al-fiqh over the definition of qiyas.
4
Check completeness
Determine whether the definition is complete (tamm) or incomplete (naqis). Equality is required for complete definitions even by early scholars. A complete definition includes all essential properties (for hadd) or the equal property (for rasm). The passage notes that incomplete definitions may be broader or narrower.
The commentator al-Jalal clarifies that equality is only stipulated in the complete definition.

Chapter: On definition and its divisions. Know that the later scholars considered in definition that it should convey a conceptualization of the definiendum, either by essence or by a feature that distinguishes it from everything else. Thus they stipulated equality between the definition and the definiendum, and excluded the broader and the narrower from being suitable as definitions entirely. So definition, whether complete or incomplete, is not permissible with the broader or narrower according to them. As for the early scholars, they considered conceptualization by essence or by some feature, whether that conceptualization distinguishes it from everything else or from some of what is other than it. Distinction from everything else is not necessary according to them, so they permitted definition with the broader and the narrower, but they restricted this permission to incomplete definition, not complete, as stated. Al-Dasuqi: (His statement: they stipulated equality) i.e., in truth (sidq), not in knowledge; for that is invalid. (His statement: As for the early scholars, they considered ... etc.) Some supported him by saying that if equality were stipulated, the discipline would be deficient; for just as the desired from assent is certainty and mere conviction and opinion, so too the desired from conceptualization is entry by the broader or narrower face. (His statement: Distinction from everything else) i.e., only, is not necessary according to them. (His statement: By incomplete definition) i.e., whether it is a definition (hadd) or a description (rasm), and his statement: (not complete) i.e., whether it is a definition or description. Al-'Attar: An incomplete description, but it is stronger than the property alone, and the compound of it and the differentia is incomplete but more complete than the differentia alone. End quote. And it is sound. (His statement: And they excluded the broader and the narrower) al-Sayyid said: The correct view is that what is considered in the definiens is that it leads to the conceptualization of the thing, either by essence or by some feature, whether that conceptualization distinguishes it from everything else or from some of what is other than it. As for distinction from all, it is not obligatory. There is no doubt that just as conceptualization of a thing by essence is acquired and in need of a definition, so too its conceptualization by some feature, whether with distinction from everything else or from some of it, is acquired. So its conceptualization by a broader or narrower face, if acquired, is not acquired except by the broader or narrower; so both are suitable for definition in general. End quote. And it has been permitted in incomplete definition that it be broader than the definiendum. This refers to the doctrine of the early scholars, and it is the correct view according to the investigators. Al-Dasuqi: (His statement: And it has been permitted ... etc.) This corresponds to his statement: (So it is not valid with the broader and narrower). So it is more appropriate to mention it after that, before his statement: And definition by the proximate differentia ... etc., due to its connection. It should be said: Since knowledge of this corresponding point depends on knowledge of the incomplete, because of al-'Attar's statement: (His statement: And it has been permitted ... etc.) He indicated with the word 'qad' and the passive construction the weakness of the permissibility. (His statement: And it is the correct view according to the investigators) al-Jalal said: The stipulation of equality in the absolute definition is not the doctrine of the investigators. They said: The purpose of definition is depiction; whether it is by a face that is equal, broader, or narrower. And the discipline has a role in all of it, so there is no justification for not considering them. Yes, equality is stipulated in the complete definition... End quote. That is, equality is a condition in the complete definition, whether it is a definition or a description. As for the first, because it requires mentioning all the essential properties; as for the second, because it requires mentioning the necessary equal property, so they are equal to the defined/described, whether they are real or nominal. The author said in Sharh al-Risala: Just as among assent there is demonstrative, rhetorical, and others, and what leads to assent includes their methods, so too among conceptualization there is the real that distinguishes from everything else and what is broader than that. So what leads to conceptualization—namely, the explicatory statement—must include the method of leading to all types of conceptualization. And when they restricted it to the first two, they must specify in the chapters of logic what leads to the third. Then the Shaykh and many of the investigators explicitly stated that incomplete descriptions may be broader than the essence, and language dictionaries are filled with nominal definitions that are broader. End quote. Abu al-Fath discussed it by saying that this is only complete if it is established that conceptualization by the broader or narrower absolutely or in some respect may be theoretical and in need of a definition, but that is neither clear nor clarifying, because it is possible that all of that is necessary. And if generalization is used in it, the proof for generalization is not complete.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of two schools of thought regarding the conditions for a valid definition (ta'rif). It begins by stating the view of the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) who require that a definition must convey a conceptualization (tasawwur) of the definiendum either by its essence (kunnh) or by a distinctive feature that distinguishes it from everything else. Consequently, they insist on equality (musawat) between the definiens and definiendum in terms of scope, rejecting broader (a'am) or narrower (akhass) terms as suitable for definition, whether the definition is complete (tamm) or incomplete (naqis). The early scholars (mutaqaddimun), on the other hand, are presented as requiring only conceptualization by essence or by some feature, without the need for distinction from all other things—distinction from some is sufficient. Thus they permit the use of broader or narrower terms, but only in incomplete definitions, not complete ones. The commentary by al-Dasuqi clarifies that 'equality' here refers to truth (sidq), not knowledge, and that the early scholars' view is supported by an analogy with assent (tasdiq): just as assent can be certain, merely assertive, or conjectural, so too conceptualization can be achieved through broader or narrower faces. Al-'Attar then discusses incomplete description (rasm naqis), noting that it is stronger than the property (khassa) alone, and a compound of it with the differentia (fasl) is more complete. Al-Sayyid is quoted to affirm that the correct criterion is whether the definiens leads to conceptualization, regardless of whether it distinguishes from all or some. The text then states that incomplete definitions may indeed be broader, and this is the correct view among investigators. Al-Dasuqi notes the weak construction ('ujiza' in passive) indicating the weakness of the permissive view, but then cites al-Jalal and the author of Sharh al-Risala to argue that equality is only required for complete definitions (whether real or nominal), while incomplete definitions (like those in language dictionaries) are often broader. The passage concludes with a critique by Abu al-Fath, who questions whether conceptualization through broader or narrower terms is always theoretical—it might be necessary (daruri)—and thus the proof for generalization is incomplete.

Checkpoint
According to the early scholars (mutaqaddimun), what is the fundamental condition for a definition to be valid?
A) It must be equal in scope to the definiendum.
B) It must distinguish the definiendum from everything else.
C) It must convey a conceptualization (tasawwur) of the definiendum.
D) It must be a complete definition (ta'rif tamm).

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of broader or narrower definitions depends on whether the definition is complete or incomplete, and on which school one follows; early scholars prioritize conceptualization over strict co-extension.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the following definition from a usul al-fiqh text: 'Al-ijma' (consensus) is the agreement of the mujtahids of the Muslim community after the death of the Prophet on a ruling.' Is this definition equal, broader, or narrower than the definiendum? Which school would accept it and why? Use the criteria from this lesson.
