Why Incomplete Definitions Can Be Broader or Narrower
Al-Dasuqi discusses the permissibility of broader definitions in incomplete definitions and addresses objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why incomplete definitions (hadd naqis and rasm naqis) may be broader or narrower than the definiendum, and distinguish this from complete definitions.

Core Idea
Incomplete definitions aim at conceptualization, not precise delimitation, so they can be broader or narrower.

In logic, complete definitions must exactly match the defined thing. But sometimes we only need a rough idea. This lesson explores how incomplete definitions can be broader or narrower, and why this is acceptable according to the verifying scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the distinction between complete and incomplete definitions
Recall that a complete definition (hadd tam or rasm tam) requires the definiens to be exactly equal (musawi) in extension to the definiendum. Incomplete definitions (hadd naqis or rasm naqis) lack this condition.
Passage: 'Yes, equality is stipulated in the complete definiens.'
2
Understand the purpose of incomplete definitions
The goal of any definition is conceptualization (tasawwur). The verifying scholars say: 'The purpose of definition is conceptualization, whether it is by a way that is equal, broader, or narrower.' This justifies the permissibility of broader or narrower definiens.
Al-Jalal's comment emphasizes this.
3
See how broader/narrower works in practice
An incomplete hadd uses a proximate differentia (e.g., 'animal' for 'man' is broader). An incomplete rasm uses a property (khassa) that may be broader (e.g., 'writer in potentiality' for 'man') or narrower (e.g., 'writer in actuality'). Al-Farabi confirms: limits broader than the name are incomplete; descriptions that are coextensive are complete.
Examples: 'man is a writer' (if potential, broader; if actual, narrower).
4
Apply to an Islamic science example
In usul al-fiqh, when jurists define 'riba' as 'increase', this incomplete description is broader than prohibited transactions; it helps conceptualize but is not a complete legal definition. Recognizing this prevents demanding exact equality where not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدْ أُجِيْزَ فِي التَّعريفِ النَّاقِصِ أَنْ يَكُونَ أَعَمَّ مِنَ المُعَرَّفِ، وَهَذَا إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى مَذْهَبِ المُتَقَدِّمِينَ، وَهُوَ الصَّوَابُ عِنْدَ المُحَقِّقِينَ. قَالَ الدَّسُوقِيُّ: هَذَا مُقَابِلٌ لِقَوْلِهِ: فَلَا يَصِحُّ بِالأَعَمِّ وَالأَخَصِّ، فَالأَوْلَى أَنْ يَذْكُرَهُ عَقِبَهُ. قَالَ العَطَّارُ: أَشَارَ بِلَفْظِ قَدْ وَبِنَاءِ الفِعْلِ لِلْمَجْهُولِ إِلَى ضَعْفِ المُجَوِّزِ. قَالَ الجَلَالُ: اشْتِرَاطُ المُسَاوَاةِ فِي مُطْلَقِ المُعَرِّفِ لَيْسَ مَذْهَبَ المُحَقِّقِينَ، قَالُوا: المَقْصُودُ مِنَ التَّعْرِيفِ التَّصْوِيرُ؛ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ بِوَجْهٍ مُسَاوٍ أَوْ أَعَمَّ أَوْ أَخَصَّ. نَعَمْ تُشْتَرَطُ فِي المُعَرِّفِ التَّامِّ. قَالَ المُصَنِّفُ فِي شَرْحِ الرِّسَالَةِ: كَمَا أَنَّ مِنَ التَّصْدِيقِ بُرْهَانِيًّا وَخِطَابِيًّا، فَكَذَلِكَ مِنَ التَّصَوُّرِ حَقِيقِيٌّ مُمَيَّزٌ وَأَعَمُّ مِنْ ذَلِكَ، فَالْقَوْلُ الشَّارِحُ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَشْمَلَ طَرِيقَ الإِيصَالِ إِلَى جَمِيعِ أَنْوَاعِ التَّصَوُّرِ. ثُمَّ إِنَّ الشَّيْخَ وَكَثِيرًا مِنَ المُحَقِّقِينَ صَرَّحُوا بِأَنَّ الرُّسُومَ النَّاقِصَةَ يَجُوزُ أَنْ تَكُونَ أَعَمَّ مِنَ المَاهِيَّةِ. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: كَمَا أُجِيزَ فِي التَّعْرِيفِ النَّاقِصِ كَوْنُ المُعَرِّفِ أَعَمَّ؛ كَذَلِكَ أُجِيزَ أَنْ يَكُونَ أَخَصَّ، فَلِمَ تَرَكَهُ المُصَنِّفُ؟ قَالَ الدَّسُوقِيُّ: نَاسَبَ تَقْدِيمُ قَوْلِهِ: وَالتَّعْرِيفُ... إِلَخْ. ثُمَّ إِنَّ مَا ذَكَرَهُ مِنْ تَجْوِيزِ أَعَمِّيَّةِ التَّعْرِيفِ النَّاقِصِ وَأَخَصِّيَّتِهِ مُشْكِلٌ؛ لِأَنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ النَّاقِصَ إِمَّا حَدٌّ أَوْ رَسْمٌ، وَقَدِ اعْتُبِرَ فِي الحَدِّ النَّاقِصِ الفَصْلُ القَرِيبُ، وَفِي الرَّسْمِ النَّاقِصِ الخَاصَّةُ، وَلَا مُنَافَاةَ بَيْنَ الأَعَمِّيَّةِ وَالأَخَصِّيَّةِ مَعَ وُجُودِهِمَا. وَقَدْ يُجَابُ: بِأَنَّ الخَاصَّةَ تَارَةً تَكُونُ شَامِلَةً وَتَارَةً غَيْرَ شَامِلَةٍ، فَالْكَاتِبُ وَالضَّاحِكُ بِالقُوَّةِ شَامِلَةٌ، وَبِالفِعْلِ غَيْرُ شَامِلَةٍ، فَإِذَا عُرِّفَ الإِنْسَانُ بِالْكَاتِبِ أَوِ الضَّاحِكِ. قَالَ أَبُو نَصْرٍ الفَارَابِيُّ فِي المَدْخَلِ الأَوْسَطِ: وَمَا كَانَ مِنَ الحُدُودِ أَعَمَّ مِنَ الِاسْمِ المَحْدُودِ؛ كَانَ ذَلِكَ حَدًّا نَاقِصًا، وَمَا كَانَ مِنَ الرُّسُومِ يُفْهَمُ بِنَحْوٍ يَخُصُّ الشَّيْءَ وَيُسَاوِي المَفْهُومَ عَنِ اسْمِهِ، فَهُوَ رَسْمٌ تَامٌّ.
It has been permitted in the incomplete definition that it be broader than the defined thing. This indicates the doctrine of the earlier scholars, and it is the correct view according to the verifying scholars. Al-Dasuqi said: This is contrasted with his statement: 'It is not valid with the broader and the narrower', so it would be better to mention it right after that. Al-Attar said: He indicated by the word 'qad' and the passive construction the weakness of the one who permits it. Al-Jalal said: Stipulating equality in the absolute definiens is not the doctrine of the verifying scholars. They said: The purpose of definition is conceptualization, whether it is by a way that is equal, broader, or narrower. Yes, equality is stipulated in the complete definiens. The author said in the commentary on the Risala: Just as among assents there are demonstrative and rhetorical, so among conceptions there are genuine and distinct and broader than that; so the explicative statement must encompass the method of conveying all types of conception. Then the Shaykh and many of the verifying scholars explicitly stated that incomplete descriptions (rusum naqisa) may be broader than the quiddity. If it is said: Just as it has been permitted in the incomplete definition that the definiens be broader, similarly it has been permitted that it be narrower, so why did the author omit it? Al-Dasuqi said: It was appropriate to advance his statement 'And the definition...' etc. Then what he mentioned of permitting the broader and the narrower of the incomplete definition is problematic, because the incomplete definition is either a limit (hadd) or a description (rasm), and in the incomplete limit the proximate differentia is considered, and in the incomplete description the property (khassa) is considered; there is no incompatibility between the broader and the narrower when both exist. And it may be answered: The property is sometimes comprehensive and sometimes non-comprehensive; for example, 'writer' and 'laughing' in potentiality are comprehensive, but in actuality are non-comprehensive, so if man is defined as 'writer' or 'laughing'... Abu Nasr al-Farabi said in al-Madkhal al-Awsat: 'Whatever among the limits is broader than the name limited, that is an incomplete limit; and whatever among the descriptions is understood in a way that particularizes the thing and equals the understanding of its name, that is a complete description.'
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn statement that permits a broader definiens in an incomplete definition. The commentator al-Dasuqi first notes that this ruling contrasts with earlier statements forbidding broader or narrower definiens. Al-Attar observes that the passive construction and the particle 'qad' imply that the permission is weak. Al-Jalal clarifies that the verifiers do not insist on exact equality in all definitions; the goal is merely conceptualization, and broader or narrower definitions can achieve that. However, exact equality remains required in complete definitions (complete hadd or rasm). The author is then quoted to show that just as there are different types of assent (demonstrative, rhetorical), there are different types of conception, and the explicative statement must cover all routes to conception. Many scholars, including the Shaykh, explicitly allow incomplete descriptions (rusum naqisa) to be broader than the quiddity. The objection is then raised: if broader is permitted, why not narrower? Al-Dasuqi replies that the matn implicitly includes both, since an incomplete definition is either a deficient limit (using a proximate differentia) or a deficient description (using a property). These can be broader or narrower depending on the property chosen; for example, defining man as 'writer' or 'laughing in potentiality' is broader, while 'writer in actuality' is narrower. Al-Farabi is cited to support the distinction: limits broader than the name are incomplete; descriptions that are coextensive and particularizing are complete. The passage thus defends the permissibility of broader and narrower definiens in incomplete definitions, aligning with the practical use of definitions in logic and language.

أعم
أخص
مساو
حد

B) Incomplete definitions (hadd naqis or rasm naqis)

D) Only definitions by property (rasm)

Incomplete definitions serve conceptualization and may be broader or narrower; only complete definitions require exact equality.

Hadd and Rasm

Distinguishing Broader and Narrower Definiens in Incomplete Definition
Author addresses objection that if broader is allowed, narrower should also be allowed in incomplete definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether a given incomplete definition uses a broader or narrower definiens and evaluate its admissibility according to early logicians.

Core Idea
Incomplete definitions can be broader or narrower, but each is permissible only in its proper type.

This section tackles an objection: if broader definiens is allowed in incomplete definition, why not narrower? The commentator al-Dasuqi explains that narrower definiens is indeed permitted in incomplete descriptions (rasm nāqiṣ) when the special property is taken actually. Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to evaluate definitions in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The passage begins with a question: if a broader definiens is allowed in incomplete definition, then a narrower definiens should also be allowed. Why did the author omit it? Recognize that this is a challenge to the consistency of the classification.
2
Examine the response
Al-Dasuqi points out that the special property (khāṣṣa) can be comprehensive (potential) or non-comprehensive (actual). When it is actual, the definiens is narrower, and this is permitted in an incomplete description.
Example: 'laugher actually' is narrower than 'man' because not all men are actually laughing.
3
Distinguish hadd nāqiṣ vs rasm nāqiṣ
Incomplete definitions come in two types: incomplete hadd (using only some essential predicates, e.g., genus alone) and incomplete rasm (using a non-essential property). The broader definiens is typical for hadd nāqiṣ, while narrower is for rasm nāqiṣ.
Early logicians allowed both genus alone (broader) and actual special property (narrower) as incomplete definitions.
4
Apply the concept
Given a definition like 'man is a writer actually', determine if it is broader or narrower, and whether it is admissible as an incomplete description. 'Writer actually' is narrower and is an incomplete rasm.
This applies to definitions in fiqh, such as defining 'riba' with a broader or narrower description.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي الْمَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ. فإن قيل : كما أُجيز في التَّعريف الناقص كون المعرّف أعم؛ كذلك أُجيز أنْ يكونَ أخص ، فلِمَ ترَكَه المصنف؟! الدسوقي: المصنّف : (وقد يجوز في الناقص ... إلخ)؛ ناسب تقديم قوله: (والتعريفُ ... إلخ)، ثمَّ إِنَّ مَا ذكرَهُ مِن تجويز أعمّيَّةِ التَّعريف النَّاقص، وأخصيَّتِهِ مُشكل؛ لأنَّ التّعريف الناقص ؛ إما حد أو رسم ، وقد اعتبر في الحد الناقص الفصل القريب، واعتبر في الرَّسم النَّاقص الخاصة، وَلَا تنافي بين الأعميَّةِ والأخصيَّةِ مع وجودِهِمَا. وَقَدْ يُجابُ : بأنَّ الخاصَّةَ؛ تارةً تكون شاملةً، وتارةً غير شاملة، فالكاتب والصَّاحِكُ بالقوَّةِ شاملة، وبالفعل غير شاملة، فإذا عُرِّفَ الإنسانُ بالكاتب أو الصَّاحكِ بالفعل، أو بالجسم الضَّاحكِ بالفعل؛ كان رسماً ناقصاً، وهو تعريف بالأخص ، والمتقدّمونَ المجوّزونَ لِلتَّعريف بالأعم والأخص ؛ يرونَ أنَّ الحدَّ مَا كانَ بالذَّاتِيَّاتِ كُلِّهَا أو بعضها ، فإنْ كانَ بِكُلِّها كَالجنس والفصل القريبَيْنِ؛ فحد تام، وإنْ كانَ بِبَعضِهَا كَالجنس فقط، أو الفصل فقط، أو الفصل مع الجنس البعيد؛ فهو حد ناقص، وحينئذ ؛ فيجوزُ التَّعريفُ عندَهُم بالجنس فقط، وهو أعمُ مِنَ المعرَّفِ، فتأمل.
Section: on the definition and its parts. So if it is said: Just as is allowed in the incomplete definition that the definiens be broader, likewise it is allowed that it be narrower, so why did the author omit it? Al-Dasuqi: The author (says): 'And it may be allowed in the incomplete... etc.'; it is fitting to advance his saying: 'And the definition... etc.' Then indeed what he mentioned of permitting the broaderness of the incomplete definition and its narrowness is problematic; because the incomplete definition is either a definition (hadd) or a description (rasm), and in the incomplete definition the proximate differential is considered, and in the incomplete description the special property is considered, and there is no incompatibility between broaderness and narrowness with their existence. And it may be answered: that the special property is sometimes comprehensive and sometimes non-comprehensive. So 'writer' and 'laugher potentially' are comprehensive, and 'actually' are non-comprehensive. So if man is defined as 'writer' or 'laugher actually' or 'a body that laughs actually', it is an incomplete description, and it is a definition by the narrower. And the earlier scholars who allow definition by the broader and the narrower hold that the definition (hadd) is that which is by all the essential predicates or some of them. If it is by all of them like the proximate genus and differential, it is a complete definition; if it is by some of them like the genus alone, or the differential alone, or the differential with the remote genus, then it is an incomplete definition. And then definition is allowed according to them by the genus alone, which is broader than the defined term. So reflect.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn that discusses the definition and its types. It begins with a section heading 'On the definition and its parts'. Then a question is posed: if a broader definiens is allowed in incomplete definition, why did the author not also allow a narrower definiens? The commentator al-Dasuqi responds. First, he notes that the author's statement about allowing broaderness in incomplete definition is problematic because incomplete definitions are either a definition (hadd) using a proximate differential or a description (rasm) using a special property. Both broader and narrower are not inherently contradictory. Then he provides an answer: the special property can be comprehensive (like 'potential writer') or non-comprehensive (like 'actual writer'). If you define man as 'actual writer', it is a narrower description. The earlier logicians allowed both broader and narrower definitions, because they considered a definition (hadd) to be composed of all or some of the essential predicates. If you use all (genus and proximate differential), it's complete; if you use only some (e.g., genus alone), it's incomplete but permissible. That genus alone is broader than the defined term. So the omission of narrower definition is not a problem; both are allowed in principle.

التعريف الناقص
الأعم والأخص

Key Takeaway
In incomplete definitions, broader definiens (genus alone) and narrower definiens (actual special property) are both permitted, but they belong to different types: incomplete hadd and incomplete rasm respectively.

Three Invalid Types of Definition: al-A'am, al-Akhass, al-Mubayin
Author and commentators on invalid definition types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given term is more general, more specific, or disparate relative to the defined and justify why it cannot serve as a valid definition.

Core Idea
Definitions must be coextensive; thus a'am, akhass, and mubayin all fail.

In this passage, the author and his commentators explain that a definition cannot be broader, narrower, or completely unrelated to the term being defined. Understanding why these three types fail is essential for constructing valid definitions in any Islamic science, from fiqh to kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three invalid types
Look at the author's enumeration: al-a'am (more general), al-akhass (more specific), and al-mubayin (disparate). Note that he omitted mubayin but it is invalid a fortiori.
2
Understand the a fortiori argument for mubayin
Since a'am is closer to the defined but still invalid, mubayin, which is far more remote, is even more clearly invalid. The commentators explain this reasoning.
3
Test with the example 'animal' for 'man'
'Animal' is a'am because it includes horses and other creatures. It is not coextensive with 'man', so it fails as a definition. Similarly, defining 'man' by 'rational' would be akhass if 'rational' only applied to humans? Actually 'rational' is a differentia; the point is coextension.
Distinguish between genus and differentia; here the problem is that a valid definition must be convertible (mutasawi).
4
Distinguish between complete and incomplete definitions
Later scholars forbid a'am and akhass in all definitions. Earlier scholars allow them in incomplete definitions like linguistic definitions. The passage explains this nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي الْمَعْرَفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ
يذكُرُه؛ اعتماداً على فهم المتعلّم واختصاراً في العبارة، وهذا كما قال في تعدادِ مَا لَا يقعُ معرّفاً: فلا يصح بالأعم، والأخص، والمساوي معرفةً، والأخفى»، فَتَرَكَ المباين مع أنَّه لا يقع معرّفاً أيضاً، وإنَّما تركه بناءً على أنَّ التَّعريف لَمَّا لم يجز بالأعم، فالمباين بطريق الأولى؛ لأنَّه في غاية البعد عن المعرّف.
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ: اعْتِمَادَاً عَلَى فَهْمِ الْمُتَعَلِّم) أي: فهمه ذلك من المعلم. (قَوْلُهُ: وَهَذَا) أي: إسقاط الأخص هنا مثل قوله: (في تعدادِ ما لا يقع معرَّفاً)؛ حيثُ أسقط المباينَ لِعِلْمِهِ مِمَّا ذكرَهُ بالأولى.
(قَوْلُهُ: فَلَا يَصُحُ ... إلخ) بدل مِمَّا قالَه ... إلخ.
(قَوْلُهُ: فَتَرَكَ الْمُبَايِنَ) أي: لأنَّه ترك ... إلخ، فهو علَّةٌ لقوله: (وهذا كَمَا قال . . . إلخ). (قَوْلُهُ: فَالْمُبَايِنُ بِطَرِيْقِ ... إِلَخ) قد بحثَ فِيهِ بأَنَّهُ إِنَّما تركَهُ لِخروجِهِ مِنَ اعتبارِ الحمل في المعرَّفِ، ولكنَّهُ يُشكل بذكرِ الأخصٌ مُطلقاً، فإِنَّه لا يحملُ إِلَّا أَنْ يُقالَ: إنَّهُ يُقالُ عليه في الجملة، والحقُّ أنَّ المباين والأخص خرجا بقول المصنف: (مُعرِّفُ الشَّيءِ مَا يُقالُ عليه؛ أي: ما يصحُ حمله عليه، وهَذَانِ لَيْسَا كذلك.
العطار
الحيوانُ؛ فإنَّهُ ينفتُ تَصوُّرُهُ عَن تصورِ الإنسانِ ويوجد بدونِهِ ذهناً، وكذلك يوجد خارجاً في الفرس بدونِ الإنسان.
(قَوْلُهُ: لِأَنَّهُ فِي غَايَةِ الْبُعْدِ) فهو لا يفيد تمييزاً أصلاً بخلافهما، وإن احتمل احتمالاً بعيداً أن يكونَ مُميَّزاً في الجملةِ كَمَا قيلَ: وَبِضِدِّهَا تَتَمَيَّزُ الأَشياءُ»، قالَ السَّيِّدُ: وأبعد منهُ إفادتُهُ تمييزاً تاما بأنْ يكونَ بين المتباينيْنِ خُصوصيَّةٌ تقتضي
والحاصلُ: أَنَّ التَّعريف بالأعم والأخصّ لم يجز عند المتأخّرينَ مُطلقاً، أي: في التّعريف التّامّ والنَّاقص، وعند المتقدمين لم يجز في التّعريفِ التّامّ أيضاً، وأمَّا في الناقص فجائز (كَاللَّفْظِيّ)؛ أي: كالتَّعريف اللفظي، فإنَّه يجوز أيضاً بالأعم والأخص.
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ: كَاللَّفْظِيّ) اعلَمُ أَنَّهُ اختُلِفَ في التَّعريف اللفظي؛ هل هو تعريف حقيقة، وأنَّهُ قسم من أقسام التّعريفِ، أَوْ ليس تعريفاً؟ قالَ الخطَّابِيُّ في حواشي التَّلويح والأكثرون على الفرق بينَ التَّعريف اللفظي والاسميّ، فإنَّهم قالُوا: التّعريفُ قِسمان: تعريف بالحقيقة، وتعريف بحسب اللفظ. اهـ. إذا عَلِمْتَ هذا؛ فقول المصنفِ: كاللفظ؛ الكاف إما للتمثيل أو للتنظير، فإن قلْنَا: إِنَّ التَّعريف اللفظى مِن المعرّفات؛ فتكون للتمثيل، والعكس العكس.
(قَوْلُهُ: فَإِنَّهُ يَجُوْزُ أَيْضَاً بِالْأَعَمّ كما إذا قُلْتَ في تعريفِ العُقارِ: الَّذي هو ماءُ العنب المشكر، وكقولك في تعريف العَشجَد النقد، فهذا تعريف بالأعم، وقوله: ( والأخص) كَمَا إذا قُلْتَ في تعريف المشكرِ عقر، وفي تعريف النقدِ: ذَهَب.
العطار
الانتقال مِن أحدِهِمَا إلى الآخَرِ، قال في شرح المطالع: وأيضاً المباينُ نِسبته إلى المباين الآخَرِ كَنسبتِهِ إلى غيرِهِ، وَكَنسبة المباين الآخَرِ إِليهِ، فَتعريفُهُ إِيَّاهُ دونَ غَيْرِهِ ودونَ العكس تَرجيحُ بِلَا مُرجّح.
(قَوْلُهُ: فَإِنَّهُ يَجُوْزُ أَيْضَاً بِالأَعَمِّ وَالأَخَصّ) وحقه أن يكون بالألفاظ المترادفة: كَمَا يُقالُ: الغَضَنْفِرُ: الأسد، فإنْ لم يوجد ذلكَ ذُكِرَ مُركَّبٌ يُقصد به تعيينُ المعنى، ولا يكونُ التَّفصيل المستفاد مقصوداً، وإلا لَكَانَ تعريفاً اسميًا، ويجري
الشرنوبي
(قَوْلُهُ: الخطابي ... إلخ) ظاهر عبارته أن التعريف الاسمي هو الحقيقي، وهو خلاف المنقول عن المصنف وغيره من أن الحقيقي ما يكون للماهية المحققة كالإنسان، والاسمي ما يكون للماهية التي لم يعلم وجودها كالعنقاء، وكلاهما خلاف اللفظي إذ هو من قبيل التصديق كما قال السيد وغيره وعليه تكون الكاف للتنظير فقط.
Section: On the definition (al-ma'rif) and its divisions. He mentions it, relying on the student's understanding and brevity in expression. This is as he said in enumerating what does not serve as a definition: 'It is not valid by the more general, the more specific, and the equal as a definition, and the more hidden.' So he omitted the disparate (al-mubayin) even though it also does not serve as a definition. He omitted it only because when definition is not permissible by the more general, then the disparate is a fortiori [invalid]; because it is at the utmost distance from the defined. Al-Dasuqi: His statement: 'relying on the student's understanding' means his understanding of that from the teacher. His statement: 'and this' means dropping the more specific here like his statement: 'in enumerating what does not serve as a definition' because he dropped the disparate due to knowing it from what he mentioned a fortiori. His statement: 'So it is not valid... etc.' is a substitution for what he said... etc. His statement: 'So he omitted the disparate' means because he omitted... etc., so it is a cause for his statement: 'and this is as he said... etc.' His statement: 'So the disparate by way of... etc.' has been discussed in it because he omitted it because of its exclusion from the consideration of predication in definition, but it is problematic with mentioning the more specific absolutely, because it is not predicated unless it is said that it is said of it in general, and the truth is that the disparate and the more specific are excluded by the author's statement: 'The definition of a thing is what is said of it... i.e. what can be predicated of it, and these two are not like that.' Al-At'tar: [Example:] Animal; for its conception occurs independently of the conception of man and exists without it mentally, and likewise it exists externally in the horse without man. His statement: 'because it is at the utmost distance' so it does not provide any distinction at all unlike them, even if it possibly remotely might be a distinguisher in general as was said: 'And by their opposites things are distinguished.' Al-Sayyid said: And more remote than it is its providing complete distinction by there being between two disparate things a particularity that necessitates. The summary: That definition by the more general and the more specific is not permissible according to the later scholars absolutely, i.e. in complete and incomplete definition, and according to the earlier scholars it is not permissible in complete definition either, but in incomplete definition it is permissible, like the linguistic definition; i.e. like the linguistic definition, for it is also permissible by the more general and the more specific. Al-Dasuqi: His statement: 'like the linguistic' know that there is disagreement about the linguistic definition: Is it a real definition and a division of the divisions of definition, or is it not a definition? Al-Khattabi said in the footnotes of al-Talwih: And the majority are for the distinction between the linguistic definition and the nominal definition, for they said: Definition is two divisions: definition by reality and definition according to the word. End. If you know this, then the author's statement: 'like the linguistic' – the kaf is either for exemplification or for comparison. If we say that the linguistic definition is among the definitions, then it is for exemplification, and vice versa. His statement: 'for it is also permissible by the more general' as when you say in defining 'uqqar: that which is the intoxicating grape juice, and as your saying in defining 'ashjad: naqd, so this is a definition by the more general, and his statement: 'and the more specific' as when you say in defining the intoxicant: 'uqqar, and in defining naqd: gold. Al-At'tar: The transition from one of them to the other. He said in Sharh al-Matali': And also the disparate, its relation to the other disparate is like its relation to something else, and like the relation of the other disparate to it, so defining it by it to the exclusion of others and to the exclusion of the converse is a preponderance without a preponderator. His statement: 'for it is also permissible by the more general and the more specific' and its right is to be by synonymous terms, as it is said: al-ghadanfar: the lion. If that is not found, a compound is mentioned by which the meaning is intended to be specified, and the detail obtained is not intended, otherwise it would be a nominal definition, and it proceeds. Al-Sharnubi: His statement: 'al-Khattabi... etc.' The apparent meaning of his expression is that the nominal definition is the real one, which contradicts what is transmitted from the author and others that the real definition is for the verified essence like man, and the nominal definition is for the essence whose existence is not known like the phoenix, and both are contrary to the linguistic definition because it is of the type of assent as said by al-Sayyid and others, and accordingly the kaf is only for comparison.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage is a definitional commentary on the section concerning the definition and its invalid varieties. It opens with the author's statement that the student is expected to understand the definition by relying on the teacher's explanation and brevity. The author enumerates what does not serve as a definition: the more general (al-a'am), the more specific (al-akhass), the equal (al-musawi), and the more hidden (al-akhfa). Notably, he omits the disparate (al-mubayin) even though it is also invalid. The reason given is a fortiori: if the more general (which is closer to the defined) is invalid, then the disparate (which is far more remote) is even more clearly invalid. Al-Dasuqi explains that the author relied on the student's understanding and dropped the disparate for that reason. He also notes that the author's definition of a definiens is 'what can be predicated of the defined' — and the disparate and the more specific fail this condition. Al-At'tar provides the example of 'animal' as a general term that exists independently of 'man' both mentally and externally (e.g., in a horse), illustrating why it cannot be a proper definition. The summary states the ruling: later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) forbid definition by the more general or more specific in both complete and incomplete definitions; earlier scholars (mutaqaddimin) forbid it only in complete definitions but allow it in incomplete definitions, specifically the linguistic definition. Al-Dasuqi then discusses disagreement over whether the linguistic definition is a real definition. He quotes al-Khattabi distinguishing between definition by reality and definition by word. The author's phrase 'like the linguistic' is either exemplary or comparative depending on one's view. Examples are given: defining 'uqqar (a type of wine) by the more general 'intoxicating grape juice', and defining the intoxicant (muskir) by the more specific 'uqqar. Al-At'tar adds that the disparate cannot define because it has no special relation to the defined; any attempt to distinguish one disparate from another by it would be arbitrary. Finally, al-Sharnubi clarifies that the nominal definition (definition of an essence whose existence is unknown) differs from the linguistic definition (which is merely explanatory of a word), and the kaf in the text is only for comparison, not exemplification. Throughout, the passage guards against the misunderstanding that any general, specific, or disparate term can serve as a valid definition; only a coextensive predicate that clarifies the essence is acceptable.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the author omit al-mubayin even though it is also invalid?
A) Because it is not a type of definition at all.
B) Because it is a fortiori invalid once al-a'am is invalid.
C) Because it is valid in some contexts.
D) Because the commentator disagreed.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must be coextensive; therefore, terms that are more general, more specific, or completely disparate cannot define.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the term 'salah' in fiqh. Could it be defined as 'acts of worship'? Identify whether this is a'am, akhass, or mubayin relative to 'salah', and explain why it is or is not a valid definition.

Linguistic Definition: Real Definition or Mere Word Explanation?
Commentary on the linguistic definition and its status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between linguistic, nominal, and real definitions and evaluate the scholarly disagreement over whether linguistic definitions count as definitions.

Core Idea
The linguistic definition explains a word, not the essence, and scholars differ on whether it is a true definition.

The passage discusses the linguistic definition (ta'rif lafzi) and the disagreement about its status. Al-Khattabi distinguishes between definition by reality and definition by word. Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating definitions in Islamic texts, especially when a simple explanation of a term is needed.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the three definition types
Real definition (haqiqi) captures the essence. Nominal definition (ismi) defines an essence whose existence is unknown (e.g., 'anqa'). Linguistic definition (lafzi) explains the meaning of a word via synonym or simple description.
2
Analyze al-Khattabi's distinction
He says definition is of two kinds: by reality and by word. The majority hold this view, implying linguistic definition is not a real definition.
3
Interpret the author's phrase 'like the linguistic'
The kaf can be for exemplification (if linguistic definition is a type) or for comparison (if it is not). Commentators debate this.
4
Apply to a fiqh example
Defining 'ghusl' as 'washing the body' is a linguistic definition. It does not capture the essence (niyyah, order, etc.), so it is incomplete.

العطار
الحيوانُ؛ فإنَّهُ ينفتُ تَصوُّرُهُ عَن تصورِ الإنسانِ ويوجد بدونِهِ ذهناً، وكذلك يوجد خارجاً في الفرس بدونِ الإنسان.
(قَوْلُهُ: لِأَنَّهُ فِي غَايَةِ الْبُعْدِ) فهو لا يفيد تمييزاً أصلاً بخلافهما، وإن احتمل احتمالاً بعيداً أن يكونَ مُميَّزاً في الجملةِ كَمَا قيلَ: وَبِضِدِّهَا تَتَمَيَّزُ الأَشياءُ»، قالَ السَّيِّدُ: وأبعد منهُ إفادتُهُ تمييزاً تاما بأنْ يكونَ بين المتباينيْنِ خُصوصيَّةٌ تقتضي

Commentary
This passage is a definitional commentary on the section concerning the definition and its invalid varieties. It opens with the author's statement that the student is expected to understand the definition by relying on the teacher's explanation and brevity. The author enumerates what does not serve as a definition: the more general (al-a'am), the more specific (al-akhass), the equal (al-musawi), and the more hidden (al-akhfa). Notably, he omits the disparate (al-mubayin) even though it is also invalid. The reason given is a fortiori: if the more general (which is closer to the defined) is invalid, then the disparate (which is far more remote) is even more clearly invalid. Al-Dasuqi explains that the author relied on the student's understanding and dropped the disparate for that reason. He also notes that the author's definition of a definiens is 'what can be predicated of the defined' — and the disparate and the more specific fail this condition. Al-At'tar provides the example of 'animal' as a general term that exists independently of 'man' both mentally and externally (e.g., in a horse), illustrating why it cannot be a proper definition. The summary states the ruling: later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) forbid definition by the more general or more specific in both complete and incomplete definitions; earlier scholars (mutaqaddimin) forbid it only in complete definitions but allow it in incomplete definitions, specifically the linguistic definition. Al-Dasuqi then discusses disagreement over whether the linguistic definition is a real definition. He quotes al-Khattabi distinguishing between definition by reality and definition by word. The author's phrase 'like the linguistic' is either exemplary or comparative depending on one's view. Examples are given: defining 'uqqar (a type of wine) by the more general 'intoxicating grape juice', and defining the intoxicant (muskir) by the more specific 'uqqar. Al-At'tar adds that the disparate cannot define because it has no special relation to the defined; any attempt to distinguish one disparate from another by it would be arbitrary. Finally, al-Sharnubi clarifies that the nominal definition (definition of an essence whose existence is unknown) differs from the linguistic definition (which is merely explanatory of a word), and the kaf in the text is only for comparison, not exemplification. Throughout, the passage guards against the misunderstanding that any general, specific, or disparate term can serve as a valid definition; only a coextensive predicate that clarifies the essence is acceptable.

intermediate

Ruling on Definition by the More General and More Specific
Author states the rule on definition by a'mm and akhass

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between complete and incomplete definitions and determine when definition by a more general or more specific term is permitted according to earlier and later scholars.

Core Idea
Definition by the more general is only permissible in incomplete definitions, not in complete ones.

In this passage, the author clarifies a key distinction in definition theory: the conditions under which you may define something by referring to something more general or more specific than it. This distinction depends on whether the definition aims to capture the essence (complete) or merely describe (incomplete), and also on whether you follow the earlier or later scholars. Understanding this rule prevents confusion when constructing definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of definition ruled upon
Find the terms for complete definition (التعريف التام), incomplete definition (التعريف الناقص), and verbal definition (التعريف اللفظي) in the Arabic. Note that the ruling applies separately to each.
The author also mentions verbal definition as an analogy.
2
Map the permissibility across scholars
Later scholars (المتأخرون) forbid definition by a'mm and akhass absolutely, in both complete and incomplete. Earlier scholars (المتقدمون) forbid it only in complete definitions but permit it in incomplete ones.
This difference shows a shift in strictness over time.
3
Interpret the analogy with verbal definition
The author says it is 'like verbal definition' (كاللفظي). Dasuqi explains that the kaaf can be for exemplification (if verbal definition counts as a definition) or for analogy (if it does not). Consider both possibilities.
This preserves consistency regardless of one's position on verbal definition.
4
Apply the rule to an Islamic science example
Suppose you define 'salah' as 'devotional acts' (a more general term). Is that a complete definition? No, it is incomplete. According to earlier scholars it would be permitted, but according to later scholars it is not, because they forbid absolutely. This tests your understanding.
Use this example to see how the rule works in practice.

والحاصلُ : أَنَّ التَّعريف بالأعم والأخصّ لم يجز عند المتأخّرينَ مُطلقاً، أي: في التّعريف التّامّ والنَّاقص، وعند المتقدمين لم يجز في التّعريفِ التّامّ أيضاً، وأمَّا في الناقص فجائز (كَاللَّفْظِيّ)؛ أي: كالتَّعريف اللفظي، فإنَّه يجوز أيضاً بالأعم والأخص.
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : كَاللَّفْظِيّ) اعلَمُ أَنَّهُ اختُلِفَ في التَّعريف اللفظي؛ هل هو تعريف حقيقة، وأنَّهُ قسم من أقسام التّعريفِ، أَوْ ليس تعريفاً؟
قالَ الخطَّابِيُّ (۱) في حواشي التَّلويح والأكثرون على الفرق بينَ التَّعريف اللفظي والاسميّ، فإنَّهم قالُوا : التّعريفُ قِسمان: تعريف بالحقيقة، وتعريف بحسب اللفظ . اهـ . إذا عَلِمْتَ هذا؛ فقول المصنفِ : كاللفظ ؛ الكاف إما للتمثيل أو للتنظير، فإن قلْنَا : إِنَّ التَّعريف اللفظى مِن المعرّفات ؛ فتكون للتمثيل، والعكس العكس.
The conclusion: definition by the more general and the more specific is not permissible according to the later scholars absolutely, i.e., in complete and incomplete definition. According to the earlier scholars, it is not permissible in complete definition either, but in incomplete definition it is permissible, like verbal definition; i.e., like verbal definition, for it is permissible also by the more general and the more specific. Dasuqi (commenting on the word 'like verbal'): Know that there is disagreement concerning verbal definition: is it a real definition and a division of the divisions of definition, or is it not a definition? Al-Khattabi said in the glosses of al-Talwih: The majority distinguish between verbal and nominal definition, for they said: definition is two kinds: definition by reality and definition according to the word. End. When you know this, then the author's statement 'like verbal'—the kaaf is either for exemplification or for analogy. If we say that verbal definition is among the definitions, then it is for exemplification, and the opposite is the opposite.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of defining a thing by referring to something more general (a'mm) or more specific (akhass) than it. The author begins by stating the position of the later scholars (mutakhireen): such definition is absolutely impermissible, whether in a complete definition (ta'rif tam, giving the real essence) or an incomplete definition (ta'rif naqis, a description). The earlier scholars (mutaqaddimeen) also disallow it in complete definitions, but they permit it in incomplete definitions. The author then gives an example: it is like verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi), which also allows definition by the more general or more specific. Dasuqi's commentary clarifies that there is a dispute about whether verbal definition is actually a definition at all. He cites al-Khattabi, who says that most scholars distinguish between verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) and nominal definition (ta'rif ismi), and that definition is of two types: real definition (bi'l-haqiqa) and definition according to the word. Based on this, the kaaf in 'like verbal' can be interpreted either as exemplification (if verbal definition counts as a definition) or as analogy (if it does not). This preserves the logical consistency of the author's statement regardless of one's position on verbal definition.

Key Terms
التعريف بالأعم والأخص (al-ta'rif bi'l-a'mm wa'l-akhass): Definition that identifies a thing by stating something that is more general (a'mm) or more specific (akhass) than the definiendum, e.g., defining 'human' by 'animal' (more general) or 'rational animal' (more specific). [Note: No significant shift; this term is stable across the tradition.]
التعريف التام (al-ta'rif al-tamm): Complete definition that gives the essence (mahiyya) of a thing, typically with genus and differentia.
التعريف الناقص (al-ta'rif al-naqis): Incomplete definition or description (rasm) that does not capture the full essence but provides identifying features.
التعريف اللفظي (al-ta'rif al-lafzi): Verbal definition: explaining an unfamiliar term by substituting a more familiar word or phrase, often synonymous or descriptive. [Note: Some scholars deny that verbal definition is a genuine definition; the author here treats it as a permissible kind of incomplete definition.]

C) It is permissible only if the term is a synonym.
D) It is permissible but only in verbal definitions.

Key Takeaway
Definition by a more general or more specific term is never acceptable for complete definitions; for incomplete definitions, only earlier scholars permit it.

The Scope of Verbal Definition: Beyond Synonyms
Author defines verbal definition and defends its broader scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given definition is verbal (ta'rif lafzi) and classify it as synonym, more general, or more specific.

Core Idea
Verbal definition can use synonyms, more general terms, or more specific terms—not just synonyms.

In this passage, the author defines verbal definition as 'what is intended to explain an unfamiliar term.' Some restrict it to synonyms, but the text argues this is only approximate. Understanding the full scope is crucial for correctly classifying definitions in logic and other Islamic sciences like fiqh and usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Locate the central definition
Find the author's definition of verbal definition in the Arabic: 'هُوَ مَا يُقْصَدُ بِهِ' (it is what is intended by it). Note that it is brief.
2
Identify the objection
Notice the objection: some scholars say verbal definition must be a synonym exchange. They argue a synonym cannot be more general or more specific.
This objection is raised by Dasuqi in the commentary.
3
Examine the response
The author responds that such a restriction is only approximate (taqribi), not real (tahqiqi). Verbal definition can indeed use a'mm (more general) or akhass (more specific).
The response expands the scope of verbal definition.
4
Apply the three types
From Attar's commentary, identify examples: a'mm: 'Sa'dan is a plant'; akhass: 'al-lahw is play (a type of diversion)'; mutaradif: 'ghadanfar is a lion'.
These examples illustrate the three subtypes.

(وَهُوَ ) ؛ أي : التَّعريفُ اللفظي: (مَا يُقْصَدُ به)
الدسوقي
إِنْ قُلْتَ: إِنَّ التَّعريف اللفظي قد عرَّفَهُ بعضُهُم بأنَّهُ تبديل لفظ بلفظ مُرادف له ؛ أشْهَرُ عندَ السَّامع ، والمرادفُ لا يكونُ أعم ولا أخصَّ؛ قُلْتُ : هذا التعريفُ تقريبي لا تحقيقي؛ إذ التعريفُ اللفظي ليس بلازم أن يكون مرادفاً، بل قد يكون أعم وأخصَّ كَمَا عَلِمْتَ .
(قَوْلُهُ: مَا يُقْصَدُ... إلخ) أي : لفظ واضحُ الدَّلالةِ؛ يُقصَدُ بِهِ تَعيين؛ أي: تفسيرُ مَدلولِ اللَّفظ الغير الواضح الدَّلالة على المعنى، وهذا تعريف لنوع مِنَ اللفظي، وهو ما إذا كان بالمرادفِ كَتفسير البرّ بالقمح، والغَضَنْفَرِ بالأسد، والعقار بالخمر، بِهِ إلا أن يُقال: المراد ما يقصد به تفسيرُ مدلول اللفظ ، ولو كان ذلكَ التفسيرُ في الجملة، فيشمل ما إذا كانَ أعم أو أخصَّ . وقوله: (وهو ما يقصد ... إلخ) هذا مُشكل؛ لأنَّهُ لا يُساوي التّعريف اللفظي، بَلْ مُباين له (۱) ، لأَنَّهُ لمْ يُقصدْ بِهِ تفسير المدلول وبيانه ؛ لظهوره عند المخاطب، بل القصد به بيانُ أَنَّ اللَّفظَ مَوضوع لذلك المدلول ، إلا أنْ يتكلف، ويُقالُ : المراد تفسيرُ مدلول اللفظ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ مَدلول اللفظ ، حتَّى يرجع المقصودُ إِلى أَنَّهُ تَفسِيرُ مَدلولِ اللَّفظ
العطار
في الكلماتِ الثَّلاثِ : الاسم والفعل والحرف فَبِالأعمّ كَقولهم: سعدان: نبت، وبالأخصٌ كَقول أهل اللُّغةِ اللَّهرُ : اللَّعِبُ، وهو نوع مِنَ اللَّهو، وبالمرادف : كَالغَضَنْفَرِ الأسد، والعُقار الحمر.
(۱) (قَوْلُهُ : بل مباين له ... إلخ) توضيحه أنهم عرفوا اللفظي بتبديل لفظ كـ: بر بلفظ آخر أشهر منه كقمح، والمصنف عرفه بما يقصد به تفسیر مدلول اللفظ ومدلول اللفظ المحتاج إلى التفسير هو ماهيته المجهولة لدى المخاطب، وتعريف الماهية المجهولة تعريف حقيقي لفظي إذ اللفظي ماهيته معلومة للمخاطب، ولكن يجهل وضع الاسم بإزائها. وحينئذ فقد عرف المصنف اللفظي بما هو تعريف للحقيقي مع ما بينهما من التباين، وقد تكلف المحشي في الإجابة هنا وفيما يأتي له والذي أراه أن في عبارة المصنف قلباً، وأصل العبارة ما يقصد به تفسير اللفظ إزاء مدلوله فحذف إزاء وقدم مدلول على اللفظ وأضيف إليه ولا شكّ أن القلب في مقاصد البلغاء كقول الشاعر :
مهمـــة مــغــبــرة أرجاؤه كأنَّ لون أرضه س .ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي.
Chapter: On the definition and its divisions. (It is), i.e., verbal definition: (what is intended by it). Dasuqi: If you say: Verbal definition has been defined by some of them as exchanging a word with a synonymous word that is more familiar to the listener, and a synonym is not more general or more specific; I say: This definition is approximate, not real, for verbal definition is not necessarily a synonym; rather it may be more general or more specific, as you have learned. (His statement: 'What is intended... etc.') i.e., a clear indication; by it is intended specification, i.e., interpretation of the meaning of the word that is not clear in its indication to the meaning. This is a definition of a type of verbal definition, namely when it is by synonym, like interpreting 'bar' by 'wheat', 'ghadanfar' by 'lion', and 'uqar' by 'wine'. Unless it is said: what is intended is interpretation of the meaning of the word, even if that interpretation is in general, so it includes when it is more general or more specific. And his statement: (it is what is intended... etc.) This is problematic, for it is not equivalent to verbal definition, but rather is different from it, because it is not intended by it to interpret the meaning and clarify it, due to its clarity to the addressee; rather the intention by it is to state that the word is placed for that meaning, unless one strains and says: what is intended is interpretation of the meaning of the word in terms of its being the meaning of the word, so that the purpose reduces to it being an interpretation of the meaning of the word. Attar: In the three word categories: noun, verb, and particle, so by the more general like their statement: Sa'dan is a plant, and by the more specific like the statement of lexicographers: al-lahw is play, and it is a type of diversion, and by synonym like ghadanfar is a lion, and uqar is wine. (1) (His statement: 'Rather different from it... etc.') Clarification: They defined verbal definition as replacing a word like 'bar' with another more famous word like 'wheat', and the author defined it as what is intended by it to interpret the meaning of the word, and the meaning of the word that needs interpretation is its unknown essence to the addressee. Defining an unknown essence is a real verbal definition, for in verbal definition its essence is known to the addressee, but he is ignorant of the name's application to it. Thus the author defined verbal definition as what is a definition of the real definition, despite the difference between them. The commentator strained in the answer here and in what follows; what I see is that there is an inversion (qalb) in the author's phrase; the original phrase is 'what is intended by it to interpret the word in place of its meaning' – he omitted 'place' and brought forward 'meaning' and added it to 'word' – without a doubt inversion is among the aims of eloquence, like the poet's saying: ... al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is a definitional section from the text, formally titled 'Chapter on the Definition and its Divisions.' It specifically defines verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) and then subjects that definition to critical scrutiny. The author states that verbal definition is 'what is intended by it' – presumably an explanation of an unfamiliar term. Dasuqi's commentary immediately raises an objection: some define verbal definition strictly as replacing a word with a synonym more familiar to the listener, which would preclude using more general or more specific terms. The response is that such a definition is only approximate (taqribi), not real (tahqiqi); verbal definition may indeed use a'mm or akhass terms. Dasuqi then explains the author's phrase: it means a clear clear term intended to specify the meaning of an unclear term. This applies to synonym-based definitions like 'bar' explained as 'wheat'. But if we take it more broadly to include any interpretation of meaning, then it covers a'mm and akhass as well. However, a problem arises: the author's definition seems to describe real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) rather than verbal definition, because it aims to explain the meaning of a word whose meaning is unknown – but in verbal definition, the meaning is known, only the name is unknown. The commentator Attar gives examples of verbal definition by a'mm (e.g., 'Sa'dan is a plant'), by akhass (e.g., 'al-lahw is play, a type of diversion'), and by synonym (e.g., 'ghadanfar is a lion'). Finally, al-Sharnubi offers a critical refinement: the author's definition is actually of a real definition, not a verbal one. He suggests that the author's phrase contains an inversion (qalb) – originally it should have been 'what is intended to interpret the word in place of its meaning', but 'meaning' was brought forward. This inversion, he notes, is an eloquent device, like that used in poetry. Thus the passage moves from definition to objection to critical correction, illustrating the careful analytical approach of the logicians in refining definitions.

المترادف
الأعم
الأخص

The Danger of Confusing Verbal and Real Definition
Commentators critique the author's definition as actually defining real definition, then propose a qalb solution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) and real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) and identify when a definition phrase describes the wrong type.

Core Idea
The author's phrasing accidentally defines real definition; al-Sharnubi resolves it by proposing an inversion (qalb).

The commentator al-Sharnubi detects a serious flaw in the author's definition: 'what is intended to interpret the meaning of the word' actually describes a real definition, because it assumes the meaning is unknown. This shows how careful wording is essential in logic. The solution involves recognizing a rhetorical inversion (qalb) that reinterprets the phrase correctly.

Guided Path
1
Recall the author's definition
The author defined verbal definition as 'what is intended to interpret the meaning of the word.' Identify this phrase in the Arabic.
This is the definition being critiqued.
2
Understand the critique
Al-Sharnubi argues: in verbal definition, the meaning (ma'na) is known; the listener only lacks the name. But the author's phrase 'interpret the meaning' suggests the meaning itself is unknown, which is the job of real definition.
Thus the author's definition actually defines real definition.
3
Grasp the distinction
Real definition explains the essence (mahiyya) of a thing; verbal definition explains which name corresponds to a known meaning. In verbal definition, the meaning is already known; in real definition, the meaning is unknown.
This is the key conceptual difference.
4
Examine the proposed solution
Al-Sharnubi suggests an inversion (qalb): the original intended phrase was 'what is intended to interpret the word in place of its meaning' but the author brought 'meaning' forward. This is an eloquent device that reinterprets the definition as verbal.
The qalb saves the definition by reordering the terms.

Chapter: On the definition and its divisions. (It is), i.e., verbal definition: (what is intended by it). Dasuqi: If you say: Verbal definition has been defined by some of them as exchanging a word with a synonymous word that is more familiar to the listener, and a synonym is not more general or more specific; I say: This definition is approximate, not real, for verbal definition is not necessarily a synonym; rather it may be more general or more specific, as you have learned. (His statement: 'What is intended... etc.') i.e., a clear indication; by it is intended specification, i.e., interpretation of the meaning of the word that is not clear in its indication to the meaning. This is a definition of a type of verbal definition, namely when it is by synonym, like interpreting 'bar' by 'wheat', 'ghadanfar' by 'lion', and 'uqar' by 'wine'. Unless it is said: what is intended is interpretation of the meaning of the word, even if that interpretation is in general, so it includes when it is more general or more specific. And his statement: (it is what is intended... etc.) This is problematic, for it is not equivalent to verbal definition, but rather is different from it, because it is not intended by it to interpret the meaning and clarify it, due to its clarity to the addressee; rather the intention by it is to state that the word is placed for that meaning, unless one strains and says: what is intended is interpretation of the meaning of the word in terms of its being the meaning of the word, so that the purpose reduces to it being an interpretation of the meaning of the word. Attar: In the three word categories: noun, verb, and particle, so by the more general like their statement: Sa'dan is a plant, and by the more specific like the statement of lexicographers: al-lahw is play, and it is a type of diversion, and by synonym like ghadanfar is a lion, and uqar is wine. (1) (His statement: 'Rather different from it... etc.') Clarification: They defined verbal definition as replacing a word like 'bar' with another more famous word like 'wheat', and the author defined it as what is intended by it to interpret the meaning of the word, and the meaning of the word that needs interpretation is its unknown essence to the addressee. Defining an unknown essence is a real verbal definition, for in verbal definition its essence is known to the addressee, but he is ignorant of the name's application to it. Thus the author defined verbal definition as what is a definition of the real definition, despite the difference between them. The commentator strained in the answer here and in what follows; what I see is that there is an inversion (qalb) in the author's phrase; the original phrase is 'what is intended by it to interpret the word in place of its meaning' – he omitted 'place' and brought forward 'meaning' and added it to 'word' – without a doubt inversion is among the aims of eloquence, like the poet's saying: ... al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is a definitional section from the text, formally titled 'Chapter on the Definition and its Divisions.' It specifically defines verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) and then subjects that definition to critical scrutiny. The author states that verbal definition is 'what is intended by it' – presumably an explanation of an unfamiliar term. Dasuqi's commentary immediately raises an objection: some define verbal definition strictly as replacing a word with a synonym more familiar to the listener, which would preclude using more general or more specific terms. The response is that such a definition is only approximate (taqribi), not real (tahqiqi); verbal definition may indeed use a'mm or akhass terms. Dasuqi then explains the author's phrase: it means a clear clear term intended to specify the meaning of an unclear term. This applies to synonym-based definitions like 'bar' explained as 'wheat'. But if we take it more broadly to include any interpretation of meaning, then it covers a'mm and akhass as well. However, a problem arises: the author's definition seems to describe real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) rather than verbal definition, because it aims to explain the meaning of a word whose meaning is unknown – but in verbal definition, the meaning is known, only the name is unknown. The commentator Attar gives examples of verbal definition by a'mm (e.g., 'Sa'dan is a plant'), by akhass (e.g., 'al-lahw is play, a type of diversion'), and by synonym (e.g., 'ghadanfar is a lion'). Finally, al-Sharnubi offers a critical refinement: the author's definition is actually of a real definition, not a verbal one. He suggests that the author's phrase contains an inversion (qalb) – originally it should have been 'what is intended to interpret the word in place of its meaning', but 'meaning' was brought forward. This inversion, he notes, is an eloquent device, like that used in poetry. Thus the passage moves from definition to objection to critical correction, illustrating the careful analytical approach of the logicians in refining definitions.

Key Terms

التعريف الحقيقي
القلب
الماهية

Key Takeaway
The author's definition of verbal definition is ambiguous; al-Sharnubi's critique exposes the need to distinguish between defining a name and defining an essence, and his qalb solution preserves the original intent.

The Three Types of Verbal Definition
Author defines verbal definition and its three types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any verbal definition from classical texts as using a broader, narrower, or synonymous term.

Core Idea
Verbal definition explains a word using another word that is broader, narrower, or synonymous.

This passage from Tadhheeb al-Mantiq defines verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi) and clarifies a common misconception: that it must always use synonyms. The author shows that definitions can also use broader or narrower terms, and gives clear examples from Arabic. By mastering this classification, you will be able to analyze how scholars in the Islamic sciences explain unfamiliar words.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined word and the defining word
In the author's examples, locate which word is being defined (e.g., Sa'dan) and which word is used to explain it (e.g., nabt).
The defined word is usually less familiar to the listener; the defining word is more clearly indicative.
2
Check if the defining word is a synonym
If the two words have the same meaning, they are synonyms (muradif). For instance, al-ghadanfar and al-asad both mean 'lion'.
Synonyms are the narrowest type and require no further analysis.
3
Determine if the defining word is broader or narrower
If the defining word includes the meaning of the defined word plus additional meanings, it is broader (a'am). If the defined word is a specific subset of the defining word, then the defining word is narrower (akhass).
Example: 'nabt' (plant) is broader than 'Sa'dan' (a specific plant); 'al-la'ib' (play) is narrower than 'al-lahw' (play/amusement).
4
Classify each example according to the author's enumeration
Review the three categories: by broader term (e.g., Sa'dan: nabt), by narrower term (e.g., al-lahw: al-la'ib), and by synonym (e.g., al-ghadanfar: al-asad). Verify that each example fits only one category.
The author explicitly includes nouns, verbs, and particles in this classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ (وَهُوَ) أي: التَّعريفُ اللفظي: (مَا يُقْصَدُ بِهِ تَفْسِيرُ مَدْلُولِ اللَّفْظِ) أي: لفظ واضح الدلالة يقصد به تعيين مدلول اللفظ الغير الواضح. وهو ما يقصد به تفسير مدلول اللفظ، ولو كان ذلك التفسير في الجملة، فيشمل ما إذا كان أعم أو أخص. إِنْ قُلْتَ: إِنَّ التَّعريف اللفظي قد عرَّفَهُ بعضُهُم بأنَّهُ تبديل لفظ بلفظ مُرادف له أشْهَرُ عندَ السَّامع، والمرادفُ لا يكونُ أعم ولا أخصَّ؛ قُلْتُ: هذا التعريفُ تقريبي لا تحقيقي؛ إذ التعريفُ اللفظي ليس بلازم أن يكون مرادفاً، بل قد يكون أعم وأخصَّ كَمَا عَلِمْتَ. في الكلمات الثلاث: الاسم والفعل والحرف فبالأعم كقولهم: سعدان: نبت، وبالأخص كقول أهل اللغة اللهو: اللعب، وهو نوع من اللهو، وبالمرادف: كالغضنفر الأسد والعقار الخمر.
Section: On Definition and Its Divisions. (It is) i.e., verbal definition: (that by which an explanation of the meaning of a word is intended) i.e., a clearly indicative word intended to specify the meaning of a word that is not clearly indicative. And it is that by which an explanation of the meaning of the word is intended, even if that explanation is in summary, so it includes when it is broader or narrower. If you say: verbal definition has been defined by some as replacing a word with a synonymous word more familiar to the listener, and a synonym is neither broader nor narrower; I say: this definition is approximate not exact; because verbal definition is not necessarily synonym, but may be broader or narrower as you have learned. In the three categories: noun, verb, and particle; by broader like their saying: Sa'dan: a plant; by narrower like the linguists' saying: al-lahw: play, which is a type of lah; and by synonym: like al-ghadanfar: lion, and al-'uqar: wine.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage begins a section on definition (al-marif) and its divisions. The author first defines verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi) as that which is intended to explain the meaning of a word. He clarifies that the word used for explanation is clearly indicative, while the word being defined is not. He then expands the definition to include not only synonyms but also broader and narrower terms. An objection is raised that some limit verbal definition to synonyms only. The author responds that such a definition is only approximate; in reality, verbal definition can be by a broader term (e.g., explaining 'Sa'dan' as 'a plant') or a narrower term (e.g., explaining 'al-lahw' as 'a type of play') or by synonym (e.g., 'ghadanfar' as 'lion'). The author then gives examples for each type, noting that these apply to nouns, verbs, and particles. The core teaching is that verbal definition is flexible and not restricted to synonymy.

المرادف
الأعم

Key Takeaway

Critique of the Author's Definition of Verbal Definition
Commentators critique the author's definition of verbal definition and propose an inversion to correct it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the problem in a given definition and recognize the rhetorical device of inversion (qalb) used to correct it.

Core Idea
A flawed definition can be rescued by identifying a rhetorical inversion.

The commentator points out that the author's definition of verbal definition actually describes real definition. He suggests that the author may have used a rhetorical inversion, which changes the meaning. Understanding this critique helps you spot when a definition does not match its intended category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's definition
Find in the passage how the author defines verbal definition. What does he say it is intended to do?
2
Understand the critique
The commentator argues that this definition applies to real definition because it involves explaining an unknown meaning. Why is that a problem?
3
Learn about inversion (qalb)
The commentator suggests that the author's wording may have been inverted: originally it should have been 'explain the word in exchange for its meaning'. Understand how this changes the meaning.
4
Apply the same analysis
Take another definition you encounter in Islamic logic and check if it might be misaligned with its intended type due to phrasing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ: مَا يُقْصَدُ ... إلخ هذا مُشكل؛ لأنَّهُ لا يُساوي التّعريف اللفظي، بَلْ مُباين له، لأَنَّهُ لمْ يُقصدْ بِهِ تفسير المدلول وبيانه؛ لظهوره عند المخاطب، بل القصد به بيانُ أَنَّ اللَّفظَ مَوضوع لذلك المدلول، إلا أنْ يتكلف، ويُقالُ: المراد تفسيرُ مدلول اللفظ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ مَدلول اللفظ، حتَّى يرجع المقصودُ إِلى أَنَّهُ تَفسِيرُ مَدلولِ اللَّفظِ. توضيحه أنهم عرفوا اللفظي بتبديل لفظ كـ: بر بلفظ آخر أشهر منه كقمح، والمصنف عرفه بما يقصد به تفسیر مدلول اللفظ ومدلول اللفظ المحتاج إلى التفسير هو ماهيته المجهولة لدى المخاطب، وتعريف الماهية المجهولة تعريف حقيقي لفظي إذ اللفظي ماهيته معلومة للمخاطب، ولكن يجهل وضع الاسم بإزائها. وحينئذ فقد عرف المصنف اللفظي بما هو تعريف للحقيقي مع ما بينهما من التباين، وقد تكلف المحشي في الإجابة هنا وفيما يأتي له والذي أراه أن في عبارة المصنف قلباً، وأصل العبارة ما يقصد به تفسير اللفظ إزاء مدلوله فحذف إزاء وقدم مدلول على اللفظ وأضيف إليه ولا شكّ أن القلب في مقاصد البلغاء. قَوْلُهُ: تَفْسِيرُ مَدْلُولِ اللَّفْظِ ... إلخ فيهِ: أنَّ ذلك صادق على التعريف الحقيقي تحيوان ناطق، فَمَا الفرقُ بينَهُمَا؟ قُلْتُ: الفرقُ أنَّ الحقيقي؛ القصدُ بِهِ تفسير الماهية المجملة، وبيان احتوائها وتحصيل صورتها في ذهن المخاطبِ؛ لا تفسيرُ مدلول لفظ إنسان، وإنْ كانَ بيانُ المدلول حاصلاً مِنَ التَّعريف؛ فهو حاصل غير مقصود، وأنَّ اللَّفظي؛ القصدُ بِهِ بيانُ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ اللَّفظ؛ أي: بيانُ مَدلولِهِ الَّذِي وُضِعَ بإزائِهِ، فَقَولُ المصنّف: (تفسيرُ مَدلولِ اللَّفظ)؛ أي: مِن حيثُ إِنَّه مدلول، فخرج الحقيقي. وإلى هذا أشارَ الشَّارحُ بقولِهِ: (فيفسَّرُ)؛ أي: اللفظ بلفظ . . . إلى آخره. ومُحصِّلُهُ: أَنَّ المقصودَ مِنَ التَّعريف اللفظي تعيينُ مَدلولِ اللَّفظِ مِنْ حِيثُ كونُهُ مدلولاً، بخلاف الحقيقي، فإنَّ المقصود منهُ تَعيين وتفسير الماهية المجملة. قالَ الشَّيخُ الملويُّ: التَّعريف الحقيقي: مَا يُقصد به تعيين الماهية من حيثُ احتواؤها على أجزائه. انتهى. وَلِذَا قالُوا: التّعريفُ اللفظي لا يُفيد تحصيل صورة، وإِنَّما يُفيد تمييز صُورةٍ حاصلة من بين الصُّوَرِ؛ ليعلم أنَّ اللَّفظَ المذكور موضوعٌ بإزاء هذهِ الصُّورة. قَوْلُهُ: بِأَنْ لَا يَكُونَ... إلخ فيه إشارة إلى أنَّ المراد بقوله: تعيين مدلول اللَّفظِ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ مَدلولُ اللَّفظ. قَوْلُهُ: وَالْعُقارُ: الْخَمْرُ المرادُ أنَّ لفظ العقار موضوع للخمر، وأمَّا الَّذِي يُقصدُ بِهِ تحصيلُ مَفهوم الخمرِ مثلاً؛ فهو تعريف اسمي
His saying: 'what is intended... etc.' is problematic because it does not equal verbal definition but rather differs from it, because it is not intended to explain the meaning and make it clear due to its clarity to the addressee; rather, the intention is to show that the word is assigned to that meaning, unless one forces and says: it is intended to explain the meaning of the word insofar as it is a meaning of the word, so that the intended meaning returns to being an explanation of the meaning of the word. Explanation: they defined verbal definition as replacing a word like 'burr' with another more famous like 'qamh', but the author defined it as what is intended to explain the meaning of the word, and the meaning of the word that needs explanation is its unknown essence to the addressee, and defining the unknown essence is a real definition; because in verbal definition the essence is known to the addressee but he does not know the word assigned to it. So the author has defined verbal definition as what is a definition of the real (haqiqi) despite the disparity between them. The commentator (al-muhashi) has strained in answering. What I see is that there is an inversion (qalb) in the author's expression: the original is 'what is intended to explain the word in exchange for its meaning', so he dropped 'in exchange for' and advanced 'meaning' over 'word' and annexed it. Indeed, inversion is among the purposes of eloquence. His saying: 'explanation of the meaning of the word' includes: it applies to real definition like 'animal rational', so what is the difference? I say: the difference is that real definition intends to explain the summarized essence and show its parts and form a picture of it in the mind of the addressee, not to explain the meaning of the word 'human', even if explaining the meaning occurs from the definition; it is incidental not intended. And verbal definition intends to show what the word was coined for; i.e., show its meaning that it was assigned to. So the author's saying 'explanation of the meaning of the word' means insofar as it is a meaning, so real definition is excluded. The commentator (al-sharih) pointed to this by his saying: 'so he explains the word with a word...' etc. Summary: the purpose of verbal definition is to specify the meaning of the word insofar as it is a meaning, contrary to real definition, whose purpose is to specify and explain the summarized essence. Al-Malawi said: Real definition is what is intended to specify the essence in terms of its containment of its parts. End. Therefore they said: verbal definition does not produce a picture but rather distinguishes a picture already present among pictures, so that it is known that the mentioned word is assigned to this picture. His saying: 'by not being... etc.' indicates that what is meant by his saying 'specifying the meaning of the word insofar as it is a meaning of the word.' His saying: 'al-'uqar: al-khamr' means that the word 'al-'uqar' is assigned to wine. As for that which is intended to obtain the concept of wine for example, it is a nominal definition.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) by the commentator on the author's definition of verbal definition. The commentator argues that the author's definition actually describes real definition (haqiqi) because it talks about explaining the meaning of the word, which for verbal definition is problematic: verbal definition does not explain an unknown meaning (that's for real definition), but rather clarifies the word's assignment to a known meaning. The commentator suggests there may be an inversion (qalb) in the text. He then explains the distinction: real definition aims to form a mental picture of the essence (e.g., defining 'human' as 'animal rational'), while verbal definition merely indicates the word's assignment to a concept already known (e.g., 'al-'uqar' means wine). Thus, verbal definition does not give new knowledge of the essence but only connects the word to the meaning. This distinction is crucial for understanding the function of definitions in logic. The commentator also cites al-Malawi to reinforce the point.

التعريف الحقيقي
التعريف اللفظي

Key Takeaway
A definition can be misclassified if its phrasing does not match its intended purpose; rhetorical inversion can sometimes correct such errors.

Distinguishing Verbal and Real Definitions
Commentators clarify the distinction between verbal and real definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) and real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) based on their purpose and what they explain.

Core Idea
Verbal definition tells you what a word refers to; real definition tells you what a thing is.

Having critiqued the author's definition, the commentator clarifies the precise distinction between the two types. Real definition aims to give a mental picture of the essence, while verbal definition only links a word to an already known concept. This distinction is crucial for understanding definitions in logic.

Guided Path
1
Recall the two types
Verbal definition and real definition are two distinct types. Verbal definition explains the meaning of a word, while real definition explains the essence of a thing.
2
Identify the purpose of each
Real definition intends to form a picture of the essence in the mind; verbal definition intends to specify which word is assigned to an already known meaning.
3
Understand why verbal definition does not give new knowledge
Since the meaning is already known, verbal definition only distinguishes that meaning from others by attaching a word to it.
4
Apply: classify a definition
Given a definition, determine whether it is verbal or real based on whether it aims to explain the essence or just the word.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ: مَا يُقْصَدُ ... إلخ هذا مُشكل؛ لأنَّهُ لا يُساوي التّعريف اللفظي، بَلْ مُباين له، لأَنَّهُ لمْ يُقصدْ بِهِ تفسير المدلول وبيانه؛ لظهوره عند المخاطب، بل القصد به بيانُ أَنَّ اللَّفظَ مَوضوع لذلك المدلول، إلا أنْ يتكلف، ويُقالُ: المراد تفسيرُ مدلول اللفظ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ مَدلول اللفظ، حتَّى يرجع المقصودُ إِلى أَنَّهُ تَفسِيرُ مَدلولِ اللَّفظِ. توضيحه أنهم عرفوا اللفظي بتبديل لفظ كـ: بر بلفظ آخر أشهر منه كقمح، والمصنف عرفه بما يقصد به تفسیر مدلول اللفظ ومدلول اللفظ المحتاج إلى التفسير هو ماهيته المجهولة لدى المخاطب، وتعريف الماهية المجهولة تعريف حقيقي لفظي إذ اللفظي ماهيته معلومة للمخاطب، ولكن يجهل وضع الاسم بإزائها. وحينئذ فقد عرف المصنف اللفظي بما هو تعريف للحقيقي مع ما بينهما من التباين، وقد تكلف المحشي في الإجابة هنا وفيما يأتي له والذي أراه أن في عبارة المصنف قلباً، وأصل العبارة ما يقصد به تفسير اللفظ إزاء مدلوله فحذف إزاء وقدم مدلول على اللفظ وأضيف إليه ولا شكّ أن القلب في مقاصد البلغاء. قَوْلُهُ: تَفْسِيرُ مَدْلُولِ اللَّفْظِ ... إلخ فيهِ: أنَّ ذلك صادق على التعريف الحقيقي تحيوان ناطق، فَمَا الفرقُ بينَهُمَا؟ قُلْتُ: الفرقُ أنَّ الحقيقي؛ القصدُ بِهِ تفسير الماهية المجملة، وبيان احتوائها وتحصيل صورتها في ذهن المخاطبِ؛ لا تفسيرُ مدلول لفظ إنسان، وإنْ كانَ بيانُ المدلول حاصلاً مِنَ التَّعريف؛ فهو حاصل غير مقصود، وأنَّ اللَّفظي؛ القصدُ بِهِ بيانُ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ اللَّفظ؛ أي: بيانُ مَدلولِهِ الَّذِي وُضِعَ بإزائِهِ، فَقَولُ المصنّف: (تفسيرُ مَدلولِ اللَّفظ)؛ أي: مِن حيثُ إِنَّه مدلول، فخرج الحقيقي. وإلى هذا أشارَ الشَّارحُ بقولِهِ: (فيفسَّرُ)؛ أي: اللفظ بلفظ . . . إلى آخره. ومُحصِّلُهُ: أَنَّ المقصودَ مِنَ التَّعريف اللفظي تعيينُ مَدلولِ اللَّفظِ مِنْ حِيثُ كونُهُ مدلولاً، بخلاف الحقيقي، فإنَّ المقصود منهُ تَعيين وتفسير الماهية المجملة. قالَ الشَّيخُ الملويُّ: التَّعريف الحقيقي: مَا يُقصد به تعيين الماهية من حيثُ احتواؤها على أجزائه. انتهى. وَلِذَا قالُوا: التّعريفُ اللفظي لا يُفيد تحصيل صورة، وإِنَّما يُفيد تمييز صُورةٍ حاصلة من بين الصُّوَرِ؛ ليعلم أنَّ اللَّفظَ المذكور موضوعٌ بإزاء هذهِ الصُّورة. قَوْلُهُ: بِأَنْ لَا يَكُونَ... إلخ فيه إشارة إلى أنَّ المراد بقوله: تعيين مدلول اللَّفظِ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ مَدلولُ اللَّفظ. قَوْلُهُ: وَالْعُقارُ: الْخَمْرُ المرادُ أنَّ لفظ العقار موضوع للخمر، وأمَّا الَّذِي يُقصدُ بِهِ تحصيلُ مَفهوم الخمرِ مثلاً؛ فهو تعريف اسمي
His saying: 'what is intended... etc.' is problematic because it does not equal verbal definition but rather differs from it, because it is not intended to explain the meaning and make it clear due to its clarity to the addressee; rather, the intention is to show that the word is assigned to that meaning, unless one forces and says: it is intended to explain the meaning of the word insofar as it is a meaning of the word, so that the intended meaning returns to being an explanation of the meaning of the word. Explanation: they defined verbal definition as replacing a word like 'burr' with another more famous like 'qamh', but the author defined it as what is intended to explain the meaning of the word, and the meaning of the word that needs explanation is its unknown essence to the addressee, and defining the unknown essence is a real definition; because in verbal definition the essence is known to the addressee but he does not know the word assigned to it. So the author has defined verbal definition as what is a definition of the real (haqiqi) despite the disparity between them. The commentator (al-muhashi) has strained in answering. What I see is that there is an inversion (qalb) in the author's expression: the original is 'what is intended to explain the word in exchange for its meaning', so he dropped 'in exchange for' and advanced 'meaning' over 'word' and annexed it. Indeed, inversion is among the purposes of eloquence. His saying: 'explanation of the meaning of the word' includes: it applies to real definition like 'animal rational', so what is the difference? I say: the difference is that real definition intends to explain the summarized essence and show its parts and form a picture of it in the mind of the addressee, not to explain the meaning of the word 'human', even if explaining the meaning occurs from the definition; it is incidental not intended. And verbal definition intends to show what the word was coined for; i.e., show its meaning that it was assigned to. So the author's saying 'explanation of the meaning of the word' means insofar as it is a meaning, so real definition is excluded. The commentator (al-sharih) pointed to this by his saying: 'so he explains the word with a word...' etc. Summary: the purpose of verbal definition is to specify the meaning of the word insofar as it is a meaning, contrary to real definition, whose purpose is to specify and explain the summarized essence. Al-Malawi said: Real definition is what is intended to specify the essence in terms of its containment of its parts. End. Therefore they said: verbal definition does not produce a picture but rather distinguishes a picture already present among pictures, so that it is known that the mentioned word is assigned to this picture. His saying: 'by not being... etc.' indicates that what is meant by his saying 'specifying the meaning of the word insofar as it is a meaning of the word.' His saying: 'al-'uqar: al-khamr' means that the word 'al-'uqar' is assigned to wine. As for that which is intended to obtain the concept of wine for example, it is a nominal definition.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) by the commentator on the author's definition of verbal definition. The commentator argues that the author's definition actually describes real definition (haqiqi) because it talks about explaining the meaning of the word, which for verbal definition is problematic: verbal definition does not explain an unknown meaning (that's for real definition), but rather clarifies the word's assignment to a known meaning. The commentator suggests there may be an inversion (qalb) in the text. He then explains the distinction: real definition aims to form a mental picture of the essence (e.g., defining 'human' as 'animal rational'), while verbal definition merely indicates the word's assignment to a concept already known (e.g., 'al-'uqar' means wine). Thus, verbal definition does not give new knowledge of the essence but only connects the word to the meaning. This distinction is crucial for understanding the function of definitions in logic. The commentator also cites al-Malawi to reinforce the point.

Key Terms
التعريف الحقيقي
التعريف اللفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what is the main purpose of a real definition?
A) To explain the meaning of a word.
B) To specify the essence of a thing by its parts.
C) To provide a synonym.
D) To distinguish a known picture.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between verbal and real definition lies in whether the definition aims to explain the word's meaning (verbal) or the thing's essence (real).
