Distinction Between Verbal, Real, and Nominal Definitions
Commentary on the distinction between verbal, real, and nominal definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between verbal (lafẓī), real (ḥaqīqī), and nominal (ismī) definitions and determine which category a given definition belongs to.

Core Idea
The purpose of a definition determines whether it is verbal, real, or nominal.

In this lesson, we examine a commentary passage by al-Dasūqī and al-ʿAṭṭār that clarifies the crucial distinction between verbal, real, and nominal definitions. Understanding these categories is essential for evaluating definitions in Islamic sciences, as each type serves a different epistemic function.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of definition
From the passage, extract the three types: verbal (lafẓī), real (ḥaqīqī), and nominal (ismī). Note their Arabic names.
Verbal and nominal are often conflated; this passage carefully separates them.
2
Understand the purpose of each
Verbal definition specifies the referent of a word (e.g., 'al-ghadanfar is the lion'). Real definition explains the essence (e.g., 'man is rational animal'). Nominal definition defines an essence whose existence is not yet known.
Real definitions provide a new conception; verbal definitions only distinguish an already known image.
3
Analyze the examples
The passage gives 'al-ghadanfar is the lion' as verbal, and mentions 'rational animal' as real. Consider why the latter is not verbal: it aims to explain the essence, not just the word.
The same phrase can be used as either type depending on the intention.
4
Note the relationship among types
Nominal definitions can become real once the existence of the defined essence is proven. The commentator cites al-Saʿd's example of defining 'science' at the start of a book (nominal) vs. after studying (real).
This fluidity shows that definition type depends on context and knowledge.

(قَوْلُهُ : تَفْسِيرُ مَدْلُولِ اللَّفْظِ ... إلخ) فيهِ : أنَّ ذلك صادق على التعريف الحقيقي تحيوان ناطق، فَمَا الفرقُ بينَهُمَا ؟ ! قُلْتُ : الفرقُ أنَّ الحقيقي ؛ القصدُ بِهِ تفسير الماهية المجملة، وبيانُ احتوائها وتحصيل صورتها في ذهن المخاطبِ؛ لا تفسيرُ مدلول لفظ إنسان، وإنْ كانَ بيانُ المدلول حاصلاً مِنَ التَّعريف ؛ فهو حاصل غير مقصود، وأنَّ اللَّفظي ؛ القصدُ بِهِ بيانُ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ اللَّفظ ؛ أي: بيانُ مَدلولِهِ الَّذِي وُضِعَ بإزائِهِ، فَقَولُ المصنّف : (تفسيرُ مَدلولِ اللَّفظ)؛ أي: مِن حيثُ إِنَّه مدلول، فخرج الحقيقي. وإلى هذا أشارَ الشَّارحُ بقولِهِ : (فيفسَّرُ ) ؛ أي : اللفظ بلفظ . . . إلى آخره . ومُحصِّلُهُ : أَنَّ المقصودَ مِنَ التَّعريف اللفظي تعيينُ مَدلولِ اللَّفظِ مِنْ حِيثُ كونُهُ مدلولاً، بخلاف الحقيقي، فإنَّ المقصود منهُ تَعيين وتفسير الماهية المجملة . قالَ الشَّيخُ الملويُّ : التَّعريف الحقيقي : مَا يُقصد به تعيين الماهية من حيثُ احتواؤها على أجزائه. وَلِذَا قالُوا : التّعريفُ اللفظي لا يُفيد تحصيل صورة، وإِنَّما يُفيد تمييز صُورةٍ حاصلة من بين الصُّوَرِ ؛ ليعلم أنَّ اللَّفظَ المذكور موضوعٌ بإزاء هذهِ الصُّورة. (قَوْلُهُ : بِأَنْ لَا يَكُونَ... إلخ) فيه إشارة إلى أنَّ المراد بقوله: تعيين مدلول اللَّفظِ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ مَدلولُ اللَّفظ . (قَوْلُهُ : وَالْعُقارُ : الْخَمْرُ) المرادُ أنَّ لفظ العقار موضوع للخمر، وأمَّا الَّذِي يُقصدُ بِهِ تحصيلُ مَفهوم الخمرِ مثلاً ؛ فهو تعريف اسمي. (قَوْلُهُ: وَلَيْسَ هَذَا ) أي : التَّعريفُ اللفظي؛ تعريفاً حقيقيًا يُراد ... إلخ؛ أي: أنَّ التَّعريف الحقيقي يُرادُ بِهِ إفادةُ تصورٍ غير حاصل، والتعريف اللفظي؛ يُراد به تَعيينُ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ اللَّفْظُ مِن بين جميع المعاني الحاصلة عند المخاطب؛ لأجل يُلتفت إليه، ويُعلم أنَّ اللَّفظ موضوعَ بإزائِهِ ، مثلاً إذا قالَ السَّائلُ: ما الإنسان؟ فَقُلْتَ لَهُ : حيوان ناطق، فقد فَسَرْتَ وبيَّنْتَ لَهُ تلكَ الماهية المجملة، وحصلت عنده صورةُ الماهِيَّةِ المفصَّلة، حيثُ بَيَنْتَ لَهُ أجزاءها . (قَوْلُهُ : وَلَيْسَ هَذَا تَعْرِيْفَاً حَقِيقِيًّا بل مالُهُ إلى التّصديق، وهو ما اختارَهُ السَّيِّدُ، في حاشيةِ التَّجريدِ : المقصود منه الإشارة إلى صورة حاصلةٍ وَتَعيينُها مِن بين الصُّوَرِ الحاصلة؛ ليعلم أنَّ اللَّفظَ المذكور موضوعٌ بإزاء الصُّورة المشار إليها ، فَمَالُهُ إلى التصديق، والحكم بأنَّ هذا اللفظ موضوعٌ بإزاء ذلك المعنى ا.هـ. وإليهِ يُشيرُ كلامُ الشَّارح الآتي : وعلى هذا ؛ فقول المصنف : كاللفظي؛ تَنظير، والذي اختاره المصنِّفُ أَنَّ التَّعريف اللفظي مِن قبيل التّعريف الاسمي؛ فَيَكونُ قولُهُ: كَاللفظي؛ تمثيلاً، والفرقُ بينَ التَّعريف الاسمي والتَّعريف الحقيقي؛ أنَّ الحقيقي : هو الذي يكون للماهية المعلومة الوجود، والاسمي : هو الذي يكونُ لِلماهِيَّةِ الَّتي لم يعلم وُجودُهَا ؛ سواء كانت معدومةً أو موجودةً، فإذا أُقِيمَ الدَّليلُ على وجودِهَا ؛ كَانَ التَّعريفُ الاسميُّ بِعَينِهِ تَعريفاً حقيقيًّا، ولذلك قال الشعدُ في شرح المقاصدِ : إِنَّ تعريف العِلْم المذكورِ في مُقدِّمَةِ الشُّروع اسمي، وبعد الإحاطة بمسائل ذلكَ العلم ؛ ينقلب تعريفاً حقيقيًّا، والفرقُ بينَ التَّعريف اللفظي والاسميَّ عَلَى مَا هو مُختارُ السَّيِّدِ وغيرِهِ مِن أَنَّهُمَا مُتَقابلانِ ؛ أنَّ اللفظي لا يفيد تحصيل صورةٍ، وإِنَّما يفيد تمييزَهَا ليعلم أنَّ اللَّفظَ مَوضوع بإزائِهَا ؛ فَمَالُهُ التَّصديقُ كَمَا سمعت، ولا يندرج تحت القولِ الشارح، وأما الاسمي ؛ فهو تعريف بالحقيقة ومُندرج تحت القولِ الشَّارحِ، وأَنَّ الاسميَّ لا يجوز أن يكون بلفظ مرادف ، وأنَّهُ مُختص بالاسم، واللفظي بخلافِهِ فيهما، وأن الاسمي أنسبُ بالمفهومات الاصطلاحية، واللفظى أنسب باللغة.
Interpretation of the signification of the word: that the word is not clear in its indication of the meaning, so it is interpreted by a word clearer in indication of that meaning, like our saying: al-ghadanfar is the lion, and al-ʿuqār is wine. (His saying: Interpretation of the signification of the word ... etc.) There is in it that that applies to the real definition like 'rational animal', so what is the difference between them? I said: The difference is that the real definition intends by it the interpretation of the summarized essence, and clarifying its components and obtaining its image in the mind of the addressee; not the interpretation of the signification of the word 'human', even if the clarification of the signification results from the definition; it is obtained but not intended. And the verbal definition intends by it the clarification of what the word was coined for; i.e., the clarification of its signification which was placed in exchange for it. So the author's saying (interpretation of the signification of the word) means: from the perspective that it is a signification, so the real definition is excluded. And to this the commentator pointed by his saying: (so it is interpreted) i.e., the word by a word ... etc. Its summary: that the purpose of the verbal definition is to specify the signification of the word from the perspective that it is a signification, unlike the real definition, for its purpose is to specify and interpret the summarized essence. Al-Mallawi said: The real definition is what is intended by it to specify the essence from the perspective of its containing its parts. And therefore they said: The verbal definition does not provide obtaining an image, but rather it provides distinguishing an already obtained image from among images; so that it is known that the mentioned word is placed in exchange for this image. (His saying: that it is not ... etc.) In it is an indication that the intended by his saying: specification of the signification of the word from the perspective that it is the signification of the word. (His saying: and al-ʿuqār is wine) The intended is that the word al-ʿuqār is coined for wine. As for that which is intended by it to obtain the concept of wine, for example, it is a nominal definition. (His saying: And this is not) i.e., the verbal definition, a real definition intended ... etc.; i.e., because the real definition is intended by it to provide an unobtained conception, and the verbal definition is intended by it to specify what the word was coined for from among all the meanings present with the addressee; so that he pays attention to it, and knows that the word is placed in exchange for it. For example, if the questioner says: What is man? And you said to him: Rational animal, then you have interpreted and clarified for him that summarized essence, and the detailed image of the essence is obtained for him, since you explained its parts to him. (His saying: And this is not a real definition but tends toward assent, and it is what al-Sayyid chose, in the gloss on al-Tajrīd: Its purpose is to point to an obtained image and specify it from among the obtained images; so that it is known that the mentioned word is placed in exchange for the pointed-to image, so it tends toward assent, and the judgment that this word is placed in exchange for that meaning. End quote. And to this the following speech of the commentator refers: On this, the author's saying 'like the verbal' is an analogy, and what the author chose is that the verbal definition is of the category of nominal definition; so his saying 'like the verbal' is a representation. And the difference between nominal and real definition is that the real definition is for the essence whose existence is known, and the nominal is for the essence whose existence is not known, whether it is non-existent or existent. If evidence is established for its existence, then the nominal definition itself becomes a real definition. Therefore al-Saʿd said in Sharh al-Maqāṣid: The definition of the science mentioned in the introduction of the subject is nominal, and after comprehending the issues of that science, it turns into a real definition. And the difference between verbal and nominal definition according to what al-Sayyid and others chose, that they are opposites, is that the verbal does not provide obtaining an image, but rather provides distinguishing it so that it is known that the word is placed in exchange for it, so it tends toward assent as you heard, and it does not fall under the commentator's statement. As for the nominal, it is a definition by reality and falls under the commentator's statement, and that the nominal may not be with a synonymous word, and that it is specific to nouns, and the verbal differs from it in both, and that the nominal is more suitable for technical concepts, and the verbal is more suitable for language.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharp and hashya) on the distinction between verbal definition (al-taʿrīf al-lafẓī) and real definition (al-taʿrīf al-ḥaqīqī), with additional discussion of nominal definition (al-taʿrīf al-ismī). The passage opens by defining verbal definition: interpreting a word's meaning with a clearer word, like 'al-ghadanfar is the lion' or 'al-ʿuqār is wine'. The commentator (al-Dasūqī) raises an objection: this definition could also apply to real definition, e.g., 'man is a rational animal', so what distinguishes them? The answer is that real definition intends to explain the summarized essence (al-māhiyya al-mujmala) and to obtain its detailed image in the mind; clarifying the word's signification is incidental. Verbal definition, by contrast, intends solely to specify what the word was coined for. The commentator emphasizes that verbal definition does not provide a new conception (taṣawwur); it merely distinguishes an already present image, leading to assent (taṣdīq) about the word's reference. Al-ʿAṭṭār adds that if the purpose is to obtain the concept of wine, that is a nominal definition, not verbal. The passage then elaborates on the difference between nominal and real definitions: real definitions are for essences known to exist; nominal definitions are for essences not yet known to exist, but if existence is proven, the nominal definition becomes real. Finally, the passage contrasts verbal and nominal definitions, noting that verbal definitions tend towards assent and are not restricted to nouns or synonyms, while nominal definitions are by reality and fall under the commentator's general statement. This careful distinction is crucial for understanding how definitions function in logic and epistemology.

Key Terms
التعريف اللفظي
التعريف الحقيقي
التعريف الاسمي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary difference between a real definition (ḥaqīqī) and a verbal definition (lafẓī)?
A) Real definitions use synonyms; verbal definitions do not.
B) Real definitions intend to explain the essence; verbal definitions intend only to specify the word's referent.
C) Verbal definitions provide a new conception; real definitions do not.
D) Real definitions are only for non-existent essences; verbal definitions are for existent ones.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between verbal, real, and nominal definitions hinges on the definer's intention: to specify a word's referent, to explain an essence, or to define an essence whose existence is not yet known.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Verbal vs. Real Definition: Tasawwur vs. Tasdiq
Author distinguishes verbal from real definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a verbal definition from a real definition by analyzing whether the definition conveys a new concept (tasawwur) or simply identifies a word's referent (tasdiq).

Core Idea
Verbal definition gives assent, not concept.

Understanding the difference between verbal and real definition is crucial for any Islamic scholar. When you define a term, are you teaching someone a new concept, or are you just telling them which meaning a word refers to? The classical logicians distinguished these two functions sharply. In this passage, the author and his commentators clarify that verbal definition (التعريف اللفظي) does not produce a new mental image but rather confirms the link between a word and an already known meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the definition
Ask: is the goal to convey a new concept (tasawwur) or to specify which existing meaning a word refers to (tasdiq)? The passage uses the example of 'ghadafar' and 'lion'.
2
Check if the definiendum's meaning is already present
If the meaning is already in the mind, the definition is likely verbal. If it is new, it is real.
3
Determine the outcome
A real definition results in a detailed concept (tasawwur). A verbal definition results in a judgment (tasdiq) about word-meaning correspondence. The commentators stress that the outcome of verbal definition is tasdiq.
4
Classify the definition
Based on the above, classify an example as verbal or real definition.
The passage explicitly distinguishes the two.

فَصْلٌ: فِي الْمَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ
وليس هذا تعريفاً حقيقيًّا يُرادُ بِهِ إفادةُ تصوّرٍ غيرِ حاصل
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ: وَلَيْسَ هَذَا ) أي : التَّعريفُ اللفظي؛ تعريفاً حقيقيًا يُراد ... إلخ؛ أي: أنَّ التَّعريف الحقيقي يُرادُ بِهِ إفادةُ تصورٍ غير حاصل، والتعريف اللفظي؛ يُراد به تَعيينُ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ اللَّفْظُ مِن بين جميع المعاني الحاصلة عند المخاطب؛ لأجل يُلتفت إليه، ويُعلم أنَّ اللَّفظَ موضوعَ بإزائِهِ ، مثلاً إذا قالَ السَّائلُ: ما الإنسان؟ فَقُلْتَ لَهُ : حيوان ناطق، فقد فَسَرْتَ وبيَّنْتَ لَهُ تلكَ الماهية المجملة، وحصلت عنده صورةُ الماهِيَّةِ المفصَّلة، حيثُ بَيَنْتَ لَهُ أجزاءها .
العطار
قال
(قَوْلُهُ : وَلَيْسَ هَذَا تَعْرِيْفَاً حَقِيقِيًّا بل مالُهُ إلى التّصديق، وهو ما اختارَهُ السَّيِّدُ، في حاشيةِ التَّجريدِ : المقصود منه الإشارة إلى صورة حاصلةٍ وَتَعيينُها مِن بين الصُّوَرِ الحاصلة؛ ليعلم أنَّ اللَّفظَ المذكور موضوعٌ بإزاء الصُّورة المشار إليها ، فَمَالُهُ إلى التصديق، والحكم بأنَّ هذا اللفظ موضوعٌ بإزاء ذلك المعنى ا.هـ. وإليهِ يُشيرُ كلامُ الشَّارح الآتي : وعلى هذا ؛ فقول المصنف : كاللفظي؛ تَنظير، والذي اختاره المصنِّفُ أَنَّ التَّعريف اللفظي مِن قبيل التّعريف الاسمي؛ فَيَكونُ قولُهُ: كَاللفظي؛ تمثيلاً، والفرقُ بينَ التَّعريف الاسمي والتَّعريف الحقيقي؛ أنَّ الحقيقي : هو الذي يكون للماهية المعلومة الوجود، والاسمي : هو الذي يكونُ لِلماهِيَّةِ الَّتي لم يعلم وُجودُهَا ؛ سواء كانت معدومةً أو موجودةً، فإذا أُقِيمَ الدَّليلُ على وجودِهَا ؛ كَانَ التَّعريفُ الاسميُّ بِعَينِهِ تَعريفاً حقيقيًّا، ولذلك قال الشعدُ في شرح المقاصدِ : إِنَّ تعريف العِلْم المذكورِ في مُقدِّمَةِ الشُّروع اسمي، وبعد الإحاطة بمسائل ذلكَ العلم ؛ ينقلب تعريفاً حقيقيًّا، والفرقُ بينَ التَّعريف اللفظي والاسميَّ عَلَى مَا هو مُختارُ السَّيِّدِ وغيرِهِ مِن أَنَّهُمَا مُتَقابلانِ ؛ أنَّ اللفظي لا يفيد تحصيل صورةٍ، وإِنَّما يفيد تمييزَهَا ليعلم أنَّ اللَّفظَ مَوضوع بإزائِهَا ؛ فَمَالُهُ التَّصديقُ كَمَا سمعت، ولا يندرج تحت القولِ الشارح، وأما الاسمي ؛ فهو تعريف بالحقيقة ومُندرج تحت القولِ الشَّارحِ، وأَنَّ الاسميَّ لا يجوز أن يكون بلفظ مرادف ، وأنَّهُ مُختص بالاسم، واللفظي بخلافِهِ فيهما، وأن الاسمي أنسبُ بالمفهومات الاصطلاحية، واللفظى أنسب باللغة،
إنَّما المراد تعيين ما وُضِعَ له اللَّفْظُ مِن سائر المعاني؛ ليُلتفت إليه، ويُعلم أنَّه موضوع بإزائه .
الدسوقي
وإذا قالَ السَّائلُ : ما الغَضَنْفَر ؟ ، فَقُلْتَ لهُ : الأسد ؛ فالمخاطب لم يجهل حقيقةً الأسد، بلْ مُتصوِّرٌ لَهَا كَغيرِهَا ، فَلَمْ تُفِدْهُ بِجوابِكَ حصول صورة الأسد في ذهنِهِ؛ لحصولها فيه قبل جوابِكَ له، وإنَّما أفدَّتَهُ أنَّ هذهِ الحقيقة دون غيرها من الحقائقِ الحاصلة عندك؛ مَوضوع بإزائِهَا لفظُ الغَضَنْفَر .
وَلَمَّا كانَ مآلُ هذا التّصديقِ ، وَكَأَنَّكَ قُلْتَ لهُ : الغَضَنْفَرُ موضوع للأسد ؛ قالَ بعضُهم : التَّعريفُ اللفظي ليس تعريفاً أصلاً، فَضْلاً عن كونه ناقصاً . (قَوْلُهُ : إِنَّمَا الْمُرَادُ تَعْيِينُ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ اللَّفْظُ أي : بلفظ أوضح منه؛ مُرادف له، أو أعم منه، أو أخص العطار
.
والمحقِّقُ الدَّوَانيُّ أَيَّدَ مَا ذهب إليه المصنِّفُ بأنَّهُ قد علَّلَ القومُ تقدُّمَ مَطلَبِ مَا الاسمية على جميع المطالب بأنَّهُ : ما لم يفهم معنى اللفظ؛ لم يمكِّن التصديق بوجودِهِ، فَلَا يتمشى طلب حقيقتِهِ وَلَا التَّصديقُ بالهيئة المركَّبةِ، فَإِنَّ ذلكَ الكلامَ إنَّما يتم إذا كانَ التَّعريفُ اللَّفظي داخلاً في مطلب «ما» كما لا يخفى ا.هـ. ويوضحه ما ذكره في الحواشي القديمة على الشارح الجديدِ للتَّجريدِ بأَنَّ لَنَا مَطلَبَيْنِ ؛ مَطلب «ما» ويُطلبُ بِهَا التَّصوُّرُ ، ومَطلب هل) ويُطلَبُ بِهَا التَّصديقُ والتَّصوُّرُ على قِسْمَيْنِ؛ تَصوُّرٌ بحسب الاسم وهو تصوُّرُ الشَّيء باعتبار مفهومه مع قطعِ النَّظرِ عن انطباقِهِ على طبيعة موجودة في الخارج، وهذا التَّصرُّرُ يجري في الموجودات قبل العلم بوجودِهَا، وفي المعدوماتِ أيضاً ، والطَّالبُ له «ما» الشَّارحة للاسم، وثانيهما : تصور بحسب الحقيقةِ ؛ أعني : تصرُّرَ الشَّيءِ الَّذي عُلِمَ وُجودُهُ، وَالطَّالبُ لهذا التَّصورِ مَا الحقيقيَّةُ، وكذلك التصديقُ ينقسم إلى التصديق بوجودِ الشَّيء في نفسه وإلى التصديق بثبوتِهِ لغيرِهِ والطَّالبُ لِلأَوَّلِ : «هَل» البسيطةُ، ولِلثَّاني: «هَل» المركَّبَةُ، ولا شُبهة في أنَّ مَطلَبَ مَا الشَّارحةِ مُقدَّم على هَل البسيطة، فإنَّ الشَّيءَ ما لم يتصوَّرُ مَفهومُهُ لم يمكِّن طلب التصديق بوجودِهِ، كَمَا أَنَّ مَطلَبٌ هَل» البسيطة
Chapter: On Definition and Its Types. And this is not a real definition intended to convey a concept not yet obtained. (al-Dusuqi: His saying: 'And this is not a real definition' means the verbal definition; a real definition intended to convey a concept not yet obtained, while the verbal definition is intended to specify what the word was placed for from among all the meanings present with the addressee, so that it is attended to and it is known that the word is placed for it. For example, if the questioner says: 'What is man?' and you say to him: 'Rational animal,' you have explained and clarified that summary quiddity, and the detailed form of the quiddity occurs to him, since you have explained its parts. (al-Attar: He said: His saying: 'And this is not a real definition' but rather its outcome is assent (tasdiq). This is what al-Sayyid chose in his gloss on al-Tajrid: the purpose is to point to an already present form and specify it among the already present forms, so that it is known that the mentioned word is placed for the indicated form. So its outcome is assent, and the judgment that this word is placed for that meaning. End quote. And the commentator's subsequent words refer to this. According to this, the author's saying 'like the verbal' is an analogy. What the author chose is that verbal definition is of the type of nominal definition; so his saying 'like the verbal' is an example. The difference between nominal definition and real definition is that real definition is for a quiddity whose existence is known, while nominal definition is for a quiddity whose existence is not known, whether it is non-existent or existent. If proof is established for its existence, then the nominal definition itself becomes a real definition. Therefore al-Sa'd said in Sharh al-Maqasid: The definition of knowledge mentioned in the introduction of the book is nominal, and after encompassing the issues of that science, it turns into a real definition. The difference between verbal and nominal definition according to what is chosen by al-Sayyid and others that they are opposed: verbal definition does not produce a form, it only distinguishes it so that it is known that the word is placed for it; so its outcome is assent as you heard, and it is not included under the commentator's statement. As for nominal definition, it is a definition by the reality and is included under the commentator's statement. Also, nominal definition cannot be by a synonym, and it is specific to nouns, while verbal definition is different in both respects; and nominal definition is more appropriate for conventional concepts, while verbal definition is more appropriate for language. The purpose is only to specify what the word is placed for from among the other meanings, so that it is attended to and it is known that it is placed for it. (al-Dusuqi:) And if the questioner says: 'What is ghadafar?' and you say to him: 'Lion,' then the addressee does not ignore the reality of lion, but rather conceives of it like other realities. So you have not conveyed to him with your answer the obtainment of the form of lion in his mind, because it was already present before your answer. Rather, you have conveyed to him that this reality, to the exclusion of other realities present with you, is that for which the word ghadafar is placed. And since the outcome of this is assent, as if you said to him: 'Ghadafar is placed for lion,' some said: The verbal definition is not a definition at all, let alone being incomplete. (His saying: The purpose is only to specify what the word is placed for, i.e., by a clearer word, synonymous with it, or more general, or more specific. al-Attar.) And al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawwani supported what the author went to, that the people have justified the precedence of the request of 'what' (ma) for the name over all other requests, because: as long as the meaning of the word is not understood, it is not possible to assent to its existence, so the request for its reality or the assent to the composite statement cannot proceed. For that statement is only completed if the verbal definition enters into the request of 'what' (ma), as is not hidden. End quote. It is clarified by what was mentioned in the old glosses on the new commentary on al-Tajrid: that we have two requests: the request of 'what' (ma) by which concept (tasawwur) is sought, and the request of 'whether' (hal) by which assent (tasdiq) is sought. And concept is of two types: concept by name, which is the concept of a thing in terms of its meaning, disregarding its application to a nature existing in the external world. This concept applies to existents before knowing their existence, and also to non-existents. The seeker of this is 'what' (ma) that explains the name. The second type is concept by reality, meaning the concept of a thing whose existence has been known. The seeker of this concept is the real 'what' (ma). Likewise, assent is divided into assent to the existence of the thing in itself and assent to its being established for something else. The seeker of the first is the simple 'whether' (hal basita), and the seeker of the second is the compound 'whether' (hal murakkaba). There is no doubt that the request of 'what' (ma) that explains the name precedes the simple 'whether' (hal basita), because as long as the meaning of a thing is not conceived, it is not possible to seek assent to its existence, just as the request of the simple 'whether'
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the nature and types of definition, specifically distinguishing between verbal (lafzhi), real (haqiqi), and nominal (ismi) definitions. The author begins by stating that the verbal definition is not a real definition intended to convey a new concept. Rather, it merely specifies which of the already present meanings in the mind of the addressee corresponds to the word. The commentator al-Dusuqi clarifies: a real definition aims to produce a concept not yet obtained, while a verbal definition aims to identify the referent of the word among known meanings. An example is given: if someone asks 'What is man?' and you answer 'Rational animal,' that is a real definition because it provides the constituent parts of the quiddity. Then al-Attar adds a point: the outcome of verbal definition is assent (tasdiq), not a new concept – it is a judgment that the word is placed for that meaning. He refers to al-Sayyid's view in the gloss on al-Tajrid. The discussion then turns to the distinction between nominal and verbal definitions. The author of the matn considered verbal definition a type of nominal definition. The commentator explains that real definition is for a quiddity whose existence is known; nominal definition is for a quiddity whose existence is not yet known. If proof establishes its existence, the nominal definition becomes real. Al-Sa'd in Sharh al-Maqasid illustrates this: the definition of knowledge at the start of a book is nominal; after studying the subject, it becomes real. Then the difference between verbal and nominal definition is delineated: verbal definition does not provide a new form, only distinguishes an existing form; nominal definition does provide a definition by reality. Also, nominal definition cannot be by a synonym and is limited to nouns, whereas verbal definition can be by a synonym and applies to all parts of speech. Nominal definition is more suited for conventional terms, verbal for linguistic terms. The passage then gives the example of 'ghadafar' (a synonym for lion). If someone asks 'What is ghadafar?' and you say 'Lion,' the addressee already knows the reality of lion; you are only informing him that the word 'ghadafar' refers to that reality. The outcome is a judgment, so some scholars said verbal definition is not a definition at all. Finally, al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawwani supports the author by explaining the priority of the request 'what' (ma) over the request 'whether' (hal) – one must first understand the meaning of a word before seeking assent to its existence or to its attributes. The passage then introduces the classification of requests: 'ma' for concept (tasawwur) and 'hal' for assent (tasdiq). Concept is divided into concept by name (which applies even before knowing existence) and concept by reality (after existence is known). Assent is divided into assent to existence (simple 'hal') and assent to a predicate (compound 'hal'). The request 'ma' that explains the name must precede simple 'hal', because without understanding the concept, one cannot seek existence. The text ends mid-sentence, but the point is clear.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary function of a verbal definition (التعريف اللفظي)?
A) To provide a complete scientific definition of an unknown quiddity.
B) To specify which among existing meanings a word is placed for, resulting in assent (tasdiq).
C) To establish the external existence of the defined thing.
D) To list all possible synonyms of the word.

Key Takeaway
The essential distinction: real definition provides a new concept; verbal definition provides a judgment about word-meaning correspondence.

?

Nominal Definition and the Hierarchy of Requests
Author discusses nominal definition and the priority of requests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate nominal definition from real and verbal definitions, and explain the priority of the 'what' request (ma sharha) over the 'whether' request (hal basita).

Core Idea
Nominal definition becomes real when existence is proven.

Nominal definition (التعريف الاسمي) sits at the boundary between ignorance and knowledge. It defines a thing without presupposing its existence, and can transform into a real definition once existence is established. This passage also explores the logical order of inquiries: one must first understand the meaning of a word (ma sharha) before seeking its existence (hal basita). This hierarchy is foundational for how Islamic scholars structure their arguments in kalam and usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify whether the quiddity's existence is known
Check if the defined thing's external existence is established. If not, the definition is nominal.
The passage says real definition is for a quiddity whose existence is known; nominal for unknown existence.
2
Classify the definition as nominal or real
If existence is unknown, it's nominal; if known, it's real. Note that nominal can become real later.
Example from al-Sa'd: the definition of 'knowledge' in the introduction is nominal, but becomes real after studying the science.
3
Distinguish nominal from verbal definition
Nominal definition provides a definition by reality (includes genus/differentia), while verbal definition only specifies word-meaning. Also, nominal cannot be by a synonym and is restricted to nouns.
The passage contrasts the two on these points.
4
Order the requests (matlab) correctly
Place 'ma sharha' (what does the word mean?) before 'hal basita' (does it exist?). This is because you must understand a concept before seeking its existence.
The passage uses al-Dawwani's argument to justify this priority.

(قَوْلُهُ : وَلَيْسَ هَذَا تَعْرِيْفَاً حَقِيقِيًّا بل مالُهُ إلى التّصديق، وهو ما اختارَهُ السَّيِّدُ، في حاشيةِ التَّجريدِ : المقصود منه الإشارة إلى صورة حاصلةٍ وَتَعيينُها مِن بين الصُّوَرِ الحاصلة؛ ليعلم أنَّ اللَّفظَ المذكور موضوعٌ بإزاء الصُّورة المشار إليها ، فَمَالُهُ إلى التصديق، والحكم بأنَّ هذا اللفظ موضوعٌ بإزاء ذلك المعنى ا.هـ. وإليهِ يُشيرُ كلامُ الشَّارح الآتي : وعلى هذا ؛ فقول المصنف : كاللفظي؛ تَنظير، والذي اختاره المصنِّفُ أَنَّ التَّعريف اللفظي مِن قبيل التّعريف الاسمي؛ فَيَكونُ قولُهُ: كَاللفظي؛ تمثيلاً، والفرقُ بينَ التَّعريف الاسمي والتَّعريف الحقيقي؛ أنَّ الحقيقي : هو الذي يكون للماهية المعلومة الوجود، والاسمي : هو الذي يكونُ لِلماهِيَّةِ الَّتي لم يعلم وُجودُهَا ؛ سواء كانت معدومةً أو موجودةً، فإذا أُقِيمَ الدَّليلُ على وجودِهَا ؛ كَانَ التَّعريفُ الاسميُّ بِعَينِهِ تَعريفاً حقيقيًّا، ولذلك قال الشعدُ في شرح المقاصدِ : إِنَّ تعريف العِلْم المذكورِ في مُقدِّمَةِ الشُّروع اسمي، وبعد الإحاطة بمسائل ذلكَ العلم ؛ ينقلب تعريفاً حقيقيًّا، والفرقُ بينَ التَّعريف اللفظي والاسميَّ عَلَى مَا هو مُختارُ السَّيِّدِ وغيرِهِ مِن أَنَّهُمَا مُتَقابلانِ ؛ أنَّ اللفظي لا يفيد تحصيل صورةٍ، وإِنَّما يفيد تمييزَهَا ليعلم أنَّ اللَّفظَ مَوضوع بإزائِهَا ؛ فَمَالُهُ التَّصديقُ كَمَا سمعت، ولا يندرج تحت القولِ الشارح، وأما الاسمي ؛ فهو تعريف بالحقيقة ومُندرج تحت القولِ الشَّارحِ، وأَنَّ الاسميَّ لا يجوز أن يكون بلفظ مرادف ، وأنَّهُ مُختص بالاسم، واللفظي بخلافِهِ فيهما، وأن الاسمي أنسبُ بالمفهومات الاصطلاحية، واللفظى أنسب باللغة،
إنَّما المراد تعيين ما وُضِعَ له اللَّفْظُ مِن سائر المعاني؛ ليُلتفت إليه، ويُعلم أنَّه موضوع بإزائه .
الدسوقي
وإذا قالَ السَّائلُ : ما الغَضَنْفَر ؟ ، فَقُلْتَ لهُ : الأسد ؛ فالمخاطب لم يجهل حقيقةً الأسد، بلْ مُتصوِّرٌ لَهَا كَغيرِهَا ، فَلَمْ تُفِدْهُ بِجوابِكَ حصول صورة الأسد في ذهنِهِ؛ لحصولها فيه قبل جوابِكَ له، وإنَّما أفدَّتَهُ أنَّ هذهِ الحقيقة دون غيرها من الحقائقِ الحاصلة عندك؛ مَوضوع بإزائِهَا لفظُ الغَضَنْفَر .
وَلَمَّا كانَ مآلُ هذا التّصديقِ ، وَكَأَنَّكَ قُلْتَ لهُ : الغَضَنْفَرُ موضوع للأسد ؛ قالَ بعضُهم : التَّعريفُ اللفظي ليس تعريفاً أصلاً، فَضْلاً عن كونه ناقصاً . (قَوْلُهُ : إِنَّمَا الْمُرَادُ تَعْيِينُ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ اللَّفْظُ أي : بلفظ أوضح منه؛ مُرادف له، أو أعم منه، أو أخص العطار
.
والمحقِّقُ الدَّوَانيُّ أَيَّدَ مَا ذهب إليه المصنِّفُ بأنَّهُ قد علَّلَ القومُ تقدُّمَ مَطلَبِ مَا الاسمية على جميع المطالب بأنَّهُ : ما لم يفهم معنى اللفظ؛ لم يمكِّن التصديق بوجودِهِ، فَلَا يتمشى طلب حقيقتِهِ وَلَا التَّصديقُ بالهيئة المركَّبةِ، فَإِنَّ ذلكَ الكلامَ إنَّما يتم إذا كانَ التَّعريفُ اللَّفظي داخلاً في مطلب «ما» كما لا يخفى ا.هـ. ويوضحه ما ذكره في الحواشي القديمة على الشارح الجديدِ للتَّجريدِ بأَنَّ لَنَا مَطلَبَيْنِ ؛ مَطلب «ما» ويُطلبُ بِهَا التَّصوُّرُ ، ومَطلب هل) ويُطلَبُ بِهَا التَّصديقُ والتَّصوُّرُ على قِسْمَيْنِ؛ تَصوُّرٌ بحسب الاسم وهو تصوُّرُ الشَّيء باعتبار مفهومه مع قطعِ النَّظرِ عن انطباقِهِ على طبيعة موجودة في الخارج، وهذا التَّصرُّرُ يجري في الموجودات قبل العلم بوجودِهَا، وفي المعدوماتِ أيضاً ، والطَّالبُ له «ما» الشَّارحة للاسم، وثانيهما : تصور بحسب الحقيقةِ ؛ أعني : تصرُّرَ الشَّيءِ الَّذي عُلِمَ وُجودُهُ، وَالطَّالبُ لهذا التَّصورِ مَا الحقيقيَّةُ، وكذلك التصديقُ ينقسم إلى التصديق بوجودِ الشَّيء في نفسه وإلى التصديق بثبوتِهِ لغيرِهِ والطَّالبُ لِلأَوَّلِ : «هَل» البسيطةُ، ولِلثَّاني: «هَل» المركَّبَةُ، ولا شُبهة في أنَّ مَطلَبَ مَا الشَّارحةِ مُقدَّم على هَل البسيطة، فإنَّ الشَّيءَ ما لم يتصوَّرُ مَفهومُهُ لم يمكِّن طلب التصديق بوجودِهِ، كَمَا أَنَّ مَطلَبٌ هَل» البسيطة
Chapter: On Definition and Its Types. And this is not a real definition intended to convey a concept not yet obtained. (al-Dusuqi: His saying: 'And this is not a real definition' means the verbal definition; a real definition intended to convey a concept not yet obtained, while the verbal definition is intended to specify what the word was placed for from among all the meanings present with the addressee, so that it is attended to and it is known that the word is placed for it. For example, if the questioner says: 'What is man?' and you say to him: 'Rational animal,' you have explained and clarified that summary quiddity, and the detailed form of the quiddity occurs to him, since you have explained its parts. (al-Attar: He said: His saying: 'And this is not a real definition' but rather its outcome is assent (tasdiq). This is what al-Sayyid chose in his gloss on al-Tajrid: the purpose is to point to an already present form and specify it among the already present forms, so that it is known that the mentioned word is placed for the indicated form. So its outcome is assent, and the judgment that this word is placed for that meaning. End quote. And the commentator's subsequent words refer to this. According to this, the author's saying 'like the verbal' is an analogy. What the author chose is that verbal definition is of the type of nominal definition; so his saying 'like the verbal' is an example. The difference between nominal definition and real definition is that real definition is for a quiddity whose existence is known, while nominal definition is for a quiddity whose existence is not known, whether it is non-existent or existent. If proof is established for its existence, then the nominal definition itself becomes a real definition. Therefore al-Sa'd said in Sharh al-Maqasid: The definition of knowledge mentioned in the introduction of the book is nominal, and after encompassing the issues of that science, it turns into a real definition. The difference between verbal and nominal definition according to what is chosen by al-Sayyid and others that they are opposed: verbal definition does not produce a form, it only distinguishes it so that it is known that the word is placed for it; so its outcome is assent as you heard, and it is not included under the commentator's statement. As for nominal definition, it is a definition by the reality and is included under the commentator's statement. Also, nominal definition cannot be by a synonym, and it is specific to nouns, while verbal definition is different in both respects; and nominal definition is more appropriate for conventional concepts, while verbal definition is more appropriate for language. The purpose is only to specify what the word is placed for from among the other meanings, so that it is attended to and it is known that it is placed for it. (al-Dusuqi:) And if the questioner says: 'What is ghadafar?' and you say to him: 'Lion,' then the addressee does not ignore the reality of lion, but rather conceives of it like other realities. So you have not conveyed to him with your answer the obtainment of the form of lion in his mind, because it was already present before your answer. Rather, you have conveyed to him that this reality, to the exclusion of other realities present with you, is that for which the word ghadafar is placed. And since the outcome of this is assent, as if you said to him: 'Ghadafar is placed for lion,' some said: The verbal definition is not a definition at all, let alone being incomplete. (His saying: The purpose is only to specify what the word is placed for, i.e., by a clearer word, synonymous with it, or more general, or more specific. al-Attar.) And al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawwani supported what the author went to, that the people have justified the precedence of the request of 'what' (ma) for the name over all other requests, because: as long as the meaning of the word is not understood, it is not possible to assent to its existence, so the request for its reality or the assent to the composite statement cannot proceed. For that statement is only completed if the verbal definition enters into the request of 'what' (ma), as is not hidden. End quote. It is clarified by what was mentioned in the old glosses on the new commentary on al-Tajrid: that we have two requests: the request of 'what' (ma) by which concept (tasawwur) is sought, and the request of 'whether' (hal) by which assent (tasdiq) is sought. And concept is of two types: concept by name, which is the concept of a thing in terms of its meaning, disregarding its application to a nature existing in the external world. This concept applies to existents before knowing their existence, and also to non-existents. The seeker of this is 'what' (ma) that explains the name. The second type is concept by reality, meaning the concept of a thing whose existence has been known. The seeker of this concept is the real 'what' (ma). Likewise, assent is divided into assent to the existence of the thing in itself and assent to its being established for something else. The seeker of the first is the simple 'whether' (hal basita), and the seeker of the second is the compound 'whether' (hal murakkaba). There is no doubt that the request of 'what' (ma) that explains the name precedes the simple 'whether' (hal basita), because as long as the meaning of a thing is not conceived, it is not possible to seek assent to its existence, just as the request of the simple 'whether'
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the nature and types of definition, specifically distinguishing between verbal (lafzhi), real (haqiqi), and nominal (ismi) definitions. The author begins by stating that the verbal definition is not a real definition intended to convey a new concept. Rather, it merely specifies which of the already present meanings in the mind of the addressee corresponds to the word. The commentator al-Dusuqi clarifies: a real definition aims to produce a concept not yet obtained, while a verbal definition aims to identify the referent of the word among known meanings. An example is given: if someone asks 'What is man?' and you answer 'Rational animal,' that is a real definition because it provides the constituent parts of the quiddity. Then al-Attar adds a point: the outcome of verbal definition is assent (tasdiq), not a new concept – it is a judgment that the word is placed for that meaning. He refers to al-Sayyid's view in the gloss on al-Tajrid. The discussion then turns to the distinction between nominal and verbal definitions. The author of the matn considered verbal definition a type of nominal definition. The commentator explains that real definition is for a quiddity whose existence is known; nominal definition is for a quiddity whose existence is not yet known. If proof establishes its existence, the nominal definition becomes real. Al-Sa'd in Sharh al-Maqasid illustrates this: the definition of knowledge at the start of a book is nominal; after studying the subject, it becomes real. Then the difference between verbal and nominal definition is delineated: verbal definition does not provide a new form, only distinguishes an existing form; nominal definition does provide a definition by reality. Also, nominal definition cannot be by a synonym and is limited to nouns, whereas verbal definition can be by a synonym and applies to all parts of speech. Nominal definition is more suited for conventional terms, verbal for linguistic terms. The passage then gives the example of 'ghadafar' (a synonym for lion). If someone asks 'What is ghadafar?' and you say 'Lion,' the addressee already knows the reality of lion; you are only informing him that the word 'ghadafar' refers to that reality. The outcome is a judgment, so some scholars said verbal definition is not a definition at all. Finally, al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawwani supports the author by explaining the priority of the request 'what' (ma) over the request 'whether' (hal) – one must first understand the meaning of a word before seeking assent to its existence or to its attributes. The passage then introduces the classification of requests: 'ma' for concept (tasawwur) and 'hal' for assent (tasdiq). Concept is divided into concept by name (which applies even before knowing existence) and concept by reality (after existence is known). Assent is divided into assent to existence (simple 'hal') and assent to a predicate (compound 'hal'). The request 'ma' that explains the name must precede simple 'hal', because without understanding the concept, one cannot seek existence. The text ends mid-sentence, but the point is clear.

Key Terms
التعريف الاسمي
مطلب ما
مطلب هل
تصور
تصديق

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must the request 'what' that explains the name (ma sharha) precede the simple 'whether' (hal basita)?
A) Because existence is more important than meaning.
B) Because one cannot seek assent to existence without first understanding the meaning of the thing.
C) Because nominal definitions are always prior to real definitions.
D) Because the request 'whether' is more complex.

Key Takeaway
Nominal definitions presuppose no known existence; they can become real once existence is established. The request for meaning (ma sharha) must precede the request for existence (hal basita).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: The definition of 'al-Sifat al-Thubutiyya' in Ash'ari kalam is often given as 'meanings that subsist in the essence.' Determine whether this is a nominal or real definition, and explain what would need to be proven to turn it into a real definition.
?
Task 2: Arrange the following requests in correct temporal order: 'Does God exist?' (hal basita), 'What is God?' (ma haqiqiyya), 'What does 'God' mean?' (ma sharha). Justify using the passage.

Verbal Definition: Connecting Words to Known Concepts
Defines verbal definition as explaining a known image as the intended meaning of an obscure word.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi) from real definition (al-ta'rif al-haqiqi) and articulate the purpose of each.

Core Idea
Verbal definition clarifies which concept a word points to; it does not create new concepts.

We often know a concept but not the word for it, or hear a word but don't know what it means. The logicians distinguish between verbal definition, which connects an obscure word to a pre-existing mental image, and real definition, which unpacks the essence. This passage from the Tadhheeb defines verbal definition and highlights this contrast.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of verbal definition
Find the phrase that summarizes verbal definition. The passage says it 'interprets an image present among other images as being the intended meaning of a word.' This is the core idea.
The Arabic phrase 'صورة حاصلة' (sura hasila) refers to a concept already in the mind.
2
Contrast with real definition
The commentator explains that real definition aims to specify and interpret the summarized essence (mahiyya) without focusing on the word's denotation. Note that verbal definition is about word-concept linkage, while real definition is about revealing essence.
Real definition may also implicitly clarify the word, but that is not its primary purpose.
3
Apply the distinction to an example
The passage gives 'al-ghadanfar' (lion) and 'al-'uqar' (intoxicant) as obscure words. Explain how verbal definition works: the listener already has the concept of a lion; the definition tells them that 'ghadanfar' refers to that concept.
This shows that verbal definition presupposes prior knowledge of the concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ وحاصله : أن يُقصَدَ بِهِ تفسير صورة حاصلة من بين سائرِ الصُّورِ بأنَّها المرادَةُ بلفظة كذا . (قَوْلُهُ : وَحَاصِلُهُ) أي : حاصل التعريف اللفظي . (قَوْلُهُ : مِنْ بَيْنِ مُتعلّق بتفسير؛ أي: تعيينها من بين سائرِ الصُّورِ بأنَّها ... إلخ؛ أي : بخلافِ التَّعريف الحقيقي، فإنَّما القصدُ بِهِ تَعيين وتفسير الماهية المجملة التي هي بمعنى اللّفظِ ، بدونِ الالتفات إلى تبيين مدلولِ اللَّفظِ من حيثُ كونُهُ مدلولاً . وإنْ كانَ حاصلاً التزاماً . (قَوْلُهُ: بِلَفْظَةِ كَذَا ) أي : من اللفظ الخفيّ كَالغَضَنْفَرِ والعُقار في الأمثلة السابقة.
Chapter: On Definition and Its Divisions. Its summary: that by it is intended to interpret an image present among other images as being the intended meaning of a certain word. (His statement: 'and its summary') i.e., the summary of verbal definition. (His statement: 'from among' is attached to 'interpretation'; i.e., specifying it from among other images as being... etc.; i.e., unlike real definition, for the purpose by it is to specify and interpret the summarized essence which is the meaning of the word, without turning to clarifying the denotation of the word in terms of being a denotation, even if it results implicitly. (His statement: 'by a certain word') i.e., from an obscure word like al-ghadanfar and al-'uqar in the previous examples.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage defines verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi). The author begins by stating the section heading, then gives the summary: verbal definition seeks to explain a pre-existing mental image among other images as the one intended by a particular word. The commentator Dasuqi clarifies each part. He explains that the summary referred to is that of verbal definition. The phrase "from among" indicates that the definition singles out one specific image from the set of all images. This distinguishes verbal definition from real definition (al-ta'rif al-haqiqi), which aims to specify and interpret the summarized essence that is the meaning of the word, without focusing on clarifying the word's denotation as denotation—though that may happen implicitly. An example is given: the word "ghadanfar" (lion) or "'uqar" (intoxicating drink) are obscure words whose meanings are clarified through verbal definition. So verbal definition is useful for someone who already has the concept but does not know the word, or vice versa.

Key Terms
التعريف اللفظي
التعريف الحقيقي
صورة حاصلة

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes verbal definition from real definition?
A) Verbal definition explains the essence; real definition clarifies word meaning.
B) Verbal definition connects a word to a pre-existing image; real definition interprets the summarized essence.
C) Both definitions do the same thing but in different languages.
D) Verbal definition is only for obscure words; real definition is for common words.

Key Takeaway
Verbal definition is a tool for word-concept linkage; it does not expand knowledge of the thing itself.

The Nine Types of Definition in Islamic Logic
Mir Zahid enumerates nine types of definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate and distinguish the nine types of definition based on real/verbal, hadd/rasm, and complete/incomplete.

Core Idea
Definitions are not all the same; nine distinct types serve different epistemic purposes.

This passage from Mir Zahid al-Hindi's supercommentary systematically classifies definitions. You will learn how to break down a definition into its type by asking: Is it real or verbal? Is it by essence or name? Is it hadd or rasm? Is it complete or incomplete? Mastering this taxonomy is essential for evaluating definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first division: real vs verbal
The passage begins by dividing definition into haqiqi (real) and lafzi (verbal). Real gives a new concept; verbal recalls a stored concept. Ask: does this definition introduce a new concept or clarify a word?
2
Subdivide real definitions: by essence vs by name
Real definition divides into bihasab al-haqiqa (according to essence) and bihasab al-ism (according to name). The former gives concept of something whose existence is known externally; the latter gives concept of something whose existence is unknown. The basis is whether the existence is known.
3
Apply the hadd/rasm distinction
Each of the two real types further divides into hadd (definition by genus+differentia) and rasm (description by properties/accidents). Determine whether the definition reveals essence or merely describes.
4
Check completeness and count the nine types
Each of the four (real-essence hadd/rasm, real-name hadd/rasm) splits into tamm (complete) and naqis (incomplete). The ninth type is verbal definition itself, which may also have hadd/rasm and complete/incomplete variants. Count: 2 (real-essence: hadd tamm/naqis, rasm tamm/naqis) + similar for real-name = 4, plus verbal gives total 9.
The text states 'فترتقي أقسام التعريف إلى تسعة أقسام'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلَمْ أَنَّ التّعريف؛ إمَّا حقيقيّ : وَبِهِ يحصلُ التَّصوُّرُ ابتداءً، أو لفظي : وَبِهِ يحصلُ التَّصوُّرُ ثانياً، والأوَّلُ ينقسم إلى التّعريف بحسب الحقيقة، وهو ما يحصلُ بِهِ تصور ما عُلِمَ وجوده في نفس الأمر، وإلى التعريف بحسب الاسم، وهو ما يحصل به تصور ما لم يعلم وجودُهُ فيها، وكُلّ منهما ينقسم إلى الحدّ والرَّسم، وكُلّ مِنْ هذهِ الأربعةِ ينقسم إلى التّامّ والنَّاقص، فترتقي أقسامُ التَّعريفِ إلى تسعة أقسام
Know that definition: either real, and by it the concept is obtained initially, or verbal, and by it the concept is obtained secondarily. The first (real) divides into definition according to essence, which is that by which a concept of something whose existence is known in reality is obtained, and into definition according to name, which is that by which a concept of something whose existence is not known in it is obtained. And each of these two divides into definition proper (hadd) and description (rasm). And each of these four divides into complete and incomplete. Thus the divisions of definition amount to nine sections.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage from Mir Zahid al-Hindi's supercommentary on al-Mawaqif provides a systematic classification of definitions. It begins by stating that definition is either real (haqiqi) or verbal (lafzi). Real definition yields a concept for the first time, whereas verbal definition recalls a concept that is already stored in the mind. The real definition is further divided into two: definition according to essence (bi-hasab al-haqiqa), which gives the concept of something whose existence is already known in external reality, and definition according to name (bi-hasab al-ism), which gives the concept of something whose existence is not yet known (i.e., it clarifies the meaning of a term). Each of these two types then divides into hadd (a definition stating the essence through genus and differentia) and rasm (a description using properties and accidents). Finally, each of these four subdivisions (real-essential hadd, real-essential rasm, real-nominal hadd, real-nominal rasm) splits into complete (tamm) and incomplete (naqis), yielding eight types. The author then asserts that the total number of definition types reaches nine. The ninth is likely the verbal definition itself, which is also subdivided into hadd and rasm, but the text does not elaborate here. In standard logical works, the nine types are: haqiqi bihasab al-haqiqa hadd tamm/naqis (2), haqiqi bihasab al-haqiqa rasm tamm/naqis (2), haqiqi bihasab al-ism hadd tamm/naqis (2), haqiqi bihasab al-ism rasm tamm/naqis (2), and the verbal definition (lafzi) itself as the ninth. This classification is important because it shows that definitions are not limited to a single type; each type serves a different purpose in the acquisition of concepts. The student should memorize this enumeration and understand the basis of each distinction: reality vs. name, hadd vs. rasm, complete vs. incomplete.

Key Terms

حقيقي
لفظي
حد
رسم
تام

A) Four

C) Nine
D) Ten

Key Takeaway
The nine types of definition arise from a threefold distinction: real/verbal, essence/name, hadd/rasm, and complete/incomplete.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the definition of 'salat' in fiqh: 'Salat is a specific set of actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim.' Identify which of the nine types it is. Justify: is it haqiqi or lafzi? Had or rasm? Complete or incomplete?
?
Find a definition of 'iman' in a kalam text (e.g., 'Iman is affirmation in the heart and profession with the tongue'). Classify it according to the nine types and explain your reasoning.

The Core Debate: Conceptual vs Assertoric Verbal Definition
Authors debate whether verbal definition is conceptual or assertoric

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of al-Sayyid and al-Taftazani on the nature of verbal definition and reconstruct al-Sayyid's argument in conditional form.

Core Idea
Is verbal definition a demand for a concept or for assent?

In this passage, the author presents two opposing views on whether verbal definition is a conceptual (tasawwuri) or assertoric (tasdiqi) demand. Al-Sayyid argues that it must be assertoric to avoid the absurdity of acquiring something already possessed. Al-Taftazani counters that it is conceptual, but this raises the question of how it differs from nominal definition. Understanding this debate clarifies the role of definition in logic and epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two camps
Two main figures are named: al-Sayyid (al-Jurjani) and al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani. What does each claim about the nature of verbal definition?
Al-Sayyid says it is tasdiqi; al-Taftazani says it is tasawwuri.
2
Extract al-Sayyid's argument
Al-Sayyid argues that if verbal definition were tasawwuri, it would entail 'tahsil al-hasil' (acquiring what is already acquired). Why is that impossible? What does he propose instead?
He says the concept exists in the treasury (khazana), not in the perceptive faculty (mudrika). Verbal definition brings it to the perceptive faculty, but still he claims this is an assertoric act.
3
Reconstruct his argument as a conditional
Write the conditional: If verbal definition is tasawwuri, then it leads to acquisition of acquired. But acquisition of acquired is impossible. Therefore, verbal definition is not tasawwuri. This is modus tollens.
This formalization highlights the logical structure.
4
Examine al-Taftazani's counter
Al-Taftazani claims verbal definition is tasawwuri and sees no difference from nominal definition. But the author objects that self-evident matters can be clarified by verbal definition but not by nominal definition. Why is that a problem?
This suggests that verbal definition has a role beyond nominal definition, at least for self-evident concepts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد طال الكلام في التَّعريف اللفظي؛ فَذَهَبَ السَّيِّدُ وَمَنْ تَبِعَهُ إلى أنَّهُ مِنَ المطالبِ التَّصديقيَّةِ ؛ مُتمسِّكِينَ بأَنَّهُ لو كانَ مِنَ المطالبِ التَّصوريَّةِ ؛ لَزِمَ حصول الحاصلِ لِحصولِ التَّصورِ سابقاً، وَلَا يَخفَى أنَّ الصُّورة قبلَ التَّعريف اللفظي حاصلةٌ في الخزانة؛ لا في المدركةِ، فإنَّها منذُ زوالِ الالتفات إليها ؛ تزولُ عن المدركة وتبقى في الخزانة، ثمَّ إذا توجهت الالتفات إليها ؛ تحصلُ مرَّةٌ أُخرى في المدركة، والمقصودُ مِنَ التَّعريف اللفظي هذا الحصولُ لا الحصولُ السَّابِقُ، مع أنَّ التَّعريف اللفظي حينئذٍ يكونُ بحثاً لغويّاً خارجاً عَن طريقةِ أهل العقول، وذهب المحقِّقُ التَّفتازانيُّ وَمَنْ وافَقَهُ إِلَى أنَّهُ مِنَ المطالب التَّصوريَّةِ ؛ زاعمين عدم الفرق بينَهُ وبينَ التَّعريف الاسمي، ومن البيِّن أنَّ البديهي يحتملُ التَّعريف اللفظي ولا يحتمل الاسمي، وذهب بعضُ الأعاظم مِنَ المحققين إلى أنَّه من المطالب التَّصوريَّة، والمقصود منه الالتفاتُ إلى الصُّورة المخزونة؛ أي: غرضُ المعرَّفِ منه تصوُّرُ المعرَّف في المدركة مرَّةً ثانيةً؛ مُتمسّكاً بأنَّ القومَ علَّلُوا تقدُّمَ مَا الاسميَّةِ على جميع المطالب بأنَّهُ : مَا لَمْ يُفهم معنى اللفظ ؛ لا يمكن التصديق بوجودِهِ، ولا يتمشى طلب حقيقتِهِ وَلَا التصديقُ بهليَّتِهِ المركَّب، وهذا إنَّما يتم إذا كانَ التَّعريفُ اللفظي داخلاً في مَطلَبِ ما ، وبِهَذا تعلمُ أنَّ التَّعريف الاسمي مطلب ((ما ) الاسميَّةِ، وَبِهِ يفهم معنى اللَّفْظِ ؛ لَا بالتعريف اللفظي ، فإِنَّهُ بعد تصورِهِ فإذا لم يكن التعريفُ اللفظي داخلاً في مَطلَبِ (ما) ؛ لا يتم ذلكَ التَّعليلُ، مع أنَّ مَن قالَ إِنَّهُ مِنَ المطالب التصديقيَّة؛ لا ينكر كونَهُ مَطلَب «ما»، لكنْ ذهب إلى أنَّ ما لهُ التَّصديقُ ، وذهب بعضُ الأفاضل إلى أنَّهُ مِنَ المطالبِ التَّصوريَّةِ ؛ زعماً منه أنَّه يفيد تصور الموضوع له من حيثُ إِنَّه معنى اللفظ ، وأنتَ خبيرٌ بأَنَّهُ حينئذ يصير تعريفاً اسميًا رسميا، ويكون البحث مِن قبيل البحثِ اللُّغويّ، وتحقيق المقام أنَّهُ : إذا سُئِلَ عَن أمر بديهي فَقِيلَ : مَا الوجود مثلاً؟
And the discussion about verbal definition has become lengthy. Al-Sayyid and his followers went that it is among the assertoric demands, holding that if it were among the conceptual demands, then the acquisition of what has already been acquired would be necessary due to the prior acquisition of the concept. And it is not hidden that the form before verbal definition is present in the treasury (of the mind), not in the perceptive faculty. For after attention turns away from it, it leaves the perceptive faculty and remains in the treasury. Then when attention is directed to it, it is obtained again in the perceptive faculty. And the intended purpose of verbal definition is this (new) acquisition, not the prior acquisition. However, in that case, verbal definition becomes a linguistic inquiry outside the method of the rational people. And the investigator al-Taftazani and those who agreed with him went that it is among the conceptual demands, claiming no difference between it and nominal definition. And it is evident that the self-evident admits verbal definition but does not admit nominal definition. And some of the great investigators went that it is among the conceptual demands, and the intended purpose is paying attention to the stored form; i.e., the goal of the definer is the conceptualization of the defined in the perceptive faculty a second time. He holds that the earlier scholars justified the priority of the nominal 'what' question over all demands by saying: as long as the meaning of the word is not understood, one cannot assent to its existence, nor can one pursue the inquiry into its essence, nor assent to its composite existence. And this is only completed if verbal definition falls within the demand of 'what'. And by this you know that the nominal definition is the demand of the nominal 'what', and by it the meaning of the word is understood; not by verbal definition, because it is after its conceptualization. So if verbal definition were not included in the demand of 'what', that justification would not hold. And note that whoever said it is among the assertoric demands does not deny that it is a demand of 'what', but rather holds that it is an assertoric 'what'. And some of the distinguished scholars went that it is among the conceptual demands, claiming that it provides the conceptualization of the referent inasmuch as it is the meaning of the word. And you know well that then it becomes a nominal descriptive definition, and the inquiry becomes of the type of linguistic inquiry. And the truth of the matter is: if one is asked about a self-evident matter and asked: 'What is existence, for example?'
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed debate about the nature of verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi). The author first mentions that the discussion has become lengthy. He then presents the view of al-Sayyid (al-Sharif al-Jurjani) and his followers, who argue that verbal definition is an assertoric demand (talab tasdiqi). Their reasoning is that if it were a conceptual demand (talab tasawwuri), it would involve acquiring something already acquired, since the concept is already stored in the mind. The author then adds a clarification: the image (sura) before verbal definition is present in the treasury (khazana) of memory, not in the perceptive faculty (al-mudrika). When attention turns away, it leaves the perceptive faculty but remains stored. When attention is directed back, it is obtained again in the perceptive faculty. The goal of verbal definition is this renewed acquisition, not the original one. However, the author notes that this reduces verbal definition to a linguistic exercise outside the method of rational people. Next, the view of al-Taftazani and his followers is presented: they hold that verbal definition is a conceptual demand, seeing no difference between it and nominal definition. But the objection is raised that self-evident matters can be clarified by verbal definition but not by nominal definition, showing a distinction. Then a group of great investigators holds that verbal definition is conceptual, and its purpose is to pay attention (iltifat) to the stored form, i.e., to bring the concept back into the perceptive faculty. They base this on the principle that the nominal 'what' (ma al-ismiyya) question has priority over all demands: unless the meaning of the word is understood, one cannot proceed to seek its essence or existence. This principle requires that verbal definition be included within the demand of 'what' (matlab ma). The author then clarifies that nominal definition is truly the demand of the nominal 'what', because it provides the meaning of the word; verbal definition, on the other hand, comes after concept formation and is not the true source of understanding the word. However, those who claim verbal definition is assertoric do not deny it is a demand of 'what', but consider it an assertoric 'what'. Finally, some distinguished scholars say it is conceptual, claiming it provides the concept of the referent as the meaning of the word, but the author notes that this reduces it to a nominal descriptive definition and a linguistic investigation. The passage ends with the truth of the matter being that if someone asks about a self-evident thing like 'What is existence?', then... (the text cuts off, but the implication is that verbal definition is appropriate for such cases, despite the debate).

Refinement: Verbal Definition as Renewed Conceptual Attention
A refined view and distinctions between nominal and verbal definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the refined position that verbal definition is a conceptual demand aimed at renewing attention to a stored concept, and evaluate how it differs from nominal definition.

Core Idea
Verbal definition revives a concept from memory to the active mind.

To resolve the debate, some great investigators proposed that verbal definition is indeed conceptual, but its purpose is to redirect attention (iltifat) to a concept stored in the treasury of the mind. This view reconciles the earlier objections and maintains the priority of the nominal 'what' question. The author then clarifies that nominal definition is the true source of understanding a word, while verbal definition presupposes it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the refined position
The passage mentions 'ba'd al-a'azam min al-muhaqqiqin'. What is their claim about verbal definition?
They say it is tasawwuri, and its purpose is iltifat to the stored form.
2
Understand the justification
They argue that the priority of the nominal 'what' question requires that verbal definition be included within the demand of 'what'. How does this connect?
If verbal definition were not part of the 'what' demand, then the principle that understanding the word is prerequisite for further inquiry would not hold.
3
Distinguish from nominal definition
The author points out that nominal definition is what actually provides the meaning of the word; verbal definition comes after conceptualization. What does this imply about the relationship?
Verbal definition is a secondary renewal, not the primary understanding.
4
Evaluate the reduction to linguistic inquiry
Some other scholars held that verbal definition becomes just a linguistic clarification. What does the author think about that?
The author notes that this reduces it to a nominal descriptive definition, which is linguistic rather than logical.

Verbal Definition: Conceptual or Judgmental Demand?
Author discusses differing views on whether verbal definition is a conceptual or judgmental demand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether a given verbal definition aims at conceptualization (tasawwur) or assent (tasdiq) based on the science in which it is used.

Core Idea
Verbal definition's aim shifts: linguistic sciences seek tasdiq, rational sciences seek tasawwur.

This passage from the super-commentary on al-Tadheeb explores the nature of verbal definition. Scholars debated whether it belongs to conceptual demands (tasawwuriyyat) or judgmental demands (tasdiqiyyat). The author resolves the debate by distinguishing between linguistic and rational sciences. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying definitions in Islamic logic and methodology.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two mental faculties
The author introduces two terms: al-mudrika (the perceptive faculty) and al-khazana (the memory treasury). Before verbal definition, the image of the thing exists in the memory treasury, not in the perceptive faculty. When attention is directed, the image reappears in the perceptive faculty. Verbal definition aims to bring about this renewed appearance.
This psychological model is used to explain how verbal definition works.
2
Identify the three positions on verbal definition
Al-Taftazani and his followers say verbal definition is a conceptual demand, indistinguishable from nominal definition. Some greats (e.g., al-Dawwani) also say it is conceptual, aiming to redirect attention to the stored image. Others say it is a judgmental demand, including both conceptualization and assent.
Each scholar uses different criteria to classify verbal definition.
3
Analyze the verification (tahqiq) by discipline
The author gives the example of defining 'existence' as 'that which is an agent or patient'. In linguistic sciences, the primary purpose is assent (tasdiq) that the word denotes the meaning. In rational sciences, the primary purpose is conceptualization (tasawwur) of the meaning. The other is implicit.
This resolution ties the classification to the science's objective, not an inherent property.
4
Apply the distinction to an Islamic science example
Consider the definition of 'qiyas' (analogy). In a linguistic work, the definition aims to confirm the word's usage (tasdiq). In a usul al-fiqh work, it aims to conceptualize the logical structure of analogy (tasawwur). The same definition can serve different purposes.
This shows the practical relevance of the author's resolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولَا يَخفَى أنَّ الصُّورة قبلَ التَّعريف اللفظي حاصلةٌ في الخزانة؛ لا في المدركةِ، فإنَّها منذُ زوالِ الالتفات إليها؛ تزولُ عن المدركة وتبقى في الخزانة، ثمَّ إذا وتجهت الالتفات إليها؛ تحصلُ مرَّةٌ أُخرى في المدركة، والمقصودُ مِنَ التَّعريف اللفظي هذا الحصولُ لا الحصولُ السَّابِقُ، مع أنَّ التَّعريف اللفظي حينئذٍ يكونُ بحثاً لغويّاً خارجاً عَن طريقةِ أهل العقول، وذهب المحقِّقُ التَّفتازانيُّ وَمَنْ وافَقَهُ إِلَى أنَّهُ مِنَ المطالب التَّصوريَّةِ؛ زاعمين عدم الفرق بينَهُ وبينَ التَّعريف الاسمي، ومن البيِّن أنَّ البديهي يحتملُ التَّعريف اللفظي ولا يحتمل الاسمي، وذهب بعضُ الأعاظم مِنَ المحققين إلى أنَّه من المطالب التَّصوريَّة، والمقصود منه الالتفاتُ إلى الصُّورة المخزونة؛ أي: غرضُ المعرَّفِ منه تصوُّرُ المعرَّف في المدركة مرَّةً ثانيةً؛ مُتمسّكاً بأنَّ القومَ علَّلُوا تقدُّمَ ما الاسميَّةِ على جميع المطالب بأنَّهُ: ما لَمْ يُفهم معنى اللفظ؛ لا يمكن التصديق بوجودِهِ، ولا يتمشى طلب حقيقتِهِ وَلَا التصديقُ بهليَّتِهِ المركَّب، وهذا إنَّما يتم إذا كانَ التَّعريفُ اللفظي داخلاً في مَطلَبِ ما، وبِهَذا تعلمُ أنَّ التَّعريف الاسمي مطلب ما الاسميَّةِ، وَبِهِ يفهم معنى اللَّفْظِ؛ لَا بالتعريف اللفظي، فإِنَّهُ بعد تصورِهِ فإذا لم يكن التعريفُ اللفظي داخلاً في مَطلَبِ ما؛ لا يتم ذلكَ التَّعليلُ، مع أنَّ مَن قالَ إِنَّهُ مِنَ المطالب التصديقيَّة; لا ينكر كونَهُ مَطلَب ما، لكنْ ذهب إلى أنَّ ما لهُ التَّصديقُ، وذهب بعضُ الأفاضل إلى أنَّهُ مِنَ المطالبِ التَّصوريَّةِ؛ زعماً منه أنَّه يفيد تصور الموضوع له من حيثُ إِنَّه معنى اللفظ، وأنتَ خبيرٌ بأَنَّهُ حينئذ يصير تعريفاً اسميًا رسميا، ويكون البحث مِن قبيل البحثِ اللُّغويّ، وتحقيق المقام أنَّهُ: إذا سُئِلَ عَن أمر بديهي فَقِيلَ: مَا الوجود مثلاً؟ فيُقالُ: مَا يكون فاعلاً أو مُنفعلاً، فَمِنْ شَأنِهِ أَنَّهُ يحصلُ لهُ منه للسائل إحضار معنى الوجود، والالتفات إليه من بين الصُّورِ المخزونة، وأن يحصل لهُ التَّصديق بأنَّ لفظ الوجود موضوع لهذا المعنى، فإذا قيل ذلك في العلوم اللغويَّة؛ فالمقصود منه التصديق، وإنْ كانَ التَّصوُّرُ حاصِلاً في ضمنِهِ؛ إذْ نَظَرُ أرباب تلك الصناعاتِ مقصور على الألفاظ، وإذا قيلَ ذلكَ في العلوم العقليَّةِ؛ فالمقصود منه على ما هو وظيفةُ هذه العلومِ النَّصور، وإنْ كانَ التَّصديق حاصلاً في ضمنه ا.هـ. وَلِلفاضل المرعشي كلامٌ في هذا المقام ذَكَرَهُ في تقرير القوانين، فإِنْ ضممتَهُ إلى ما هنا; وقعت على حقيقة الحال وسبقت غيرَكَ في هذا المجال.
And it is not hidden that the image before the verbal definition is present in the treasury (of memory), not in the perceptive faculty, because from the moment attention is withdrawn from it, it disappears from the perceptive faculty and remains in the treasury. Then when attention is directed to it, it appears again in the perceptive faculty. The purpose of the verbal definition is this attainment (in the perceptive faculty), not the prior attainment (in the treasury). Moreover, the verbal definition would then be a linguistic inquiry outside the method of the rational scholars. The investigator al-Taftazani and those who agreed with him held that it is from the conceptual demands, claiming no difference between it and the nominal definition, while it is evident that the self-evident can bear verbal definition but not nominal definition. Some of the greats among the investigators held that it is from the conceptual demands, and its purpose is to direct attention to the stored image; meaning: the aim of the definer is the conceptualization of the definiendum in the perceptive faculty a second time, adhering to the fact that the scholars explained the priority of the 'what' nominal request over all demands by saying that unless the meaning of the word is understood, it is not possible to assent to its existence, nor can one proceed to seek its reality, nor to assent to its composite hawness. This is only complete if the verbal definition is included in the 'what' demand. And by this you know that the nominal definition is the 'what' nominal demand, and by it the meaning of the word is understood, not by the verbal definition, because after its conceptualization (?) So if the verbal definition is not included in the 'what' demand, that explanation is not complete. Even though whoever said it is from judgmental demands does not deny that it is a 'what' demand, but he held that its 'what' includes judgment. And some of the excellent ones held that it is from conceptual demands, claiming that it provides conceptualization of the referent in that it is the meaning of the word. And you are aware that then it becomes a formal nominal definition, and the inquiry becomes a linguistic inquiry. The verification of the matter is that if one is asked about a self-evident matter, e.g., 'what is existence?', he responds: 'that which is an agent or patient.' It is proper that from this answer the questioner obtains the bringing to mind of the meaning of existence, and attention to it from among the stored images, and that he obtains the assent that the word 'existence' is assigned to this meaning. So if this is said in the linguistic sciences, the purpose is assent, even though conceptualization is implicit in it, because the focus of the masters of those disciplines is on words. And if this is said in the rational sciences, the purpose, according to the function of these sciences, is conceptualization, even though assent is implicit in it. End. And al-Fadil al-Mar'ashi has words on this topic which he mentioned in his Taqrir al-Qawanin; if you add them to what is here, you will arrive at the true state of affairs and surpass others in this field.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary expansion on the nature of verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi) and whether it belongs to conceptual demands (al-matalib al-tasawwuriyya) or judgmental demands (al-matalib al-tasdiqiyya). The author begins by clarifying that before verbal definition, the image (sura) of the thing is already stored in the memory treasury (khazana), not actively in the perceptive faculty (mudrika). When attention is withdrawn, the image leaves the perceptive faculty but remains stored. When attention is turned to it again, it reappears in the perceptive faculty. The purpose of verbal definition is precisely this renewed appearance, not the original storage. However, if verbal definition only recalls an already known image, it becomes a linguistic inquiry, not a rational one. The author then reports the view of al-Taftazani and his followers, who consider verbal definition a conceptual demand, indistinguishable from nominal definition (ta'rif ismi). They claim that self-evident matters can be verbally defined but not nominally defined, implying a difference. Next, 'some of the greats' (al-Dawwani) also hold it is conceptual, aiming to redirect attention to the stored image, relying on the principle that understanding the word's meaning is prerequisite for any further inquiry—thus the verbal definition must be part of the 'what' demand (matlab ma). The nominal definition provides understanding of the word's meaning, not the verbal definition. Those who say verbal definition is judgmental concede it is a 'what' demand but one that includes tasdiq. Then 'some of the excellent ones' (Mulla Sadra) also say it is conceptual, providing conceptualization of the referent as the meaning of the word, which the author notes turns it into a formal nominal definition (ta'rif ismi rasmī) and a linguistic inquiry. The author then gives the verification (tahqiq): if one asks about a self-evident thing like 'existence', the answer 'that which is an agent or patient' brings the meaning of existence to mind and gives assent that the word 'existence' denotes this meaning. In linguistic sciences, the aim is assent (tasdiq), though conceptualization is implicit; in rational sciences, the aim is conceptualization (tasawwur), though assent is implicit. This distinguishes the two disciplines: linguists focus on words, rational scholars focus on meanings. The author concludes by recommending al-Mar'ashi's work for further insight.

Key Terms
التعريف اللفظي
المطالب التصورية
المطالب التصديقية
بديهي
الخزانة
المدركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a self-evident concept like 'existence' is defined verbally in the rational sciences, what is the primary purpose?
A) To provide assent (tasdiq) that the word denotes the meaning
B) To provide conceptualization (tasawwur) of the meaning
C) To provide both equally
D) To provide a nominal definition

Key Takeaway
The function of verbal definition is not fixed; it varies according to the discipline: in linguistic sciences it primarily gives assent (tasdiq), while in rational sciences it primarily gives conceptualization (tasawwur).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the verbal definition of 'ijma'' (consensus) in a usul al-fiqh textbook: 'Ijma' is the agreement of the mujtahids of the Ummah on a legal ruling after the death of the Prophet (s).' Identify whether this definition primarily aims at tasawwur or tasdiq in the context of usul al-fiqh, and explain your reasoning based on the author's criteria.
