Real Definition vs. Non-Real Definitions
Author clarifies the agreement that the definition is not real.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) and non-real definitions (verbal/nominal) and identify which type of definition a given statement falls into based on the criteria from this passage.

Core Idea
Not every definition reveals the essence; many are merely verbal or nominal.

The passage opens by stating that the definition under discussion is not a real definition by agreement (ittifaqan). This immediately highlights the crucial distinction between definitions that capture the quiddity (mahiyya) of a thing and those that only specify the referent of a word or clarify meaning through other words. In this lesson, we will dissect the criteria that make a definition 'real' and see how verbal and nominal definitions fall short.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of definition
From the passage, extract the three kinds: real (haqiqi), verbal (lafzi), and nominal (ismi). Notice how the passage says the negated definition is either verbal or of the type of nominal.
The passage explicitly negates it being real, leaving the other two possibilities.
2
Understand the criteria for a real definition
A real definition should provide conceptualization (tasawwur) of what has not been obtained at all, either by its quiddity (bi-kunnihi) or by its distinction from all others (bi-tamyizihi 'an jami' aghyarihi). This is the standard from the tradition.
The commentator's later phrase reinforces this.
3
Contrast with verbal definition
A verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) explains the meaning of a word using other words, relying on already known concepts. It does not reveal the essence.
Often used for clarifying ambiguous terms.
4
Contrast with nominal definition
A nominal definition (ta'rif ismi) specifies the referent of a word without revealing its essence. It differs from verbal definition in that it focuses on naming rather than lexical explanation.
The passage says it is 'muqabil li-l-ismi' or 'min qabil al-ismi'.
5
Apply the distinction
Given an example of a definition from fiqh or kalam, determine whether it is real, verbal, or nominal by checking if it reveals the quiddity or only clarifies the word's meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ: وَلَيْسَ هَذَا تَعْرِيْفَاً حَقِيقِيًّا أي اتّفاقاً، بل هو تعريف لفظي مُقابل للاسميّ، أو مِنْ قَبيلِ الاسمي فيه ما تقدَّمَ ثمَّ إِنَّ صَدرَ عبارةِ الشَّارحِ؛ يميلُ لِكلامٍ السَّيِّدِ، وعجزُهَا لِكلام المصنفِ، فَقولُ البعض أرادَ بحقيقتِهِ المنفيَّةِ أن يفيد تصوَّر ما لم يحصل أصلاً بكنههِ أو بتمييزه عن جميع أغياره كما يرشدُ له قولُهُ بعدُ: (وإنَّما المرادُ تَعيينُ مَا وضعَ لَهُ اللَّفْظُ ...إلخ)، ومَنْ نزَّله على ما يراهُ السَّيِّدُ؛ فَقَدْ وهم غفلة عمَّا بعدَه .ا.هـ. أخذ بالظَّاهر كالمنزلِ أيضاً، ثمّ إنَّ ذلكَ البعض بعدَ أنْ نقل عبارةَ الجلالِ في مراتبِ التَّصورِ التي نقلناها; نقل اعتراض العصام عليها وأخذ في ردّ تلك الاعتراضات، والكُلَّ أوهام على أوهام، فَخُذْ مَا نقلناهُ لَّكَ وَإِنْ أَدَّى إلى تطويل; فإنّي أرجو إنْ شاءَ الله تعالى أنْ يكونَ عليهِ التَّعويلُ : ود إنَّ السّلاحَ جميعُ النَّاسِ تَحمِلُهُ وليسَ كُلُّ ذواتِ المُخْلَبِ السَّبُعُ
His statement: 'And this is not a real definition' means by agreement, but it is a verbal definition opposed to the nominal, or of the type of nominal definition as previously mentioned. Then, the beginning of the expression of the commentator leans toward the statement of al-Sayyid, and its end toward the statement of the author. So some intended by the negated reality that it should provide conceptualization of what has not been obtained at all, either by its quiddity or by its distinction from all others, as indicated by his later statement: 'But the intention is only to specify what the word is assigned to... etc.' And whoever interprets it according to what al-Sayyid sees has erred, being heedless of what comes after. End. He took the apparent meaning like the one who also interpreted? Then, after that someone had quoted al-Jalal's statement on the ranks of conceptualization which we quoted, he transmitted al-Isam's objection to it and began refuting those objections, and all are errors upon errors. So take what we have transmitted to you, even if it leads to length, for I hope, God willing, that reliance will be upon it: 'And indeed, the weapon that all people carry is not every clawed animal is a lion...'
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage continues the super-commentary on the definition discussion. The author clarifies the meaning of the commentator's (al-Attar's) statement that 'this is not a real definition' (laysa hadha ta'rifan haqiqiyyan). The phrase 'real definition' is negated by agreement (ittifaqan) — meaning everyone agrees it is not a real definition. Instead, it is either a verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) as opposed to nominal definition, or a type of nominal definition (as previously discussed). The author then notes a tension: the beginning of the commentator's expression leans toward al-Sayyid's view, while the end leans toward the author's (al-Dasuqi's) view. Some interpreters took the negated 'reality' to mean that it should provide conceptualization of something not previously obtained at all — either by its quiddity (kunnihi) or by its distinction from all others — as indicated by the commentator's later phrase 'But the intention is only to specify what the word is assigned to...' The author criticizes these interpreters, saying that whoever interprets according to al-Sayyid's view is heedless of what comes after. Then the author reports that someone (presumably the same 'some') quoted al-Jalal al-Dawwani's statement on the ranks of conceptualization, then transmitted al-Isam's objection, and then began refuting those objections. The author dismisses all of these as errors upon errors. He urges the reader to take the transmitted material as it is, even if lengthy, as it is reliable. The passage ends with a poetic verse: 'The weapon that all people carry is not every clawed animal is a lion' — a metaphor for not every apparent definition is valid.

تعريف حقيقي
تعريف اسمي
التعريف اللفظي

Checkpoint

A) It is not a definition at all
B) It is not a definition that reveals the quiddity or fully distinguishes
C) It is not a verbal definition
D) It is not a nominal definition

Key Takeaway
The crucial distinction between real and non-real definitions hinges on whether the definition reveals the quiddity or fully distinguishes the thing from all others; if it merely clarifies the word's meaning, it is verbal or nominal.

Navigating Commentator Disagreements
Author warns against partial interpretation of the commentator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a commentator's interpretation is inconsistent with the overall text and evaluate conflicting scholarly opinions on definitional matters.

Core Idea
A commentator's opening words may lean one way, but his later words may correct it.

In this passage, the super-commentator al-Dasuqi points out that the commentator al-Attar's statement has an internal tension: the beginning seems to agree with al-Sayyid's view, while the end aligns with al-Dasuqi's own view. This demonstrates the importance of reading a scholar's full expression and not taking an isolated part as the final position. The author also criticizes those who misinterpreted the statement by ignoring the later part.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two parts of the commentator's statement
In the Arabic, identify the beginning and end of the commentator's expression. The passage says 'the beginning of the expression leans toward al-Sayyid's view, and its end toward the author's view.'
This is a direct statement from the super-commentator.
2
Understand the two views on the definition
Al-Sayyid's view likely interprets 'real definition' in a certain way, while al-Dasuqi's view offers another. The exact content is not given, but the tension is about what 'real' means in the negated phrase.
3
Analyze the author's criticism
The author says that whoever interprets the commentator's statement according to al-Sayyid's view alone has erred, being heedless of what comes after. This teaches us to consider the full context.
The error is from a partial reading.
4
Apply the principle to your own reading
When you encounter a scholarly text, always read the entire passage and note any shifts in position. Do not take an early sentence as final without checking later qualifications.

قَوْلُهُ: وَلَيْسَ هَذَا تَعْرِيْفَاً حَقِيقِيًّا أي اتّفاقاً، بل هو تعريف لفظي مُقابل للاسميّ، أو مِنْ قَبيلِ الاسمي فيه ما تقدَّمَ ثمَّ إِنَّ صَدرَ عبارةِ الشَّارحِ؛ يميلُ لِكلامٍ السَّيِّدِ، وعجزُهَا لِكلام المصنفِ، فَقولُ البعض أرادَ بحقيقتِهِ المنفيَّةِ أن يفيد تصوَّر ما لم يحصل أصلاً بكنههِ أو بتمييزه عن جميع أغياره كما يرشدُ له قولُهُ بعدُ: (وإنَّما المرادُ تَعيينُ مَا وضعَ لَهُ اللَّفْظُ ...إلخ)، ومَنْ نزَّله على ما يراهُ السَّيِّدُ؛ فَقَدْ وهم غفلة عمَّا بعدَه .ا.هـ. أخذ بالظَّاهر كالمنزلِ أيضاً، ثمّ إنَّ ذلكَ البعض بعدَ أنْ نقل عبارةَ الجلالِ في مراتبِ التَّصورِ التي نقلناها; نقل اعتراض العصام عليها وأخذ في ردّ تلك الاعتراضات، والكُلَّ أوهام على أوهام، فَخُذْ مَا نقلناهُ لَّكَ وَإِنْ أَدَّى إلى تطويل; فإنّي أرجو إنْ شاءَ الله تعالى أنْ يكونَ عليهِ التَّعويلُ : ود إنَّ السّلاحَ جميعُ النَّاسِ تَحمِلُهُ وليسَ كُلُّ ذواتِ المُخْلَبِ السَّبُعُ
His statement: 'And this is not a real definition' means by agreement, but it is a verbal definition opposed to the nominal, or of the type of nominal definition as previously mentioned. Then, the beginning of the expression of the commentator leans toward the statement of al-Sayyid, and its end toward the statement of the author. So some intended by the negated reality that it should provide conceptualization of what has not been obtained at all, either by its quiddity or by its distinction from all others, as indicated by his later statement: 'But the intention is only to specify what the word is assigned to... etc.' And whoever interprets it according to what al-Sayyid sees has erred, being heedless of what comes after. End. He took the apparent meaning like the one who also interpreted? Then, after that someone had quoted al-Jalal's statement on the ranks of conceptualization which we quoted, he transmitted al-Isam's objection to it and began refuting those objections, and all are errors upon errors. So take what we have transmitted to you, even if it leads to length, for I hope, God willing, that reliance will be upon it: 'And indeed, the weapon that all people carry is not every clawed animal is a lion...'
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage continues the super-commentary on the definition discussion. The author clarifies the meaning of the commentator's (al-Attar's) statement that 'this is not a real definition' (laysa hadha ta'rifan haqiqiyyan). The phrase 'real definition' is negated by agreement (ittifaqan) — meaning everyone agrees it is not a real definition. Instead, it is either a verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) as opposed to nominal definition, or a type of nominal definition (as previously discussed). The author then notes a tension: the beginning of the commentator's expression leans toward al-Sayyid's view, while the end leans toward the author's (al-Dasuqi's) view. Some interpreters took the negated 'reality' to mean that it should provide conceptualization of something not previously obtained at all — either by its quiddity (kunnihi) or by its distinction from all others — as indicated by the commentator's later phrase 'But the intention is only to specify what the word is assigned to...' The author criticizes these interpreters, saying that whoever interprets according to al-Sayyid's view is heedless of what comes after. Then the author reports that someone (presumably the same 'some') quoted al-Jalal al-Dawwani's statement on the ranks of conceptualization, then transmitted al-Isam's objection, and then began refuting those objections. The author dismisses all of these as errors upon errors. He urges the reader to take the transmitted material as it is, even if lengthy, as it is reliable. The passage ends with a poetic verse: 'The weapon that all people carry is not every clawed animal is a lion' — a metaphor for not every apparent definition is valid.

Key Terms
تعريف حقيقي
تعريف اسمي
التعريف اللفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what error did some interpreters commit regarding the commentator's statement?
A) They thought the definition was real
B) They ignored the end of the commentator's expression and interpreted only the beginning
C) They claimed the definition was nominal
D) They agreed with al-Sayyid but not with al-Dasuqi

Key Takeaway
When reading a scholarly commentary, do not take the first part as final; always read the whole expression and note any shifts in position.

The Weapon and the Lion: A Metaphor for Logical Caution
Author uses a poetic metaphor to caution against superficial judgments of definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the logical fallacy of assuming a definition is real based on superficial similarity, using the metaphor from the passage.

Core Idea
Not every clawed animal is a lion, and not every apparent definition is real.

The passage ends with a poetic line: 'And indeed, the weapon that all people carry is not every clawed animal is a lion.' This metaphor warns against assuming that any definition that looks like a real definition actually is one. Just as having claws does not make an animal a lion, having the form of a definition does not make it a real definition. In this lesson, we unpack this metaphorical caution and its logical application.

Guided Path
1
Understand the literal meaning of the verse
The verse says that while many people carry weapons, not every clawed animal is a lion. Claws are a characteristic of lions but not exclusive to them; other animals also have claws.
The metaphor contrasts a superficial feature (claws) with the true essence (being a lion).
2
Identify the parallel in definitions
Similarly, many statements have the outward form of a definition (e.g., 'X is Y') but not all are real definitions. A real definition must reveal the quiddity or full distinction; a mere description or verbal explanation shares the form but not the essence.
3
Recognize the fallacy
The fallacy is assuming that because something shares a feature with a real definition (e.g., it provides some information about the thing), it is therefore a real definition. This is a hasty generalization or a false analogy.
This is a common error in theological and legal reasoning.
4
Apply the caution
When you encounter a definition, ask: Does it reveal the essence of the thing? Does it distinguish it from all others? If not, it is not a real definition, even if it looks like one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ: وَلَيْسَ هَذَا تَعْرِيْفَاً حَقِيقِيًّا أي اتّفاقاً، بل هو تعريف لفظي مُقابل للاسميّ، أو مِنْ قَبيلِ الاسمي فيه ما تقدَّمَ ثمَّ إِنَّ صَدرَ عبارةِ الشَّارحِ؛ يميلُ لِكلامٍ السَّيِّدِ، وعجزُهَا لِكلام المصنفِ، فَقولُ البعض أرادَ بحقيقتِهِ المنفيَّةِ أن يفيد تصوَّر ما لم يحصل أصلاً بكنههِ أو بتمييزه عن جميع أغياره كما يرشدُ له قولُهُ بعدُ: (وإنَّما المرادُ تَعيينُ مَا وضعَ لَهُ اللَّفْظُ ...إلخ)، ومَنْ نزَّله على ما يراهُ السَّيِّدُ؛ فَقَدْ وهم غفلة عمَّا بعدَه .ا.هـ. أخذ بالظَّاهر كالمنزلِ أيضاً، ثمّ إنَّ ذلكَ البعض بعدَ أنْ نقل عبارةَ الجلالِ في مراتبِ التَّصورِ التي نقلناها; نقل اعتراض العصام عليها وأخذ في ردّ تلك الاعتراضات، والكُلَّ أوهام على أوهام، فَخُذْ مَا نقلناهُ لَّكَ وَإِنْ أَدَّى إلى تطويل; فإنّي أرجو إنْ شاءَ الله تعالى أنْ يكونَ عليهِ التَّعويلُ : ود إنَّ السّلاحَ جميعُ النَّاسِ تَحمِلُهُ وليسَ كُلُّ ذواتِ المُخْلَبِ السَّبُعُ

Commentary
This passage continues the super-commentary on the definition discussion. The author clarifies the meaning of the commentator's (al-Attar's) statement that 'this is not a real definition' (laysa hadha ta'rifan haqiqiyyan). The phrase 'real definition' is negated by agreement (ittifaqan) — meaning everyone agrees it is not a real definition. Instead, it is either a verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) as opposed to nominal definition, or a type of nominal definition (as previously discussed). Key Terms
تعريف حقيقي (ta'rif haqiqi): A real definition that reveals the quiddity (mahiyya) of a thing or distinguishes it from all others; negated here by agreement. [Note: Stable across the tradition; often contrasted with ta'rif lafzi or ta'rif ismi.]
تعريف اسمي (ta'rif ismi): A nominal definition that specifies the referent of a word without revealing the essence. [Note: Stable; sometimes synonymous with ta'rif lafzi in some texts, but here distinguished.]
التعريف اللفظي (al-ta'rif al-lafzi): Verbal definition; an explanation of the meaning of a word using other words, often relying on stored knowledge. [Note: Stable across the tradition.]

The metaphor warns us not to judge a definition by its outward form; a real definition must meet the criteria of revealing quiddity or full distinction, not just look like one.

Real vs. Verbal Definition in Islamic Logic
Author defines real and verbal definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) and a verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) using criteria from the Islamic logical tradition.

Core Idea
Not all definitions reveal essences; some only clarify words.

In this passage, the author explains that definitions can be either real—revealing the essence of a thing—or verbal—merely clarifying the linguistic reference. Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating definitions in Islamic sciences, where a misidentified type can lead to flawed reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Look at the definiendum in the Arabic passage. For example, the term 'وجود' (existence) is used to illustrate the definition process.
2
Check if the definition reveals quiddity
Determine whether the definition describes the essential nature (mahiyya) of the thing or merely explains the word's reference. The passage states that a real definition gives conceptualization of the essence.
3
Classify as real or verbal
Apply the author's criterion: if the definition primarily serves to bring to mind the meaning and affirm the word's reference, it is verbal; if it aims to conceptualize the essence, it is real.
The passage notes that in linguistic sciences the goal is assent (tasdiq), hence verbal definitions are common.
4
Test with an Islamic example
Consider the definition of 'khamr' (intoxicating drink). A real definition would state 'an intoxicating beverage derived from grapes or dates' (capturing essence), while a verbal definition would say 'the word khamr refers to intoxicating drinks'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ
فيُقالُ : مَا يكون فاعلاً أو مُنفعلاً ، فَمِنْ شَأنِهِ أَنَّهُ يحصلُ لهُ منه للسائل إحضار معنى الوجود، والالتفات إليه من بين الصُّورِ المخزونة، وأن يحصل لهُ التَّصديق بأنَّ لفظ الوجود موضوع لهذا المعنى، فإذا قيل : ذلك في العلوم اللغويَّة؛ فالمقصود منه التصديق، وإنْ كانَ التَّصوُّرُ حاصِلاً في ضمنِهِ؛ إذْ نَظَرُ أرباب تلك الصناعاتِ مقصور على الألفاظ، وإذا قيلَ ذلكَ في العلوم العقليَّةِ؛ فالمقصود منه على ما هو وظيفةُ هذه العلومِ النَّصور، وإنْ كانَ التَّصديق حاصلاً في ضمنه ا.هـ. وَلِلفاضل المرعشي كلامٌ في هذا المقام ذَكَرَهُ في تقرير القوانين، فإِنْ ضممتَهُ إلى ما هنا ؛ وقعت على حقيقة الحال وسبقت غيرَكَ في هذا المجال.
(قَوْلُهُ: وَلَيْسَ هَذَا تَعْرِيْفَاً حَقِيقِيًّا أي اتّفاقاً، بل هو تعريف لفظي مُقابل للاسميّ، أو مِنْ قَبيلِ الاسمي فيه ما تقدَّمَ ثمَّ إِنَّ صَدرَ عبارةِ الشَّارحِ ؛ يميلُ لِكلامٍ السَّيِّدِ، وعجزُهَا لِكلام المصنفِ ، فَقولُ البعض أرادَ بحقيقتِهِ المنفيَّةِ أن يفيد تصوَّر ما لم يحصل أصلاً بكنههِ أو بتمييزه عن جميع أغياره كما يرشدُ له قولُهُ بعدُ: (وإنَّما المرادُ تَعيينُ مَا وضعَ لَهُ اللَّفْظُ ...إلخ)، ومَنْ نزَّله على ما يراهُ السَّيِّدُ؛ فَقَدْ وهم غفلة عمَّا بعدَه .ا.هـ. أخذ بالظَّاهر كالمنزلِ أيضاً، ثمّ إنَّ ذلكَ البعض بعدَ أنْ نقل عبارةَ الجلالِ في مراتبِ التَّصورِ التي نقلناها ؛ نقل اعتراض العصام عليها وأخذ في ردّ تلك الاعتراضات، والكُلَّ أوهام على أوهام ، فَخُذْ مَا نقلناهُ لَّكَ وَإِنْ أَدَّى إلى تطويل ؛ فإنّي أرجو إنْ شاءَ الله تعالى أنْ يكونَ عليهِ التَّعويلُ :
ود
إنَّ السّلاحَ جميعُ النَّاسِ تَحمِلُهُ وليسَ كُلُّ ذواتِ المُخْلَبِ السَّبُعُ
وإلى هنا انتهى بنا الكلام عن قسم التَّصورات
Chapter: On Definition and its Divisions. It is said: that which is an agent or patient, its condition is that from it the questioner obtains a bringing to mind of the meaning of existence, and turning attention to it from among stored forms, and that he obtains assent that the word 'existence' is assigned to this meaning. So when this is said in the linguistic sciences, the intent is assent, even if conceptualization is included within it; for the consideration of those craftspeople is confined to words. And when this is said in the rational sciences, the intent, according to the function of these sciences, is conceptualization, even if assent is included within it. End. And al-Fadil al-Mar'ashi has words on this subject mentioned in his 'Taqrir al-Qawanin'; if you add it to what is here, you will reach the true state and surpass others in this field. (His saying: 'And this is not a real definition' i.e., by consensus, rather it is a verbal definition corresponding to the nominal, or of the nominal type as previously mentioned. Then the beginning of the commentator's statement leans toward al-Sayyid's words, while its end leans toward the author's words. So some said: By 'its negated reality' he intended that it gives a conceptualization of what was not obtained at all by its essence or by distinguishing it from all its others, as is indicated by his subsequent saying: 'Rather the intent is to specify what the word was placed for... etc.' And whoever interprets it according to al-Sayyid's view has erred, heedless of what follows it. End. He also took the apparent like the one who interprets. Then that some person, after quoting the words of al-Jalal on the ranks of conceptualization which we have quoted, he quoted the objection of al-Isam against it and began to refute those objections, and all are errors upon errors. So take what we have quoted to you, even if it leads to length; for I hope, God willing, that it will be relied upon. And the poem: 'People all carry weapons, but not every clawed beast is a lion.' And up to here ends our discussion on the section of conceptualizations.
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on definition and its divisions. It begins by distinguishing between real definition (تعريف حقيقي) that reveals the essence and verbal definition (تعريف لفظي) that merely clarifies the linguistic reference. The author discusses the roles of tasawwur (concept formation) and tasdiq (assent) in definitions. In linguistic sciences, the goal is assent (tasdiq) that a word corresponds to its meaning, even if conceptualization is implied. In rational sciences, the goal is conceptualization (tasawwur), even if assent is implied. The passage then cites al-Mulla 'Ali al-Qari and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani on the nature of real definition. Some scholars argued that a real definition must provide a conceptualization of the essence or distinguish it from all others. The author criticizes those who misinterpret this, calling their views 'errors upon errors.' He then concludes with a line of poetry. An example from fiqh: The definition of 'khamr' as an intoxicating drink is a real definition if it captures the essence, but a verbal definition merely clarifies that the word 'khamr' refers to intoxicating drinks.

تعريف حقيقي
تعريف لفظي
تصور
تصديق

Tasawwur and Tasdiq in Definitions
Author discusses roles of tasawwur and tasdiq in definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a definition aims primarily for conceptualization (tasawwur) or assent (tasdiq) based on the science in which it is used.

Core Idea
In linguistic sciences, definitions aim for assent; in rational sciences, they aim for conceptualization.

The author distinguishes between two cognitive goals of definitions: tasawwur (conceptualization) and tasdiq (assent). In the linguistic sciences—like lexicography—the primary aim is to affirm that a word corresponds to a meaning (tasdiq). In the rational sciences—like logic or kalam—the aim is to form a mental concept of the thing’s essence (tasawwur). Understanding this helps you evaluate definitions in their proper context.

Guided Path
1
Note the science in which the definition appears
Read the passage and identify whether the definition is presented in a linguistic context or a rational context. For example, if a definition is from a dictionary, it is linguistic; if from a theology book, it is rational.
2
Determine if the focus is on word or meaning
In linguistic sciences, the definition concentrates on the word's usage; in rational sciences, it concentrates on the thing's essence. The passage says: 'نظر أرباب تلك الصناعات مقصور على الألفاظ' (the consideration of those craftspeople is confined to words).
3
Identify whether tasawwur or tasdiq is primary
If the definition aims to affirm that the word signifies a meaning, the primary result is tasdiq (even if tasawwur is implied). If it aims to form a concept of the essence, the primary result is tasawwur (even if tasdiq is implied).
The author explicitly says: 'في العلوم اللغوية... فالمقصود منه التصديق' and 'في العلوم العقلية... فالمقصود منه على ما هو وظيفة هذه العلوم التصور'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ
فيُقالُ : مَا يكون فاعلاً أو مُنفعلاً ، فَمِنْ شَأنِهِ أَنَّهُ يحصلُ لهُ منه للسائل إحضار معنى الوجود، والالتفات إليه من بين الصُّورِ المخزونة، وأن يحصل لهُ التَّصديق بأنَّ لفظ الوجود موضوع لهذا المعنى، فإذا قيل : ذلك في العلوم اللغويَّة؛ فالمقصود منه التصديق، وإنْ كانَ التَّصوُّرُ حاصِلاً في ضمنِهِ؛ إذْ نَظَرُ أرباب تلك الصناعاتِ مقصور على الألفاظ، وإذا قيلَ ذلكَ في العلوم العقليَّةِ؛ فالمقصود منه على ما هو وظيفةُ هذه العلومِ النَّصور، وإنْ كانَ التَّصديق حاصلاً في ضمنه ا.هـ. وَلِلفاضل المرعشي كلامٌ في هذا المقام ذَكَرَهُ في تقرير القوانين، فإِنْ ضممتَهُ إلى ما هنا ؛ وقعت على حقيقة الحال وسبقت غيرَكَ في هذا المجال.
(قَوْلُهُ: وَلَيْسَ هَذَا تَعْرِيْفَاً حَقِيقِيًّا أي اتّفاقاً، بل هو تعريف لفظي مُقابل للاسميّ، أو مِنْ قَبيلِ الاسمي فيه ما تقدَّمَ ثمَّ إِنَّ صَدرَ عبارةِ الشَّارحِ ؛ يميلُ لِكلامٍ السَّيِّدِ، وعجزُهَا لِكلام المصنفِ ، فَقولُ البعض أرادَ بحقيقتِهِ المنفيَّةِ أن يفيد تصوَّر ما لم يحصل أصلاً بكنههِ أو بتمييزه عن جميع أغياره كما يرشدُ له قولُهُ بعدُ: (وإنَّما المرادُ تَعيينُ مَا وضعَ لَهُ اللَّفْظُ ...إلخ)، ومَنْ نزَّله على ما يراهُ السَّيِّدُ؛ فَقَدْ وهم غفلة عمَّا بعدَه .ا.هـ. أخذ بالظَّاهر كالمنزلِ أيضاً، ثمّ إنَّ ذلكَ البعض بعدَ أنْ نقل عبارةَ الجلالِ في مراتبِ التَّصورِ التي نقلناها ؛ نقل اعتراض العصام عليها وأخذ في ردّ تلك الاعتراضات، والكُلَّ أوهام على أوهام ، فَخُذْ مَا نقلناهُ لَّكَ وَإِنْ أَدَّى إلى تطويل ؛ فإنّي أرجو إنْ شاءَ الله تعالى أنْ يكونَ عليهِ التَّعويلُ :
ود
إنَّ السّلاحَ جميعُ النَّاسِ تَحمِلُهُ وليسَ كُلُّ ذواتِ المُخْلَبِ السَّبُعُ
وإلى هنا انتهى بنا الكلام عن قسم التَّصورات
Chapter: On Definition and its Divisions. It is said: that which is an agent or patient, its condition is that from it the questioner obtains a bringing to mind of the meaning of existence, and turning attention to it from among stored forms, and that he obtains assent that the word 'existence' is assigned to this meaning. So when this is said in the linguistic sciences, the intent is assent, even if conceptualization is included within it; for the consideration of those craftspeople is confined to words. And when this is said in the rational sciences, the intent, according to the function of these sciences, is conceptualization, even if assent is included within it. End. And al-Fadil al-Mar'ashi has words on this subject mentioned in his 'Taqrir al-Qawanin'; if you add it to what is here, you will reach the true state and surpass others in this field. (His saying: 'And this is not a real definition' i.e., by consensus, rather it is a verbal definition corresponding to the nominal, or of the nominal type as previously mentioned. Then the beginning of the commentator's statement leans toward al-Sayyid's words, while its end leans toward the author's words. So some said: By 'its negated reality' he intended that it gives a conceptualization of what was not obtained at all by its essence or by distinguishing it from all its others, as is indicated by his subsequent saying: 'Rather the intent is to specify what the word was placed for... etc.' And whoever interprets it according to al-Sayyid's view has erred, heedless of what follows it. End. He also took the apparent like the one who interprets. Then that some person, after quoting the words of al-Jalal on the ranks of conceptualization which we have quoted, he quoted the objection of al-Isam against it and began to refute those objections, and all are errors upon errors. So take what we have quoted to you, even if it leads to length; for I hope, God willing, that it will be relied upon. And the poem: 'People all carry weapons, but not every clawed beast is a lion.' And up to here ends our discussion on the section of conceptualizations.
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on definition and its divisions. It begins by distinguishing between real definition (تعريف حقيقي) that reveals the essence and verbal definition (تعريف لفظي) that merely clarifies the linguistic reference. The author discusses the roles of tasawwur (concept formation) and tasdiq (assent) in definitions. In linguistic sciences, the goal is assent (tasdiq) that a word corresponds to its meaning, even if conceptualization is implied. In rational sciences, the goal is conceptualization (tasawwur), even if assent is implied. The passage then cites al-Mulla 'Ali al-Qari and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani on the nature of real definition. Some scholars argued that a real definition must provide a conceptualization of the essence or distinguish it from all others. The author criticizes those who misinterpret this, calling their views 'errors upon errors.' He then concludes with a line of poetry. An example from fiqh: The definition of 'khamr' as an intoxicating drink is a real definition if it captures the essence, but a verbal definition merely clarifies that the word 'khamr' refers to intoxicating drinks.

Key Terms
تصور
تصديق
تعريف حقيقي
تعريف لفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of science does the author say the primary aim of definition is assent (tasdiq)?
A) Rational sciences like logic
B) Linguistic sciences like lexicography
C) Natural sciences like physics
D) All sciences equally

Key Takeaway
The primary goal of a definition—conceptualization or assent—depends on the science in which it is used.

The Debate on Real Definition: Al-Qari vs. Al-Jurjani
Author critiques scholars on real definition criteria

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the debate between al-Mulla 'Ali al-Qari and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani regarding the criteria for a real definition.

Core Idea
Scholars disagreed whether a real definition must reveal the essence or just distinguish the thing from others.

In this passage, the commentator engages with two prominent scholars: al-Mulla 'Ali al-Qari and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani. The key dispute is whether a real definition must provide conceptualization of the thing's essence (كنه) or whether it suffices to distinguish it from all others (تمييز عن جميع أغياره). The author of the commentary sides with al-Jurjani, critiquing those who misinterpret the definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani holds that real definition must give a conceptualization of the essence or at least distinguish it from all others. Al-Mulla 'Ali al-Qari is criticized for interpreting the definition too narrowly.
2
Find the author's critique
The author explicitly says that those who follow al-Qari's view have erred, heedless of what follows. He calls their objections 'errors upon errors.'
3
Determine the correct criterion
The author implies that a real definition should either reveal the essence (كنه) or provide a distinguishing mark (تمييز) that separates the thing from all others. A verbal definition only clarifies the word's reference.

The Aspects of Predication and the Distinction Between Hikaya and Mahki
Author explains hathiyyat in different proposition types and defines hikaya and mahki anhu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the aspect of predication (hathiyya) for categorical, negative, relational, and conditional propositions, and distinguish between hikaya and mahki anhu.

Core Idea
The hikaya is the mental story; the mahki is the external reality; the nisba lives only in the story.

In Islamic logic, every proposition has an internal structure that includes a mental representation (hikaya) and an external referent (mahki anhu). The aspect (hathiyya) under which the predicate relates to the subject varies depending on the type of proposition. This lesson explores these distinctions as laid out by the author and clarified by Mir Zahid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposition types discussed
The author discusses categorical propositions ('حمليات'), negative attributes ('عدمية'), relational attributes ('إضافية'), and conditional propositions ('شرطية'). List each type and note the key phrases in the Arabic that indicate them.
2
Extract the hathiyya for each type
For categorical: the relation of the predicate to the subject. For negative: the relation of the absence of accompaniment. For relational: the relation of a distinct matter. For conditionals: either the validity of affirming one on condition of the other (conjunctive) or the validity of disjunction (disjunctive). Write down the Arabic terms for each aspect.
3
Understand the hikaya-mahki distinction
Mir Zahid states: hikaya is the very concept (mafhum) of the proposition, mahki is its referent (musdaq). The relation (nisba) is only in the hikaya, not in the mahki. They differ in essence (dhat), not in consideration (i'tibar). Reflect on a concrete example like 'The world is created.'
4
Apply the distinction to a new proposition
Choose a simple categorical proposition from a theological text, such as 'Knowledge is eternal.' Identify what the hikaya is (the concept of knowledge being eternal) and what the mahki anhu is (the actual attribute of knowledge in extra-mental reality).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المحمول بالموضوع، وفي حمل العدميَّاتِ : حيثيَّةُ نسبة عدمِ مُصاحبتِهِ لأمرٍ آخر، وفي حمل الإضافيات : حيثيَّةُ نسبة أمرٍ مُباين، وأما في الشرطيَّاتِ ; فهو كون المعنيين في نفسَيْهِمَا ; بحيثُ يصحُ الحُكم بثبوتِ أحدهما على تقدير ثبوتِ الآخر، أو كونهما في نفسهما بحيثُ يصح الحكم بالانفصال بينَهُما ، وهاتان الحيثيتان أيضاً يختلفان باختلافِ الاتصال والانفصال، قال مير زاهد : وبالجملة; الحكاية هي نفس مفهوم القضيَّة، والمحكي عنه هو مصداقها، والنّسبةُ إنَّما هي في الحكاية دون المحكي، والتَّغايرُ بينَهُما تغايرُ بالذَّاتِ لا بالاعتبار ا.هـ.
The predicate in relation to the subject, and in the predication of negative attributes: the aspect is the relation of the absence of its accompanying another thing, and in the predication of relational attributes: the aspect is the relation of a distinct matter. As for conditional propositions, it is that the two meanings are in themselves such that it is valid to judge the affirmation of one upon the condition of the affirmation of the other, or that they are in themselves such that it is valid to judge disjunction between them. These two aspects also differ according to conjunction and disjunction. Mir Zahid said: In summary, the story (hikaya) is the very concept of the proposition, and the thing told about (mahki anhu) is its referent (musdaq). The relation (nisba) is only in the story, not in the thing told about. The difference between them is a difference in essence, not in consideration. End.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage discusses the different 'aspects' (hathiyyat) involved in predication across various types of propositions. The author begins with categorical propositions, where the aspect is the relation of the predicate to the subject. For negative attributes ('adamiyyat), the aspect is the relation of non-existence (absence) of the predicate's accompaniment with something else. For relational attributes (idafiyyat), the aspect is the relation of a distinct matter (i.e., the relatum). In conditional propositions (shartiyyat), the aspect is that the two meanings (the antecedent and consequent) are such that it is valid to judge one upon the condition of the other (in conjunctive conditionals) or to judge separation between them (in disjunctive conditionals). These two types differ according to conjunctive or disjunctive form. The passage then quotes Mir Zahid, who gives a general definition: the story (hikaya) is the very concept of the proposition (mafhum al-qadiyya), and the thing told about (mahki anhu) is the external reality or referent (musdaq) of that proposition. The relation (nisba) inheres in the story, not in the external reality. The difference between the story and the thing told about is a difference in essence (dhat), not merely in consideration (i'tibar). This clarifies that the mental representation (hikaya) is distinct from the extra-mental reality (mahki). In Islamic logic, understanding this distinction is crucial for analyzing propositions about existence, attributes, and conditional judgments. For example, in the proposition 'The world is created,' the hikaya is the mental relation between 'world' and 'created,' while the mahki is the actual world itself.

Key Terms
حيثية
حكاية
محكي عنه
نسبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the proposition 'The world is created,' the hikaya is:
A) The actual world
B) The concept of the world being created
C) The predicate 'created'
D) The external relation between world and creator

Key Takeaway
The hikaya is the mental concept of the proposition, while the mahki anhu is its extra-mental referent; the relation (nisba) resides only in the hikaya.

1. For the proposition 'All humans are mortal,' write down what you think the hikaya is and what the mahki anhu is, based on Mir Zahid's definitions.
?
2. Choose one type of conditional proposition (conjunctive) and state the hathiyya as described in the passage.

Qawl in Logic: Compound Expression Only
Author defines qawl as compound expression, including verbal and mental, and distinguishes logicians' vs. grammarians' usage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the logicians' definition of qawl from the grammarians' broader usage and identify examples of compound expressions in logic.

Core Idea
In logic, qawl is always compound — a single word is not a qawl.

This lesson examines the technical definition of qawl according to the logicians. The passage from al-Dasuqi's commentary clarifies that qawl can be either a verbal utterance or a mental concept, but in both cases it must be compound — composed of at least two terms that convey a complete meaning. This differs from the grammarians' usage, where even a single word like 'Zayd' is considered qawl. Understanding this distinction is essential for moving forward in logic, because only compound expressions can be true or false, which is the basis of propositions (qadiyya).

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the definiendum in the Arabic. Here it is 'al-qawl'. What exactly is being defined?
The passage starts with 'فالقول' indicating the term under definition.
2
Extract the genus
The definition states that qawl is a compound utterance or a compound mental concept. The genus is 'compound expression' (either verbal or mental).
Both verbal (lafz murakkab) and mental (mafhum 'aqli murakkab) are included.
3
Distinguish logicians vs. grammarians
According to logicians, qawl is only compound (لا يكون إلا مركباً). Grammarians, however, include both simple and compound (المفرد والمركب).
This disciplinary difference is crucial.
4
Test examples
Apply the definition: Is 'Zayd' a qawl in logic? No, because it is simple. Is 'Zayd is standing' a qawl? Yes, because it is compound.
Also consider mental examples: thinking 'Zayd is standing' without speaking counts as a mental compound qawl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ
فالقول ـ وهو اللَّفْظُ المركَّبُ أو المفهوم العقلي المركَّبُ - جنس يشمل القضيَّةً وغيرها من المركبات
الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ: أَوْ الْمَفْهُوْمُ الْعَقْلِيُّ) وهو القضيَّةُ العقليَّةُ التي أجريتها على قلبك من غير تلفظ بها، كما إذا أجريت على قلبكَ : زيدٌ قائم، فيُقالُ لذلك : قضيَّة، كما يُقالُ على اللفظ ، قيل : على سبيل الحقيقةِ فيهما، وقيل: في أحدهما حقيقة، وفي الآخَر مَجاز، وقولُهُ: وَهُوَ اللُّفظُ المركَّبُ؛ هذا تفسير للقول عند المناطقة، وهو عندَهُم لا يكونُ إِلَّا مُركَّباً، وأما عندَ النُّحاة؛ فهو شامل للمفرد والمركب.
Chapter: On Definition and Its Divisions. Al-qawl — it is the compound utterance or the compound mental concept — a genus that includes the proposition and other compounds. Al-Dasuqi (his saying: 'or the mental concept') — it is the mental proposition that you run in your heart without uttering it, as when you run in your heart: Zayd is standing, so that is called a proposition, just as it is called for the utterance. It is said: on the basis of being literal in both, and it is said: in one of them literal, and in the other metaphorical. And his saying: 'and it is the compound utterance' — this is an interpretation of al-qawl according to the logicians, and according to them it is only compound, but according to the grammarians it includes both the simple and the compound.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage presents a formal definition (hadd) of qawl (statement/speech) in the context of logic. It begins with a chapter heading on definition and its divisions. The definition states that qawl is either a compound utterance (lafz murakkab) or a compound mental concept (mafhum 'aqli murakkab). This serves as a genus that includes the proposition (qadiyya) and other compound expressions. The commentary by al-Dasuqi clarifies that the 'mental concept' refers to a mental proposition that one entertains in the heart without uttering, such as the mental judgment 'Zayd is standing.' Such a mental entity is also called a proposition, just as the verbal utterance is. There is a debate: some say 'qawl' is literal in both verbal and mental senses, others say it is literal in one and metaphorical in the other. The passage then explains that the phrase 'compound utterance' is how logicians define qawl: for them, qawl is necessarily compound (i.e., composed of at least two words). In contrast, grammarians use 'qawl' to include both simple (single words) and compound expressions. This distinction is crucial: in logic, only compound expressions (like propositions) are considered qawl because they convey a complete meaning that can be true or false. For example, in fiqh, a simple command like 'Pray!' is considered qawl by grammarians but not by logicians, who require a subject-predicate structure. Thus, the passage defines the technical scope of qawl in logic and contrasts it with broader linguistic usage.

Key Terms
القول
اللفظ المركب
المفهوم العقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the logicians, what is the defining characteristic of al-qawl?
A) It must be a verbal utterance.
B) It must be compound (murakkab), not simple.
C) It must be a mental concept only.
D) It includes both simple and compound expressions.

Key Takeaway
In logic, qawl is defined as a compound expression (either verbal or mental), excluding simple terms; this scope distinguishes logical analysis from grammar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
From the Quranic ayah, identify which are qawl according to logicians: 'And when it is said to them, 'Do not cause corruption on the earth,' they say, 'We are but reformers.'' (select the compound qawl).
?
Give an example of a mental compound qawl (a proposition you think without speaking) from a theological debate, e.g., 'The world is created.'
